The previous single line (`let _ = self.lower_type_ref(s.ty)`) silently dropped the property — that's why `Identity::create` produced no goto-def hit. The LSP path needed no change: `goto_definition_handler` already consults `foreign_member_lookup` after the `ProjectDecl` branch (P11.5) and uses `cross_module_member_location` to compute the foreign attr/method name range. New test in `lsp_capabilities.rs::cross_module_static_call_binds_foreign_method` mirrors the `.`-shape test from P11.5 for the `::` shape.

- [x] **15.7 Static-expr / static-call type inference** (S) — new pass 3.5 in `ProjectAnalysis::rebuild` (between cross-module member resolution and the qualified-refs pass) infers types for four previously-`any` shapes:
  - `var x = Identity::create("root", "root");` → `x: Identity` (call's return type translated from the foreign method's `return_type` into the local arena).
  - `var y = Identity::create;` → `y: function` (method reference; `function` is a `native type` in `lib/std/core.gcl`).
  - `var z = Identity::id;` → `z: field` (attr reference; `field` is also a `native type` in core.gcl).
  - `var w = runtime::Identity;` → `w: type` (module-prefixed type ref; `type` is a `native type` too).
    Two-phase: phase 1 walks every module's HIR read-only and snapshots the foreign return type into an arena-free `TypeShape` enum; phase 2 mints those shapes into each affected module's `TypeArena` and updates `expr_types[call_id]` and (for `var x = ...` initializers without a declared type) re-links `def_types[name]` so inlay hints / hover / downstream inference see the right type. The fourth shape (`module::Decl`) leans on a new `ProjectIndex.module_names: HashMap<String, Uri>` map (populated by `ingest` from the URI's filename stem); the resolver also consults `has_module(name)` so leftmost segments of `module::X::Y` chains aren't flagged as unresolved. Generic substitution across modules (e.g. `Array<T>::create()` returning `Array<T>` where `T` is bound at the call site) keeps the generic head as-is without binding `T` — follow-up. 4 new tests in `lsp_capabilities.rs` cover the four shapes.

- [x] **15.8 FQN `module::Type::member` lowering + inference** (M) — chained `static_expr` (`runtime::Identity::create`, `runtime::Identity::id`, etc.) used to lower to `Expr::Unsupported` because HIR's `StaticExpr` had `ty: Idx<TypeRef>` and the grammar's chained head is itself a `static_expr` rather than a `type_ident`. Two pieces:
  - **New HIR variant `Expr::QualifiedStatic { chain: Vec<Idx<Ident>>, byte_range }`.** The lowering's `static_expr` arm detects chained heads and walks the chain into a flat `Vec<Idx<Ident>>`. Simple `Type::name` shapes still use the existing `Expr::Static`. New helper `collect_static_chain_idents` in `lower.rs`.
  - **Pass 3.5 extension.** New `resolve_qualified_static_shape` / `resolve_qualified_static_call_shape` / `resolve_qualified_chain` helpers in `project.rs` follow `chain[0]` → `ProjectIndex::module_uri` → foreign module → `chain[1]` (TypeDecl) → foreign type → `chain[2]` (Attr / Method). Method-ref → `function`, attr-ref → `field`, call-of-method → method's foreign return type translated via `read_type_shape` + `mint_type_shape`. The `def_types[name]` re-link from P15.7 picks up `var x = <chain>` shapes automatically.
  - **Acceptance:** `var x = runtime::Identity::create("a", "b");` infers `x: Identity` (matching the unprefixed form's behavior from P15.7). `var y = runtime::Identity::create;` infers `y: function`. New analyzer / resolver / capability arms cover `QualifiedStatic` (analyzer returns `any` from the per-module pass and pass 3.5 overrides; resolver records the leftmost segment via `record_use`; `Expr::Unsupported` regression audit stays empty). 2 new tests in `lsp_capabilities.rs` cover the chained call + chained method ref.

  **Chain-segment hover/goto follow-up landed.** New `AnalysisResult.foreign_decl_uses: HashMap<Idx<Ident>, ForeignDecl>` map binds chain[1] (the type segment) to its foreign top-level decl. Pass 3.5 populates both `foreign_decl_uses` (chain[1]) and `foreign_member_uses` (chain[2]) when resolving every `Expr::QualifiedStatic`. `ident_hover_markdown` now also consults `foreign_member_lookup` (closes a P15.6 gap where cross-module `Type::method` hover fell through to "expression: function") and `foreign_decl_lookup`. `goto_definition_handler` consults `foreign_decl_lookup` between the `ProjectDecl` branch and the `foreign_member_lookup` branch. 3 new tests cover hover on the static-method case, the chain-type segment, and the chain-member segment.

- [x] **15.10 Call-site argument-type validation** (S) — new pass 3.6 in `ProjectAnalysis::rebuild` (after pass 3.5 settles static-expr return types) walks every module's `Expr::Call`, resolves the callee's declaring `Decl::Fn` via a new `resolve_call_target` helper (covers `Expr::Ident → Decl/ProjectDecl`, `Expr::Static → member_uses/foreign_member_uses`, and `Expr::QualifiedStatic → resolve_qualified_chain`), and emits `value of type X is not assignable to parameter Y: T` for each mismatched arg. Foreign param types are translated into the caller's arena via `read_type_shape` + a clone of the caller's `TypeArena` (the arena gained a `Clone` derive — cheap because both fields are `Vec<Type>` / `HashMap`). Pass 3.5 also gained a 1a-tris sub-step that turns bare ident references into the right runtime type (`Identity` used as a value → `type`, `someFn` used as a value → `function`), and pass 3.6's diagnostic byte-range special-cases `Expr::Ident` (whose own `byte_range()` returns `0..0`) to use the ident's arena entry. **Acceptance:** the user's baseline (project.gcl) produces exactly the four expected `value of type 'int' is not assignable to parameter '_: <type>'` diagnostics, no more no less. 2 new tests cover the mismatch case + the bare-type-ident-as-value case.

  Generic callees still validate exclusively through `try_generic_call_inference` (P12.1) — pass 3.6 skips them so generic-param mismatch errors don't double up.

- [x] **15.9 Goto-def on module-prefix idents** (S) — new `capabilities::goto_module_segment` is consulted from `goto_definition_handler` _before_ the regular HIR-based goto path. When the cursor sits on an `ident` whose parent is a `type_ident` whose grand-parent is a `static_expr` (the leftmost segment of any `module::X` / `module::X::Y` chain), and the cursor's text matches a known module's `Document::name()`, the handler returns a `Location` pointing at line 0 of that module's URI. Pure CST walk — independent of how the chain ultimately lowers in HIR (P15.8 is still pending), so it works today on the user's `runtime::Identity::create` baseline. New unit test in `lsp_capabilities.rs`.

**M15: hover restores doc / signature / provenance; cross-module `Type::method` resolves and infers correctly (`Identity::create`, `runtime::Identity::create`, method-references, attr-references all infer the right type, not `any`); basic completion lights up in the LSP and the WASM/Monaco playground (sharing the same algorithm via a `RegistryFetcher` trait — native HTTP for the LSP, JS-callback fetch for WASM); `@library` version completion hits `get.greycat.io` in both targets and matches TS-reference behavior; `@include` directory completion is wired where the project root is known; `@include` / `@library` typos and duplicates are surfaced as diagnostics in both `cli lint` and the LSP.**

---

### Phase 16 — Member-flow inference & node-deref (~2-3 weeks)

**Goal:** chained member expressions (`x.s.size()`), method calls on primitive / cross-module receivers, and node-deref completion all behave the way the user expects. Closes the three bugs surfaced against the canonical [project.gcl](../project.gcl):

1. `var s = x.s.size();` infers `s: int`, not `s: any` — the `Expr::Member` arm's `self.any()` short-circuit hides the attr's declared type, and `Expr::Call` short-circuits the same way.
2. Completion on `x.s.|` (where `x.s: String`) lists `String`'s methods (`size`, `to_lower`, etc.) — `resolve_member` doesn't know how to find members on a `Primitive` receiver.
3. Completion on `x: node<Foo>` `.|` surfaces both node's own methods _and_ `Foo`'s attrs/methods with a `.` → `->` rewrite — the TS reference does this via `derefType.suggest()` + `additionalTextEdits`.

**Chunks:**

- [x] **16.1 Member-expr typing (intra-module)** (S) — `Expr::Member` / `Expr::Arrow` arm in `analyzer.rs` now consults `member_uses[property]` after `resolve_member`. `MemberDef::Attr(id)` returns the attr's `lower_type_ref(ty)`; `MemberDef::Method(_)` returns `Named("function")`. Cross-module bindings (in `foreign_member_uses`) still type as `any` here — pass 3.7 (P16.3) writes those back. 2 new tests: `member_attr_typing_matches_attr_decl_type`, `member_method_ref_types_as_function`. Closes the user's `project.gcl` baseline bug 1 for the intra-module shape.

- [x] **16.2 Primitive receiver member resolution** (S) — `resolve_member` now extracts a type name from `TypeKind::Primitive` (e.g. `Primitive::String → "String"`, `Primitive::Int → "int"`) and falls through to the existing `type_decls` / `decl_locations` lookup path. Lets `"hello".size()`, `1.to_string()`, etc. bind to the foreign primitive type's methods. (Effective once 16.3 / 16.4 light up cross-module typing — primitives' methods live in stdlib.)

- [x] **16.3 Member-expr typing (cross-module)** (M) — new `ProjectAnalysis::infer_cross_module_member_types` pass (pass 3.4, between cross-module member resolution and call return-type inference) walks each module's `Expr::Member` / `Expr::Arrow` whose property has a `foreign_member_uses` binding, translates the foreign attr's declared type via `read_type_shape` + `mint_type_shape`, and writes it back to `expr_types[expr_id]`. `MemberDef::Method` returns `Named("function")` (matches P16.1's intra-module shape). The same pass re-links `def_types` for `var x = recv.attr` shapes when there's no declared type. Validated against the parity oracle on `project.gcl`.

- [x] **16.4 Call-on-member return-type inference** (M) — extended `ProjectAnalysis::infer_cross_module_call_types`'s callee-shape match to recognize `Expr::Member` / `Expr::Arrow` callees. New helper `resolve_member_call_return_shape` looks up the property's binding (intra-module via `member_uses`, cross-module via `foreign_member_uses`), pulls the method's `return_type`, and produces a `TypeShape` the existing phase 2 mints into the caller's arena. `x.s.size()` now types as `core::int` end-to-end against the TS reference (the parity-types oracle's last-mile signal — see ROADMAP §18).

- [x] **16.5 node-tag / `@deref` auto-deref (analyzer + completion)** (M) — coupled fix so navigation and completion arrive together:
  - **Analyzer side** (`Expr::Arrow` arm in `analyzer.rs`): new `arrow_deref_receiver` returns the inner type for single-arg node-tag receivers (`node<T>`, `nodeTime<T>`, `nodeList<T>`, `nodeGeo<T>`); `nodeIndex<K, V>` and other multi-arg shapes don't match. The arm calls `resolve_member` with the inner type (when the helper returns `Some`), so `n->field` records `member_uses[field] = MemberDef::Attr(Foo's name attr)` — lighting up 16.1's typing, hover, and goto-def for `n->field` shapes. `Expr::Member` keeps the receiver as-is (no silent auto-deref on `.`); the rewrite advice in completion is how users discover the right shape.
  - **Completion side** (`member_completion` in `capabilities.rs`): the same `is_node_tag(name) && args.len() == 1` criterion drives a two-branch dispatch:
    - `n.|` — list the receiver type's own members (`node`'s `resolve()`, `set_value()`, …) AND the inner type's members each carrying `additional_text_edits: [TextEdit { range: <`.`-byte>, new_text: "->" }]` so accepting one rewrites `.` → `->` in source.
    - `n->|` — list only the inner type's members (the tag's own are reachable via `.` and shouldn't surface here).
  - **Pure-`@deref` user types deferred** — resolving `@deref("get")` on a non-native user type requires looking up the deref method in the (possibly foreign) type decl and instantiating its return type. The analyzer's per-module pass doesn't yet have that cross-module reach for arbitrary types. Node-tags carry their inner via the generic args, which is why this chunk lights them up cleanly while leaving the user-type case for follow-up.
  - 3 new tests in `lsp_capabilities.rs`: `n.|` lists `node`'s own + `Foo`'s with `.→->` rewrite; `n->|` lists only `Foo`'s with no rewrite; hover on `n->name` resolves through the deref to `Foo.name`.

- [x] **16.6 `arrow on non-deref receiver` lint** (S) — new typed lint `arrow-on-non-deref` walks every `Expr::Arrow` and errors when the receiver's type is neither a node tag (`is_node_tag` from `greycat-analyzer-types`) nor declared with `@deref(...)` (`ProjectIndex::type_flags`). Severity `Error` so it surfaces in cli `lint` and the LSP red-squiggle layer. Mirrors the runtime's `arrow operator cannot be applied on T` rejection. Conservative on receivers without a head name (`any` / lambda / tuple / anonymous / union / enum / generic-param) — better to under-warn than to fire on shapes the lint hasn't been formally taught. Lives outside `run_lints` because it consumes the per-module `AnalysisResult::expr_types` plus the project-wide `ProjectIndex`; `ProjectAnalysis` runs it as `run_typed_lints` after the cross-module type fixups (3.4 / 3.5) and before `validate_type_relations`. Idempotent on `invalidate` — clears the rule's prior findings before re-emitting, matching the validation post-pass scope. 5 new tests in `lint::tests` cover the node-tag, primitive, plain-user-type, `@deref`-annotated, and `any`-receiver cases.

- [x] **16.7 Null-safe access notations + `??` parity** (M) — `MemberExpr` and `OffsetExpr` gained `pre_optional: bool, post_optional: bool` flags; lowering reads the `optional` named children that bracket the property / indexer in the grammar (`seq($._expr, optional($.optional), ".", field("property", $.ident), optional($.optional))` and friends). The analyzer arms thread them through:
  - **`a?.b`** / **`a?->b`** — pre-optional. When `a: T?`, the result lifts to `(typeof a.b)?`; when `a: T`, the marker is a no-op (still type-checks).
  - **`a.b?`** / **`a->b?`** — post-optional. Lifts to nullable unconditionally — explicit "treat as nullable" suffix, regardless of the declared field type. Mirrors the runtime's "I know better" semantics for nullable-fluent chaining.
  - **`a?[i]`** / **`a[i]?`** — same plumbing on `Expr::Offset`. Element-type inference is still `any` (out of scope), but the `?` markers fold in cleanly so the lifts continue to do the right thing once element typing lands.
  - **`a?.method()`** — null-safe call. The current per-module `Expr::Call` arm returns `any` (cross-module fixups handle real return types), and `any` is already nullable, so the lift is implicit until call-return inference matures. Explicit lift on the Call's resolved return type is a follow-up.
  - **`a ?? b`** — null-coalesce widened. Was `right with nullable = false` (dropping the left entirely); now `(typeof a stripped of null) | (typeof b stripped of null)` re-wrapped nullable when `b` itself is nullable. Same-shape collapse (`int? ?? int → int`) keeps the simple case clean for the assignability checker. Distinct shapes (`Foo? ?? Bar`) widen to a 2-alt union.
  - 7 new analyzer-side tests in `analyzer::tests`: `?.` lifts on nullable receiver, `?.` is no-op on non-nullable, `.b?` lifts unconditionally, `?->` through a node-tag receiver, `??` same-shape collapse, `??` widening to a union, `??` with nullable right operand stays nullable.

  Out of scope: chained generic inference (`Array<int>::iter().next()`). The runtime doesn't currently support chained generic instantiation either, so we'd be inventing semantics.

**M16:** `cargo run -- lint project.gcl` reports zero false `any` types in `var s = x.s.size()` (s infers `int`); LSP `textDocument/completion` on `x.|` where `x: node<Foo>` returns both node's own method list and `Foo`'s attrs with the `.→->` rewrite; cross-module `recv.attr.method()` chains type correctly through the cached `ProjectAnalysis`; `recv->prop` on a non-deref receiver fires an `arrow-on-non-deref` error; null-safe access notations (`a?.b`, `a?->b`, `a?[i]`, `a?.m()`) propagate nullability through the result and `a ?? b` lifts to the correct merged type.

---

### TS-side dump tooling (oracle for parity work)

The TS reference (`greycat-lang`) ships three subcommands as of 2026-05-08
that dump the typed-AST / typed-HIR for direct comparison against the
Rust port. These are the **source of truth** for inferred-type / binding
shapes — when in doubt, run the TS dump and match it.

| Subcommand                                             | Output                                                                                                                                                                      | Use case                               |
| ------------------------------------------------------ | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------- |
| `greycat-lang dump-types <path> [--filter R]`          | JSONL: one record per typed expression with `kind`, `range` (UTF-8 byte half-open), `line:col`, `type` (FQN form like `core::Array<core::int \| null>`), `nullable`, `text` | inferred-type parity oracle            |
| `greycat-lang dump-resolutions <path> [--filter R]`    | JSONL: one record per ident use with `refKind` / `declKind` / `name` / `decl: { fqn, file, range, line, col }`                                                              | resolver / cross-module binding oracle |
| `greycat-lang dump-hir <path> [--filter R] [--pretty]` | single JSON: `modules[]` with `types`/`enums`/`functions`/`vars`, each carrying signature, span, and a typed AST body where every node has `kind`/`span`/`type`/`nullable`  | full snapshot diffs                    |

**Stability hints honored:**

- Output sorted by `(file, line, col, byteStart, byteEnd)` for clean diffs.
- Single canonical type printer (TS `shared.ts:159`) emits FQN-or-builtin form; same string regardless of context.
- Half-open UTF-8 byte ranges (matches tree-sitter conventions).
- `--filter B` / `B-B` / `L:C` / `L:C-L:C` for narrowing.
- Single-file mode walks up to find `project.gcl`, analyzes the whole project for cross-module resolutions, then scopes output to just that file.

**Operating principle:** TS reference inference is _mostly good_ — it's the oracle for compliance questions about the type system. But the Rust port doesn't have to inherit TS's historical accommodations: where the TS shape conflates two distinct concepts or under-specifies a type the language admits, we ship the more precise shape and allow-list the divergence.

> Goal restated: **compliance at the type-system level, plus better features where we can do strictly better.**

Validate every analyzer / resolver change against `dump-types` over the same fixture. When the diff is non-empty, the next question is "is this the Rust port being wrong, or is this an intentional improvement?" — answer in the allow-list (P18.3) rooted in the language reference, not in TS-inertia.

**Implementation pointer (TS side):** `packages/cli/src/dump/` with a `RecordingAnalyzer` Proxy at `shared.ts:303` that wraps `GreycatAnalyzer.analyze()` to capture per-node `Value` returns.

**Intentional divergences from TS (allow-list seeds for the P18 parity gate):**

- **Method-access without call (`x.s.method`) types as `function`, not the method's return type.** TS auto-evaluates the access to the call's return type, conflating the _method-reference value_ with the _call result_. Methods are first-class `function` values in gcl; the Rust port respects that distinction so `var f = x.s.method;` types `f: function`, not `f: int`. (P16.1's `MemberDef::Method → Named("function")` is the correct shape.)
- More entries land here as we discover them — each one needs a one-line justification rooted in the language reference, not TS-inertia.

---

### Phase 17 — Real-corpus parity ratchet (~1-2 weeks)

**Goal:** drop the false-positive count on real-world projects to (near) zero, so the diagnostic-parity oracle (P14.2) can ratchet meaningfully. Driven by [tests/parity/registry_baseline/REPORT.md](../tests/parity/registry_baseline/REPORT.md), which captured 224 false-positive diagnostics on `~/dev/datathings/greycat/apps/registry` against TS reference's 0. Every chunk targets a specific bucket from that report.

P17 sits in parallel with P16: P16 handles "Bucket A" (member-flow `any` cascades) via the typing pipeline; P17 handles the lowering / lint-policy bugs that surface as Buckets B-F regardless of typing.

**Chunks:**

- [x] **17.1 Capture baseline** (S) — done in this session. [tests/parity/registry_baseline/](../tests/parity/registry_baseline/) holds the TS + Rust outputs verbatim plus a bucketed analysis. The `REPORT.md` is the source-of-truth tracking doc for everything below.

- [x] **17.2 `for-in` lowering + tuple-form support** (M) — fixed [`hir/lower.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-hir/src/lower.rs)'s `for_in_stmt` arm which read `child_by_field_name("iterator")` (the _iterable_ expression, not a param wrapper) and asked for `name` on it, dropping the entire `for_in_stmt` from the HIR via the `?` short-circuit. New shape walks named children for `for_in_param` nodes. `ForInStmt` now carries `params: Vec<ForInParam { name, ty }>` instead of a single `iterator_name` / `iterator_type` pair, so the grammar's `sepBy2(",", $.for_in_param)` (every for-in is at least 2-tuple) is representable. Updated callers in resolver / capabilities scope walker / `lookup_name_type_in_stmt`. New resolver test `for_in_tuple_form_binds_both_params`. **Acceptance:** registry baseline went from 103 → 31 warnings (–70%) as for-in bodies finally reach the resolver. Errors went 121 → 183 because the body now visits with `any`-typed receivers — Bucket A territory, closes with P16.

- [x] **17.3 `catch (ex)` param binding** (XS) — `_catch_param` is a hidden rule (`seq("(", $.ident, ")")`), so tree-sitter inlines its children into the parent and tags every child with the `error_param` field. The previous lowering asked for a non-existent `name` sub-field; my first attempt picked the first field-tagged child (the `(` token); the working fix uses `children_by_field_name("error_param", &mut cursor).find(|c| c.kind() == "ident")`. New resolver unit test `catch_param_binds_in_catch_block` locks the binding in.

- [x] **17.4 `@library` webroot fallback** (S) — `pragma_diagnostics`'s resolution check now considers four locations before flagging an unresolved library: `<project>/lib/<name>/`, `<project>/webroot/<name>/`, the `<project>/lib/installed` manifest (`greycat install`'s record of names → versions, counts even when the directory hasn't been materialized), and the `std` fallback under `<greycat_home>`. Asset-only libraries (e.g. `explorer` ships as a webroot bundle with no `.gcl`) now resolve cleanly. 2 new tests cover the webroot and manifest cases. **Acceptance:** registry baseline's `@library('explorer'): library not found` warning is gone.

- [x] **17.5 String-interpolation `${expr}` lowering** (M) — [`StringExpr`](../greycat-analyzer-hir/src/types.rs) is now `parts: Vec<StringPart>` with `Lit { text, byte_range }` / `Interp { expr, byte_range }`. Lowering walks every `string` named child and emits `Lit` for `string_fragment` / `string_escape_sequence`, `Interp` (with the inner `_expr` lowered to a HIR expression) for `string_substitution`. `StringExpr::raw_value()` / `has_interpolation()` keep the prior literal-extraction sites working (`@permission(...)`, fmt). The resolver / analyzer now recurse into `Interp` exprs so locals referenced only inside `"${name}"` bind correctly. The parity-oracle's `dump-types` emits `TemplateExpr` at the outer string and `RawStringExpr` / `InterpolationExpr` per part — registry parity diff dropped from 3448 → ~2700 lines.

- [ ] **17.6 Gate unused-local / unused-param behind `--lint-unused`** (S) — TS reference doesn't emit unused-local / unused-param at all by default. Gate the [`unused-local`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/lint.rs) + [`unused-param`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/lint.rs) lint rules behind a CLI flag (`greycat-lang lint --lint-unused`) and an LSP setting (later — for now, off in the LSP path too). Default `lint` matches TS's "trust the user" policy. **Acceptance:** registry baseline's 31 + 23 unused-param/local warnings disappear at the default cli flag set; explicit `--lint-unused` re-enables them.

- [ ] **17.7 Re-baseline + parity ratchet test** (S) — re-run both linters on the registry project after P17.2-6 land, regenerate [registry_baseline/](../tests/parity/registry_baseline/), and add a CI test (`registry_parity_floor`) that asserts the rust output's diagnostic count is `<= N` for some N that ratchets toward zero. Mirrors the formatter parity gauntlet's `MATCH_FLOOR` pattern. P14.2 (the diagnostic parity gate) consumes this as one of its corpora.

**M17:** `greycat-analyzer lint` on `~/dev/datathings/greycat/apps/registry` produces ≤ 5 residual diagnostics (all genuine), down from 224. The registry-parity CI gate is green and the floor is live.

---

### Phase 18 — Typed-AST parity oracle (~1-2 weeks)

**Goal:** turn the TS-side `dump-types` / `dump-resolutions` / `dump-hir` subcommands into a CI-grade parity gate so any analyzer / resolver change is validated against the oracle automatically. Closes ROADMAP §7-A end-to-end with a stronger signal than the diagnostic-diff (P14.2) — it catches silent typing regressions where the type is wrong but no diagnostic fires (which is what the registry baseline shows: 96 of 121 errors were downstream effects of silent `any`-typing).

P18 sits after P16/P17 — they fix the gross gaps; P18 ratchets the residual diff toward zero with the oracle's help.

**Chunks:**

- [x] **18.1 Mirror `dump-types` / `dump-resolutions` on the Rust side** (M) — new `greycat-analyzer dump-types <path> [--filter R]` and `dump-resolutions <path> [--filter R]` subcommands in [`greycat-analyzer/src/cmd/dump_types.rs`](../greycat-analyzer/src/cmd/dump_types.rs) emit the **same JSONL shape** as the TS reference. Every `dump-types` record carries `file`, `range`, `line`, `col`, `endLine`, `endCol`, `kind` (TS-side names: `Identifier`, `InstanceAccessExpr`, `CallExpr`, `TypeIdent`, `NumLit`, `StringLit`, `TemplateExpr`, `InterpolationExpr`, `RawStringExpr`, `StaticAccessExpr`, `RefAccessExpr`, `OffsetAccessExpr`, `ObjectExpr`, `ArrayExpr`, `BinOpExpr`, `PrefixExpr`, `NonNullAssertExpr`, `AsExpr`, `IsExpr`, `ThisLit`, `BoolLit`, `CharLit`, `NullLit`, `LambdaExpr`); `type` is rendered via the new [`display_fqn`](../greycat-analyzer-types/src/lib.rs) helper that emits `core::int`, `core::Array<core::int | null>`, `project::Foo`, etc. — primitives + builtin runtime types live under `core::`, user types resolve via `ProjectIndex::decl_locations` to their home module's stem. `dump-resolutions` records carry `refKind` / `declKind` / `name` / `decl: { fqn, file, range, line, col }` and walk the HIR for both use-site bindings (via `Resolutions.uses`) _and_ decl-site self-bindings (the TS reference emits the latter for every fn / type / enum / var / fnparam / catchparam). Records sorted by `(file, line, col, byteStart, byteEnd)`; `--filter` accepts `B`, `B-B`, `L:C`, `L:C-L:C`.

- [x] **18.2 `parity-types.sh` driver + diff helper** (S) — new [`scripts/parity-types.sh`](../scripts/parity-types.sh) and [`scripts/parity-resolutions.sh`](../scripts/parity-resolutions.sh) wrap both engines, pipe through the divergences allow-list ([`scripts/_apply_divergences.py`](../scripts/_apply_divergences.py)), `LC_ALL=C sort` both streams, and emit a unified `diff -u`. Exit non-zero on non-empty diff so the script composes into CI. The python filter supports both _direct_ (kind + ts*type / rust_type) and \_position-widening* (`match_by_position = true`) entries — the latter rewrites TS-side records at the same `(file, range, kind)` as a Rust-side hit, which is what handles bare-fn-name idents whose TS shape varies per call-site (`core::int` for callee-position, `core::any | null` elsewhere).

- [x] **18.3 `tests/parity/<corpus>/{types.diff, resolutions.diff}` baselines + intentional-divergence allow-list** (S) — captured under [`tests/parity/project_gcl/`](../tests/parity/project_gcl/) and [`tests/parity/registry_baseline/`](../tests/parity/registry_baseline/). The allow-list at [`tests/parity/divergences.toml`](../tests/parity/divergences.toml) seeds three entries: method-reference value typing (TS auto-evaluates to return type, Rust types as `core::function`), bare fn-decl reference (TS=`core::any | null`, Rust=`core::function`), bare type-decl reference (Rust=`core::type`). Each entry carries `match_by_position` where TS's call-site auto-eval needs widening. `lib_std` baseline deferred — stdlib parity needs P14.x cross-module work to settle first.

- [x] **18.4 CI parity gauntlet** (S) — new [`.github/workflows/parity.yml`](../.github/workflows/parity.yml) gates on the `parity` PR label (or workflow_dispatch) since the TS reference binary isn't available on the default GitHub runner. The job builds the Rust port (`--release`), locates `greycat-lang` on PATH, and runs `parity-types.sh` + `parity-resolutions.sh` against `project.gcl`, asserting the `^[-+]\{` diff line count is ≤ the committed baseline. Future P18.5 chunks will tighten that bound iteratively.

- [ ] **18.5 Per-bucket ratchet on the registry corpus** (M) — open a tracking issue per residual diff bucket discovered by 18.3. Each subsequent P18.5.x chunk is "close bucket X by N entries". Stops when registry baseline is empty. Same gauntlet pattern as the formatter: ratchet the floor down per chunk.

**M18:** `parity-types.sh ~/dev/datathings/greycat/apps/registry` reports an empty diff. CI runs the gauntlet on every push; analyzer / resolver regressions break the build immediately. ROADMAP §7-A's "are we 1:1?" answer is automated.

---

### Phase 19 — Staged-pipeline analyzer rewrite (~4-6 weeks)

**Goal:** replace the current per-module + post-pass analyzer with a strict 12-stage pipeline (S1-S12) that builds program-wide typing knowledge in monotonically-growing layers before any body is walked. The post-pass churn (3 → 3.4 → 3.45 → 3.5 → 3.52 → 3.55 → 3.6) is a symptom of the per-module arena + name-shape translation layer; the staged design eliminates both. The 12 stages: **S1-S3** declare type/fn/modvar names (IDs stable); **S4-S6** define type structure (no type lowering yet); **S7-S11** complete attr / method / static-fields / fn / modvar TypeRefs against the now-complete name set; **S12** body walker (CFG + narrowing + per-expr typing + monomorphization + diagnostics) runs against fully-resolved signatures.

P19 lays the foundation: lift the [`TypeArena`](../greycat-analyzer-types/src/lib.rs) from per-module into project-wide, add an `arena.substitute(ty, &subst) → TypeId` primitive to replace the receiver-driven shim, and rewire every cross-module pass to mint into the shared arena instead of the per-module one. Mechanical change with no behavior delta — gated on the existing 80 + 46 + 21 + LSP-capability tests staying green and the registry parity baseline ≤ 48.

**Chunks:**

- [x] **19.1 Shared `TypeArena` (P19)** (L) — `TypeArena` lifts to [`ProjectAnalysis::arena`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/project.rs); `analyze_with_index_into(hir, res, index, &mut arena)` is the new entry point, `analyze`/`analyze_with_index` keep their old signatures by allocating + returning a private arena. `AnalysisResult` no longer owns `types`. Every cross-module post-pass (3, 3.4, 3.45, 3.5, 3.52) now mints into `&mut self.arena` via split borrows. Capability handlers (hover, inlay hints, member completion, scope name meta) pull the arena via `project.arena()` rather than `module.analysis.types`. Adds `TypeArena::substitute(ty, &HashMap<String, TypeId>) → TypeId` primitive in [`greycat-analyzer-types`](../greycat-analyzer-types/src/lib.rs) — the algebra the upcoming S12 body walker (P23) consumes directly. **No behavior change** — all 80 analyzer tests + 46 analysis tests + 21 types tests + 17 LSP capability tests stay green.

- [x] **19.2 Staged orchestrator skeleton (P20)** (M) — `ProjectAnalysis::analyze_staged` is the new top-level orchestrator with named `stage_lower` / `stage_per_module_analysis` / `stage_cross_module_post_passes` / `stage_compute_qualified_refs` methods that future phases (P21-P23) peel apart. `rebuild` re-routes through it. Same shape, named seam — 292 tests still green, no behavior change.
- [x] **19.3 S1-S6 extraction (P21)** (L) — `ProjectIndex::type_members` is the new pre-computed cross-module structure index (`type_name → { home_uri, attrs: name→Idx<TypeAttr>, methods: name→Idx<Decl> }`), populated by `ProjectIndex::ingest` alongside `decl_locations`. The analyzer's `Cx::resolve_member` consults it for foreign types and writes directly to `foreign_member_uses`. **Pass 3** (`resolve_cross_module_members`) **deleted** along with `AnalysisResult::deferred_member_uses` — no more deferral list, no more post-pass drain. 292 tests still green; registry baseline unchanged because pass 3 was a binding-resolution drain (not a typing fix), and the analyzer's foreign-binding behavior is now direct.
- [x] **19.4 S7-S11 extraction (P22)** (XL) — `ProjectAnalysis::stage_lower_signatures` walks every type's attrs + method returns project-wide, lowers each `TypeRef` into the shared arena via the new `lower_type_ref_project` free function, and records the resulting `TypeId`s on `TypeMembers::{generics, attr_types, method_returns}`. The analyzer's `Cx::foreign_member_type` consults this index inline at body-walk time + applies `arena.substitute(ty, &subst)` for receiver-driven generic substitution. **Pass 3.4 (`infer_cross_module_member_types`) and pass 3.45 (`propagate_member_types_from_current`) deleted** — together ~250 LoC of post-pass machinery removed. Pass 3.52 (`rebind_for_in_iter_types`) and the receiver-driven substitution shim (`resolve_member_call_return_shape_subst`) survive until P23 absorbs cross-module call typing into the staged S12 walker. 292 tests still green.
- [x] **19.5 S12 body walker (P23)** (XL) — analyzer's body walker now types Member / Arrow / Static / QualifiedStatic / Ident calls inline via the S7-S11 signatures index (`Cx::try_member_call_typing`, `Cx::method_return_for`, `Cx::bare_fn_return`, `Cx::qualified_static_call_return`). Static / QualifiedStatic value-position exprs (`Foo::method` without parens, `module::Type`, etc.) type inline via `static_value_type` / `qualified_static_value_type`. Bare type / fn idents type as `type` / `function` directly from the analyzer (cross-module via `index.fn_signatures`). Chain-segment bindings (`foreign_decl_uses[chain[1]]`, `foreign_member_uses[chain[2]]`) populate inline from `bind_qualified_chain_segments`. Enum types pre-registered in the shared arena via `index.enum_types`. **Pass 3.5 (`infer_cross_module_call_types`), pass 3.52 (`rebind_for_in_iter_types`), and the receiver-driven substitution shim (`resolve_member_call_return_shape_subst`) all become dead-call-targets in `stage_cross_module_post_passes`** — the post-passes shrink to just typed-lints (3.55) + type-relation validation (3.6). 292 tests still green. Pass 3.55 / 3.6 deletion + dead-code removal of the now-unused 3.5 / 3.52 / shim functions deferred to P26 cleanup.
- [x] **19.6 Query-DAG invalidation (P24)** (L) — `invalidate(uri)` now correctly re-runs `lower_signatures_into` (S7-S11) project-wide on every edit, so the post-P22 signature index doesn't go stale when an attr / method / fn return type changes. The free-function `lower_signatures_into` takes split `&mut TypeArena` + `&mut ProjectIndex` borrows so the invalidate path can build the `(Uri, &Hir)` slice from references into `self.modules` — no `Hir` clone. Dead pass 3.5 / pass 3.52 calls removed from invalidate. **Per-stage hashing follow-up landed:** `ProjectAnalysis::sig_cache: HashMap<Uri, ModuleSigCache>` records each module's signature-stage contributions (attr / method / fn / enum updates) keyed by `(module_signature_hash, project_name_set_hash)`. `module_signature_hash(hir)` walks every top-level type / fn / enum decl name, generic ident, and reachable `TypeRef` (recursively) — body statements are excluded so a body-only edit doesn't change the hash. `project_name_set_hash(index)` fingerprints the post-ingest name set so a change in name visibility (which would flip `Named(name)` ↔ `any()` inside `lower_type_ref_project`) forces a re-walk. Cache hit → reapply cached `(attr_types, method_returns, fn_signatures, enum_types)` updates verbatim; cache miss → walk that one module's signatures and refresh the entry. Arena is append-only across `invalidate` so cached `TypeId`s stay valid; `reset_state` clears the cache when `analyze_staged` rebuilds from scratch. 82 analysis tests (was 80 — 2 new tests anchor the body-only fast-path and the signature-edit refresh path).
- [x] **19.7 Cleanup (P26)** (S) — deleted the dead post-pass methods (`rebind_for_in_iter_types`, `infer_cross_module_call_types`) and the standalone shim functions (`resolve_static_member_shape`, `static_shape_from_member`, `resolve_qualified_static_shape`, `resolve_qualified_static_call_shape`, `resolve_static_call_return_shape`, `resolve_ident_call_return_shape`, `resolve_member_call_return_shape`, `resolve_member_call_return_shape_subst`, `resolve_bare_ident_decl_shape`, `read_type_id_shape`). `QualifiedTarget::EnumVariant` lost its unused `decl: Idx<Decl>` field. `TypeShape` / `read_type_shape` / `read_type_shape_subst` / `mint_type_shape` survive — they're still used by the type-relation validator (`collect_call_arg_diags_split` in S12 cross-module suffix) where the shape detour is the simplest way to mint declared param types into the shared arena without a `&mut TypeArena` borrow conflict. Net: ~600 LoC of post-pass code gone from `project.rs`. **Note: P25 parallelism is dropped per user decision** ("single-threaded forever, focus elsewhere") — LSP idle most of the time, busy ≤ 200ms; complexity budget goes into incremental invalidation (P24) instead.

- [x] **19.8 Workspace `.clone()` / `.to_string()` audit** (M) — sweep landed in two flavours: (a) **direct wins** where a clone-out-then-mutate pattern could be replaced with a borrow + pre-bound fields, (b) **annotated necessities** where the clone is genuinely required by an outstanding `&mut self` and we leave a comment explaining _why_. Concrete wins:
  - [`Cx::try_generic_call_inference`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/analyzer.rs) — dropped the `self.hir.exprs[callee].clone()` + `self.hir.decls[decl_id].clone()` pair (a full `Expr` + full `Decl` clone _per generic call_) by destructuring into `(name_idx, fn_generics, fn_params, fn_return_type)` first; only the `Vec<Idx<Ident>>` / `Vec<Idx<FnParam>>` get cloned (32-bit indices, not the underlying nodes), which is what's actually needed to release the `&self.hir` borrow before the lowering loop's `&mut self` calls.
  - [`lower_module_signatures`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/project.rs) — replaced the per-method `method_generics = generics_in_scope.clone()` (a `HashMap<Symbol, GenericOwner>` clone, where each `GenericOwner` allocates a `String`) with a push-pop pattern: insert the method's generics directly into the type-level scope, save the prior values in a small `Vec<(Symbol, Option<GenericOwner>)>`, lower, then restore. For a type with M methods × N generics this drops M HashMap clones + M\*N inner String clones to one `Vec` of length N per method.

  Annotated remaining: ~50 `.clone()` calls in `analyzer.rs` (visit_decl / visit_stmt / infer_expr clone the active `Decl` / `Stmt` / `Expr` to escape an outstanding `&self.hir` borrow before `&mut self` calls — refactoring would require splitting every match arm's borrow scope individually, which is a separate XL chunk on its own); ~15 in `project.rs` (Uri keys, Span ranges, GenericOwner inserts); ~129 in `capabilities.rs` (LSP response construction — every `CompletionItem` / `Diagnostic` takes owned strings by API; not hot paths internal to the analyzer). The bigger interning win from P19.9 already paid down the largest category (project-wide indexes' name keys) — what survives is borrow-checker mechanics, not laziness.

- [x] **19.9 Project-wide identifier interning** (L) — `Symbol(u32)` + `SymbolTable` land in [`greycat-analyzer-types`](../greycat-analyzer-types/src/lib.rs); `ProjectIndex` gains a `pub symbols: SymbolTable` field that owns the canonical storage for every name the project-wide indexes key on. Every map on `ProjectIndex` (`values`, `decl_locations`, `exposed`, `type_flags`, `module_permissions`, `module_names`, `type_members`, `fn_signatures`, `enum_types`) plus `NativeRegistry.signatures` plus the `TypeMembers.{attrs, methods, attr_types, method_returns}` and `TypeMembers.generics` / `FnSignature.generics` collections are now `Symbol`-keyed. New `&str` accessors on `ProjectIndex` (`symbol`, `type_members_for`, `fn_signature_for`, `enum_type_for`, `native_for`, `type_flags_for`, `contains_value`, `contains_type_member`, `contains_fn_signature`) and on `TypeMembers` (`attr_id`, `method_id`, `attr_ty`, `method_return`) keep the historic API surface — every callsite inside the analyzer / resolver / lints / capability handlers consumes the new helpers, no fan-out into intern-then-lookup at every body-walk site. `ProjectIndex::with_symbols(SymbolTable)` lets `invalidate` rebuild per-module data while preserving the interner so previously-issued `Symbol`s (notably the P19.6 sig_cache entries) stay valid across edits. **`TypeRegistry` deliberately stays `String`-keyed** — it's reused per-module on `AnalysisResult` where no project-wide interner is in scope; folding it in would either duplicate the table or thread `&mut SymbolTable` through every per-module entry point. 296 workspace tests (was 294 — 2 new tests anchor the symbol-table API + the cross-index intern invariant). Follow-ups: P19.x `ProjectIndex::clear()` to reuse map allocator capacity across `invalidate` (instead of `with_symbols` + `Default::default()`); evaluate `SmolStr` for the per-module `AnalysisResult.{type_decls, registry}` String storage that interning doesn't touch.

- [x] **19.12 Range / interval expressions in offset & for-in slots** (M) — grammar gap surfaced by a real-world corpus: `arr[from..to]`, `arr[from..]`, `arr[..to]` (canonical bracketless ranges) plus the math-style `]from..to]` / `[from..to[` interval forms (open/closed bracket per side) didn't parse. Two new grammar nodes in [`tree-sitter-greycat/grammar.js`](../tree-sitter-greycat/grammar.js): (a) `range_expr` is a first-class `_expr` (`from..to` with optional endpoints, prec 1 — looser than every arithmetic / comparison operator so `arr[a + b .. c - d]` parses as `(a+b)..(c-d)`); (b) `interval_expr` is a separate `_expr` for the bracket-bearing math interval (`]a..b]` / `[a..b[` / etc.) with explicit prec 2 + a left-recursive conflict declaration (`]..]..` doesn't chain). The unused `iterator_range` for-in clause was renamed and re-fielded as `range: optional($.interval_expr)` so the math-style form can attach AFTER a nullable iterator (`for (..., d in detections?]a..b])`); the bracketless form parses as `offset_expr` containing a `range_expr`. **Acceptance:** corpus parse errors went from 18 → 1 on the closed-source corpus; remaining one is a doc-comment case unrelated to ranges.

- [x] **19.23 Evict no-longer-reachable modules + LSP info logs for closure changes** (S) — closes the eviction half of P19.22. Symptom: commenting out an `@library("foo", "1.0")` line in `project.gcl` left `lib/foo/`'s modules in `SourceManager.documents` and in `ProjectAnalysis.modules`, so the types they exposed still resolved and the editor never saw the resulting "unknown type" errors. (1) **`LoadReport.reachable: Vec<Uri>`** — every URI traversed by `load_project` (newly loaded + already in manager from prior calls). The post-P19.22 `loaded` field only carried newly-loaded URIs after the idempotency change, so we couldn't compute the closure from it. (2) **`SourceManager::evict_unreachable(reachable: &HashSet<Uri>) -> Vec<Uri>`** — drops every closed (`!opened`) document not in the reachable set. Returns the evicted URIs so the LSP layer can publish empty diagnostics. Opened buffers are preserved (the editor owns their live state). (3) **`Backend::reload_project_closure` wiring** — after `load_project`, build the reachable set, evict, then `rebuild`. The full rebuild naturally drops `ProjectAnalysis.modules` entries for evicted URIs (they're no longer in `manager.iter()`). Republishes for every URI in the closure (not just newly-loaded ones) since previously-clean modules may now have new errors after a lib disappears. (4) **Info-level closure-change logs** — `[reload_project] loaded N new file(s):` and `[reload_project] evicted N unreachable file(s):` with one `+` / `-` line per URI, plus a one-line summary `closure: N reachable, M added, K evicted`. Visible in the VS Code extension's output channel without enabling debug logging. **Acceptance:** new integration test [`library_eviction.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/tests/library_eviction.rs) reproduces the bug (lib type used in `main.gcl`; comment out `@library`; assert unresolved-`Foo` diagnostic surfaces). Test fails before the fix, passes after.

- [x] **19.22 LSP keeps up with project closure changes** (M) — when the user edits `project.gcl`'s `@library` / `@include` pragmas in the editor, or when an external tool (typically `greycat install`) writes new files into `lib/<name>/` plus the `lib/installed` manifest, the LSP previously didn't notice — the resolver kept its old closure and newly-reachable modules went un-analyzed. Two complementary fixes mirror the TS reference's [packages/server/src/index.ts:294](https://hub.datathings.com/greycat/lang) approach. (1) **In-editor pragma reload** — `Backend::did_change` now checks whether the changed URI is the project entrypoint via a new `is_project_entrypoint(uri)` helper (canonical-path comparison so symlinks etc. behave). When it is, route to a new `reload_project_closure()` that calls `SourceManager::load_project` against the in-memory pragmas and runs `ProjectAnalysis::rebuild`. To make this safe (the editor owns the live state of opened buffers), [`SourceManager::load_file`](../greycat-analyzer-core/src/manager.rs) is now **idempotent across calls**: if the URI is already in `documents`, skip the disk read entirely. New 1-line `documents.contains_key(&uri)` guard at the top. New `load_project_preserves_in_memory_documents` test covers it (47 core tests, was 46). (2) **External file watcher** — `Backend::initialized` now sends `client/registerCapability` for `workspace/didChangeWatchedFiles` with two glob watchers (`**/*.gcl` and `**/lib/installed`), gated on the client supporting dynamic registration. New `did_change_watched_files` handler dispatches: `lib/installed` events trigger `reload_project_closure()`; `*.gcl` events skip files the editor owns (live state lives in `did_change`), refresh closed sources from disk + invalidate, and `Created` / `Deleted` trigger a full reload (in case the new/gone file is reachable through a pragma). New `DidChangeWatchedFiles::METHOD` dispatch in `main_loop`. **Acceptance:** adding `@library("foo", "1.0");` to `project.gcl` in the editor now triggers immediate analysis of the new lib's modules without an LSP restart; running `greycat install` while the editor is open populates the new lib's diagnostics within milliseconds of the `lib/installed` manifest being touched.

- [x] **19.21 Narrowing extensions: `?=` (coalesce-assign) + `->` (Arrow) paths** (S) — closes the two largest false-positive sources surfaced by the solarleb corpus (80 diagnostics → 38). (1) **`?=` (coalesce-assign) narrow** — new `record_coalesce_assign_narrow` mirrors `record_assign_narrow` but with `?=`'s asymmetric semantics: `x ?= value` only fires when `x` is null, so a previously-non-null `x` stays non-null. With non-null RHS, narrows LHS to non-null; with nullable RHS, makes no claim (and crucially does NOT drop existing narrows). Wired into the `BinOp::Other("?=")` arm. Closes the dominant solarleb pattern (`country->governorates ?= nodeIndex<…> {};`) where the `?=` initialization line should narrow the field for subsequent reads. (2) **Arrow-path narrowing** — `member_path` now walks `Expr::Arrow` with `->` separator (keys disjoint from dot-form so `x.y` and `x->y` don't share narrows); `member_compared_to_null` recognizes `Arrow != null` shapes; `record_assign_narrow` accepts Arrow LHS; the strip-nullable check at the bottom of the Member arm in `infer_expr` now applies to Arrow too. Together these enable `if (x->y == null) return;` post-guard narrowing and `x->y != null && x->y.foo()` short-circuit narrowing on node-tag receivers. **Acceptance:** 4 new lint unit tests cover `?=` on Member-LHS / Arrow-LHS, post-guard Arrow narrowing, and short-circuit `&&` Arrow narrowing. solarleb corpus drops from 80 → 38 diagnostics; remaining are real (5 errors in `lib/algebra/`, ~12 unused-local/param, 5 non-exhaustive enums, 5 inferred-return-type hints, 2 redundant `!!`).

- [x] **19.20 Inferred return-type hint + `*n` deref exemption** (S) — two paired changes. (1) New `lint_inferred_return_type` typed lint emits a HINT diagnostic on each `Decl::Fn` (top-level + type methods) that lacks a declared `return_type` but whose body terminates in `return e;` with a settled, informative `expr_types` entry. Skips `Any` / `Never` (uninformative), `native` / `abstract` modifiers (no body), and fns with already-declared return types. Mirrors the TS reference's `Return type can be inferred as 'X'` hint; quickfix synthesis is deferred (param-list-end position requires source scan). (2) Documented that `*n` (`Expr::Unary { op: Deref }`) is intentionally exempt from the `possibly-null` lint — the GreyCat runtime's deref operator handles a null receiver gracefully (returns `null`), so flagging would be a false positive. We diverge from the TS reference here per user direction; the doc-comment in `lint_nullability` records the rationale so it doesn't get accidentally "fixed" later. **Acceptance:** `fn foo(n: node<String>?) { return *n; }` now emits the inference hint without a spurious `'n' is possibly 'null'` warning.

- [x] **19.19 Call arity check** (S) — extended [`collect_call_arg_diags_split`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/project.rs) to compare `fnd.params.len()` against `call.args.len()` _before_ the per-arg pair-type loop, since a wrong arity makes per-arg diagnostics ambiguous (continues out of the call). Independent of generics — `fn<T>(x: T)` still has arity 1, so the check applies uniformly. Highlight range is the arg-list parens (`callee_end..call_end`), matching the TS reference's span. Covers Ident / Static / QualifiedStatic callees (the same scope as `resolve_call_target`); Member/Arrow callees aren't yet routed through that helper. **Acceptance:** `println(foo())` (where `foo` has arity 1) now reports `function `foo` expects 1 argument, but got 0` matching the TS reference.

- [x] **19.18 Module-variable shape lints** (S) — three sibling rules in a new `ModVarShape` lint (HIR-only, runs as part of `run_lints`) catch the constraints the GreyCat runtime imposes on top-level `var` declarations: `modvar-must-be-node-tag` flags non-node-tag types like `var x: int;`, `modvar-node-cannot-be-nullable` flags an outer `?` on a node-tag (`var x: node<int?>?;`) since nodes are auto-initialized, and `modvar-node-inner-must-be-nullable` flags `node<T>` whose inner `T` lacks `?` (the resolved value may be unset; collections don't enforce this). Quickfixes wired in both LSP `synthesize_fix` and CLI `--fix`: drop the trailing `?` for the outer-nullable case, append `?` to the inner type for the missing-inner-nullable case. The "must be node-tag" case has no auto-fix (depends on user intent). **Acceptance:** running `cli lint` on the project.gcl scratchpad now matches the TS reference's `Module variable type must be one of …` and `Nodes are automatically initialized by GreyCat …` errors.

- [x] **19.17 Nullability propagation + null-hygiene lint family + null-safe completion** (M) — closes a large inference flaw plus the missing TS-reference `'x' is possibly 'null'` lint family, with a completion-side affordance to keep the editor experience aligned. (1) **Nullability propagates _up the chain_** — [`Expr::Member` / `Expr::Arrow`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/analyzer.rs) used to gate the `?.` lift on `pre_optional && recv.nullable`, so `x?.y.z` (where `x: Outer?`) typed as `Z` instead of `Z?` because the outer `.z` step had `pre_optional=false`. The runtime evaluates the whole chain to null when any prior `?.` shorts, so the typing now lifts whenever the receiver is nullable, regardless of whether the user wrote `?.` at this segment. The `pre_optional` flag survives as the _lint_ gate (no diagnostic when the user wrote `?.`); typing no longer reads it. Mirrored in `try_member_call_typing`'s `CalleeShape::Member` arm so `x?.foo().bar` carries the nullability through the call as well. The P19.16 narrow-strip at the bottom of the Member arm still wins when an enclosing scope guarded the member-path non-null. (2) **`lint_nullability` typed-lint family** — four sibling rules driven by the post-S12 `expr_types` table, registered next to `lint_arrow_on_non_deref` in `run_typed_lints`: `possibly-null` (Member / Arrow / Offset on a nullable receiver without `?.` / `?->` / `?[`), `redundant-nullable-access` (`?.` etc. when receiver already non-null), `redundant-non-null-assertion` (`!!` on a non-null operand), `redundant-coalesce` (`?? rhs` on a non-null lhs). All four skip `Any` and `Null` kinds (`any` carries `nullable: true` in the arena and would over-fire). The receiver text in the `possibly-null` message is built by walking the HIR (Ident / Member / Arrow / Static / Paren chains) so we get `'foo.bar'` instead of just `'expression'` for non-trivial receivers. (3) **Optional-chaining short-circuit awareness** — naive nullability propagation would make `n?.resolve().chars()` fire `possibly-null` on `.chars()` because the chain's expression type is nullable. But optional chaining short-circuits the _whole suffix_ — at runtime, if `?.` shorts, `.chars()` isn't evaluated, so it's safe. New `chain_has_upstream_nullsafe(hir, expr_id)` helper walks the receiver chain (Member / Arrow / Offset / Call / Paren) looking for an upstream `pre_optional` / `post_optional`; the `possibly-null` lint and the completion auto-`?.` both consult it and skip when the chain is already protected. The _typing_ still propagates (the expression really is nullable), but the lint correctly recognizes the runtime guarantee. (4) **Quickfix synthesis** — both `synthesize_fix` (LSP) and `diag_to_edit` (CLI `--fix`) gained the four codes. `possibly-null` scans forward from the receiver's end over whitespace until it hits `.` / `->` / `[` and inserts `?` there; the others do byte-range deletions. The `!!` slice computation accounts for the operator being _postfix_ in GreyCat (`$._expr, "!!"` in [grammar.js:391](../tree-sitter-greycat/grammar.js#L391)). (5) **Completion auto-`?.`** — when the receiver type is nullable, the user typed plain `.` / `->`, AND the chain doesn't already have an upstream `?.`, every member-completion item now carries an `additional_text_edits` that inserts `?` at `sep_start`. The label is rewritten to `?.size` (or `?->size`) so the user sees the rewrite _before_ accepting; `filter_text` and `sort_text` keep the bare name so typing `s` still filters to `?.size` and the list ordering is unchanged from the non-null case. The label-prefix shape was chosen after the user pointed out that LSP renders `label_details.detail` _after_ the label (so `size?.` would be wrong). **Acceptance:** 11 new lint unit tests + 3 new completion tests cover the rules, the chain-protection logic, and the rewrite shape; 95 analysis tests + 74 LSP capability tests still green; running our `cli lint` against `project.gcl` now reports the same `'n' is possibly 'null'` warning the TS reference reports without false positives on `.chars()` etc.

- [x] **19.16 Post-if narrow lift + member-access narrowing + `??` precedence + runtime globals** (M) — corpus baseline 48 → 27. (1) **Post-if assignment narrow lift** — `Stmt::If` captures each branch's terminal narrow frame and joins them: a binding that's nullable before the if and non-null along _every_ reaching path (condition implication, in-branch assignment, or branch terminating) is narrowed to non-null in the post-if scope. The narrow record was previously being written to `Stmt::Assign`, but GreyCat's `=` lowers to `Expr::Binary { op: BinOp::Other("=") }` wrapped in `Stmt::Expr`, so the narrow never fired; moved the narrow record into the `Expr::Binary` arm via a new `record_assign_narrow(target, value_ty)` helper that handles both Ident-LHS and Member-LHS cases. (2) **Member-access narrowing** — new `member_narrows: Vec<HashSet<String>>` parallel stack keyed by receiver-rooted path strings (`"this.matchingNormalisation"`, `"foo.bar.baz"`); `derive_cond_narrows` detects `member_expr != null` shapes via `member_compared_to_null`, the if-handler applies path-narrows in-branch + lifts them post-if same as ident narrows, and `Expr::Member` strips the result's nullable bit when its `member_path(expr_id)` is in scope. Member-LHS assignments write / drop path narrows based on the RHS's nullability so a stale narrow doesn't survive a reassignment to a maybe-null value. (3) **`??` precedence fix** — the runtime parser (and the TS reference at [`parser.ts:2319-2367`](https://hub.datathings.com/greycat/lang) where `opPrecedence` falls through to `default: 15` for `QuestionQuestion`) treat `??` as the _highest_ binary operator, above `^`/`*`/`+`/`>`/etc. Our grammar had it at prec 3 alongside `||`, so `count ?? 0 > 0` was parsing as `count ?? (0 > 0)` (typing `int | bool`) instead of `(count ?? 0) > 0` (typing `bool`). Bumped `??` to prec 11 in [`tree-sitter-greycat/grammar.js`](../tree-sitter-greycat/grammar.js) with a corpus regression test. (4) **`Infinity` / `NaN` runtime globals** — added `BUILTIN_RUNTIME_GLOBALS` table + `ProjectIndex.runtime_globals: HashMap<Symbol, TypeId>` populated in `with_symbols`, plus `runtime_global_for(name)` accessor. The analyzer's `Definition::Project` arm consults it before falling back to `any`. (5) **Generic-arg wildcard rule conservativization** — the P19.14 follow-up's per-arg `any` wildcard (`Foo<T>` → `Foo<X, any>`) was too permissive: the runtime accepts `Map<S,int>` → `Map<any,any>` (full wildcard) but rejects `Map<S,int>` → `Map<S,any>` (partial V-wildcard) and rejects partial wildcards on user-defined generics. Tightened to "all target args are `any`" globally, matching the runtime's conservative behavior. **Anti-monkey-patching note** added to [`.claude/CLAUDE.md`](../.claude/CLAUDE.md): when a typing diagnostic looks wrong, fix the _originating_ analysis stage, not by post-patching the result downstream. **Acceptance:** corpus baseline 48 → 27 (1 remaining error is the real `this.window_frequency` source bug — corpus author's own `//todo remove nullable` comment confirms — line 1122 uses `!!`, line 1123 forgot it); registry baseline still 0; 297 workspace tests still green.

- [x] **19.15 Range expressions + cross-module generic inference + raw collection for-in** (M) — corpus baseline 75 → 48. (1) **Range as a HIR node** — `range_expr` (`from..to` / `from..` / `..to`) and `interval_expr` (`]from..to]` / `[from..to[` etc.) flatten into one `Expr::Range { from: Option<Idx<Expr>>, to: Option<Idx<Expr>>, byte_range }` since bracket inclusivity isn't load-bearing for typing. Resolver / analyzer / wasm renderer / dump*types all match the new variant. (2) **OffsetExpr slice typing** — when the index is `Expr::Range`, the offset returns the \_receiver* unchanged (`nt[1..10]` over `nodeTime<T>` still iterates as `(time, T)`). Otherwise it's element-wise lookup as before, now also covering `nodeTime<T>` (was missing). (3) **Cross-module generic call inference** — `try_generic_call_inference` matches `Definition::ProjectDecl` too: pulls pre-lowered params + return from `FnSignature` (extended with `params: Vec<TypeId>` populated by `lower_module_signatures`) and runs the same witness-driven `collect_witnesses` loop. Stdlib `abs<T>(x: T): T` now infers `T` from the call-site arg, so `abs(this.usedPV) + abs(...) + abs(...)` types as `float` instead of `any`. (4) **Raw-named collection for-in** — for-in over `Named { "nodeTime" }` (raw) binds `(time, any)`; same shape for `Array`/`Set`/`nodeList` (raw → `(int, any)`), `nodeGeo` (raw → `(geo, any)`). Was falling through to `(any, any)`. (5) **Nullable-stripping arithmetic** — `time - time?` types as `duration` (the null case raises at runtime); applied per-arm to `+`/`-`/`*` so `Coalesce`'s `rt.nullable` check on the original operand stays intact. **Acceptance:** corpus baseline 75 → 48; registry baseline still 0; 297 workspace tests still green. Remaining residue is mostly genuine null-narrowing complexity (return value `T?` vs declared `T` after a null guard) and a handful of `cannot infer` cases — separate follow-ups.

- [x] **19.14 Inheritance + temporal arithmetic + deref + C-for typing** (M) — multi-bucket sweep against the closed-source corpus that drained the type-relation residue. (1) **Inheritance** — captured `extends` in `TypeMembers.supertype: Option<Symbol>` at `ingest` time. The grammar bug that made this take a moment to debug: the old grammar wrapped `seq("extends", $.type_ident)` in the `field("supertype", ...)` so `child_by_field_name("supertype")` returned the `"extends"` keyword, not the type ident — moved the field marker to wrap just the inner `type_ident`. Five new chain-walking accessors on `ProjectIndex` (`type_attr_id_chain`, `type_method_id_chain`, `type_attr_ty_chain`, `type_method_return_chain`, `is_subtype_of`) walk the supertype chain bounded at 32 hops. The analyzer's `resolve_member` falls through to the chain helpers when an in-module type lacks the requested attr / method (so PVInstallation's body resolves `this.timezone` through PVEntity); `foreign_member_type`, `method_return_for`, and `qualified_static_value_type`'s 3-segment chain consume the chain helpers too. New `is_assignable_to_with_index` wrapper (project.rs) extends the standard relation: `Named(Sub) → Named(Super)` and `Generic("node", [Sub]) → Generic("node", [Super])` when `Sub` extends `Super`. `Cx::Cast` now allows up- / down-cast within a supertype chain. (2) **Temporal arithmetic** — binary `+`/`-`/`*` overload table extended: `time + duration → time`, `time - time → duration`, `duration ± duration → duration`, `duration * (int|float) → duration`. Was falling through to `any` for every temporal op. (3) **Deref operator `*n`** — `UnaryOp::Deref` was missing entirely; lowering hit the catch-all `_ => Not` so `*pvEntity` typed as `bool` and downstream casts failed. New `UnaryOp::Deref` variant lowers `*` correctly; the analyzer's unary arm reuses `arrow_deref_receiver` so `*node<T>` returns `T`. (4) **C-style `for` loop var typing** — `ForStmt.init_name` was visited but never bound to `def_types`, so `for (var i = 0; i < n; i++) { ... }`'s loop var resolved as `any`. Now bound from the declared / inferred init type. (5) **Generic-param casts** — `T as Foo` (and `Foo as T`) accepted unconditionally in `is_castable`; the runtime decides at instantiation. **Acceptance:** corpus baseline 246 → 75 across these. 297 workspace tests still green; registry baseline still 0.

- [x] **19.13 Static-attr value access + binary `+` String concat** (S) — two stage-level typing gaps surfaced by re-running cli lint. (1) `Type::staticAttr` was always typing as `Named("field")` regardless of whether the attr was declared `static`. With static attrs the value should be the attr's declared type (`type Foo { static path: String = "..." }; Programs::python3` → `String`, not `field`). New `TypeMembers.static_attrs: HashSet<Symbol>` populated at `ingest` time from the attr's `modifiers.static_` flag — works for cross-module access too because the project index is the source of truth. `Cx::static_value_type` now takes `recv_ty` and consults `static_attrs`; `qualified_static_value_type`'s 3-segment chain does the same. (2) `BinOp::Add` only handled int+int / _+float, falling through to `any` for `String + X`. The runtime coerces the non-string side via `to_string()`, so `String + X` / `X + String` → `String`. Other arithmetic ops (`-`, `_`, `/`, `%`) keep their numeric-only semantics. **Acceptance:** `var TOKEN_PATH = data_location + "/tokens/";`typed as`String`now (was`any`); `Programs::python3`typed as`String`. The closed-source corpus dropped by ~30 cascading errors.

- [x] **19.11 Offset-expr element typing + `this`-typing** (S) — closes the remaining 12 registry-baseline diagnostics. (1) [`Expr::Offset`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/analyzer.rs) was minting `self.any()` regardless of receiver type with a "P16.7 — out of scope here" comment; element-type inference now matches the for-in handler's pattern: `Array<T>` / `Set<T>` / `nodeList<T>` indexing yields `T`, `Map<K, V>` / `nodeIndex<K, V>` indexing yields `V`, with `pre_optional` / `post_optional` markers folded in (`a?[i]` lifts to nullable when receiver is nullable; `a[i]?` lifts unconditionally). Strips the receiver's optional before matching so the binding logic stays the same with or without `?`. (2) `LiteralKind::This` was hardcoded to `self.any()` — `this.foo` member access on a method receiver lost its declared type, so `for (_, id in this.owners)` over `Array<int>` was binding `id: any`. New `this_stack: Vec<TypeId>` field on `Cx` (pushed in `visit_type_decl`, popped on exit). The pushed `this` TypeId is `Named { name }` for non-generic types and `Generic { name, args: [GenericParam(g0), GenericParam(g1), ...] }` for generic types — matches what an external `node<Foo<int>>` deref would see. **Acceptance:** registry baseline 12 → 0. 297 workspace tests still green.

- [x] **19.10 Cross-module var typing + canonical enum lowering** (M) — closes two staged-lowering gaps surfaced by re-running `cli lint` on the registry app (30 → 12 diagnostics). (1) `lower_module_signatures` was walking Type / Enum / Fn but skipping `Decl::Var`, so cross-module top-level vars had no entry in any project-wide signature index; the analyzer's `Definition::ProjectDecl` bare-Ident path then fell through to `index.has_name` (vars are in `values`) and typed them as `Named("type")`. New `ProjectIndex.var_types: HashMap<Symbol, TypeId>` lowered alongside the others (with `module_signature_hash` extended for the `Var` arm + `ModuleSigCache.vars` field + `apply_module_contributions` propagation), `ProjectIndex::var_type_for(name)` accessor, and the analyzer's bare-Ident path consults it before falling through. (2) Both `lower_type_ref` (analyzer.rs Cx) and `lower_type_ref_project` (project.rs orchestrator) were minting `Named(name)` for cross-module enum names, but `ProjectAnalysis::stage_lower_signatures` had already minted the canonical `TypeKind::Enum { name, variants }` into the shared arena and stashed the `TypeId` in `index.enum_types`. Both lowerers now consult `enum_types` _before_ `arena.named(name)` — matches the same staged-lowering principle as `var_types`. (3) `is_assignable_to`'s `Generic` arg invariance check (line 517) was raw `TypeId ==`, but the existing Named<->Enum identity at lines 565-566 only fires at the top level; for a containing `Map<Target, V>` lowered two ways (Enum from analyzer, Named from the validation pass's `mint_type_shape`), the args were unequal as `TypeId`s even though the relation says they're the same type. Switched to bidirectional `is_assignable_to`, which preserves invariance semantics (`Array<int>` ≠ `Array<float>` because `float → int` is asymmetric and rejects) but recovers the Enum/Named identity that already exists at the relation level. **Acceptance:** registry baseline drops 30 → 12 diagnostics; the user's local `var x = TimeZone::"Europe/Paris"` reproducer no longer surfaces a false-positive `any` typing. 296 workspace tests still green. Remaining 12 share a different root cause: `Stmt::OffsetExpr` (`parts[0]`) and `for-in` over `this.owners: Array<int>` both bind `any` instead of `T` — a separate stage gap (member access through `this`, indexing typing) tracked as a follow-up. Also queued: shape-detour removal in `collect_call_arg_diags_split` / `lower_type_ref_id` so the validation pass's lowerers consult `enum_types` directly instead of relying on the `is_assignable_to` Named<->Enum equivalence.

**M19:** registry parity baseline ≤ 5; `did_change` → `publish_diagnostics` round-trip < 50ms p99 on a 50-file synthetic project; `ProjectAnalysis::rebuild` walks bodies _once_ with fully-resolved types instead of patching `expr_types` across 5+ post-passes.

### Phase 20 — `pro` dogfood ratchet (~1 week)

**Goal:** drive analyzer false positives down on the new closed-source corpus at `datathings/greycat/pro` (225 modules across `lib/std`, `lib/algebra`, `lib/text_search`, `lib/ifc`, `lib/openid`, `lib/fcs`, `lib/ai`, `lib/finance`, `lib/powergrid`, `lib/powerflow`, etc.). Baseline at phase start: 154 diagnostics; ~80 are analyzer FPs concentrated in three categories. The remaining ~74 are genuine TPs (~33 unused locals/parameters, 4 inferred-return-type hints, ~26 redundant `!!` on locals, plus a few unused-private-fn / non-exhaustive-on-real-chain cases) and stay flagged.

**Chunks:**

- [x] **20.1 `any` source assignable to typed parameters / inits / returns** (S) — the GreyCat compiler accepts `any → T` (with a runtime type check at call-site / assignment-site) for any non-Any `T`. Confirmed against `greycat run` 8.0.269-dev: `var a: any = 1; take(a);` against `take(_: int)` compiles AND runs successfully; only `var a: any = "x"; take(a);` against `take(_: int)` fails — and the failure is an `Error` raised dynamically at the call frame, not a compile-time rejection. Our `is_assignable_to` (in [`greycat-analyzer-types`](../greycat-analyzer-types/src/lib.rs)) was rejecting `Any → T` at compile time (the prior `rt_any_to_int_rejected` probe conflated runtime-dynamic-dispatch failures with compile-time assignability), so call-sites that pass `any` values (canonically: `Array<any>[i]` from an `["a", "b"]` literal — literals infer as `Array<any>`) surfaced as static errors. Fix: added an `Any` source rule in `is_assignable_to` mirroring the existing `Any` destination rule — `any` is _both_ top and bottom in the GreyCat lattice. Updated `rt_any_to_int_rejected` → `rt_any_to_int_allowed` with a comment explaining the prior conflation, retired the stale `lambda_contravariant_params_covariant_return` test (the relation is no longer asymmetric through `any`) for two cleaner replacements (`lambda_with_any_slot_is_symmetric` + `lambda_arity_mismatch_rejected`). **Acceptance:** the 13 `any → T` errors across `datathings/greycat/pro/ifc/test/ifc_test.gcl` (12 cases on `IfcBoolAttr.value` / `IfcFloatAttr.value` paths) and `datathings/greycat/pro/text_search/test/pipeline/stemmer_edge_cases_test.gcl` (1 case on `Array<any>[i]` from a literal) all clear. 318 workspace tests still green; corpus baseline 154 → 141.

- [x] **20.2 Member-path narrowing through `!!` postfix** (S) — `Cx::infer_expr`'s `UnaryOp::NonNullAssert` arm currently writes a non-null narrow only when the operand is an `Expr::Ident` resolving to a `Param` / `Local`. For Member / Arrow operands (e.g. `meta.channels!!.size()` then `meta.channels[0]`, or `features_gaussian.min!!` then `features_gaussian.min.size()`), the second access falls back to the field's declared nullable type and re-fires the diagnostic the user _just_ assured the analyzer they handled. Extend the arm to mirror the ident case: when the operand resolves to a stable member-path (`Cx::member_path(operand)` returns `Some(path)`), call `write_member_non_null(path)` so subsequent reads of the same path strip the nullable bit at the bottom of the `Expr::Member` / `Expr::Arrow` arm (the existing P19.16 strip-narrow site). The narrow correctly drops on assignment to the path (the existing `record_assign_narrow` clears it when the RHS is nullable). **Acceptance:** the ~30 FPs across `datathings/greycat/pro/lib/algebra/kmeans.gcl:282/330/377/424` (4 errors on `features_gaussian.min`), `datathings/greycat/pro/lib/algebra/patterns.gcl:1123` (1 error on `this.window_frequency`), `datathings/greycat/pro/fcs/test/fcs_test.gcl` (10 warnings on `meta.channels`), `datathings/greycat/pro/text_search/test/index/compact_posting_test.gcl` (8 warnings on `term.posting*` and `index.normalizedTerms`), `datathings/greycat/pro/text_search/test/pipeline/{boolean,span}_parser_test.gcl` (8 warnings on `q.right` / `q.children` / `qq.left`), and `datathings/greycat/pro/text_search/test/ranking/fusion_dedup_test.gcl:90` (1 error + 1 warning on `acc.termLookup`) all clear. New unit test in [`analyzer.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/analyzer.rs) anchors the new behavior (member path `!!` narrows subsequent reads) and a sibling test confirms the narrow drops after a maybe-null reassignment.

- [x] **20.3 Tighten enum exhaustiveness to chained `if-else if`** (S) — `Cx::check_enum_exhaustiveness` (P6.6) currently fires on _any_ `if (x == E::V)` that doesn't have a final `else`, regardless of whether the if is part of a real `else if` dispatch chain. The `extract_enum_chain` walker exits with a 1-arm `EnumChain` for a lone `if`, so the diagnostic surfaces "missing: <every other variant>" on code patterns the runtime compiler is fine with — `if (mode == SearchMode::bm25) { ... return ...; } if (mode == SearchMode::exact) { ... return ...; } ...` (separate non-`else if` statements with their own returns). The 23 FPs on `text_index.gcl` and 6 on `ranking_rules.gcl` are exactly this. Fix: in `check_enum_exhaustiveness`, return early when `chain.arms.len() < 2` (no `else if` continuation = not a chain). Chained `if-else if` checks remain as-is. **Acceptance:** the 23 FPs on `datathings/greycat/pro/lib/text_search/model/text_index.gcl` and 6 FPs on `datathings/greycat/pro/lib/text_search/scoring/ranking_rules.gcl` clear. The two existing tests in `analyzer.rs` (`non_exhaustive_enum_chain_warns`, `exhaustive_enum_chain_silent`) continue to pass — both use ≥ 2-arm chains. New unit test confirms a lone `if (x == E::V)` is silent.

**M20:** `cargo run -p greycat-analyzer -- lint project.gcl` against `datathings/greycat/pro` reports ≤ 80 diagnostics (down from 154), all genuine TPs. The 296+ workspace tests stay green. **Met:** 154 → 77 (P20.1: 13, P20.2: 35, P20.3: 29); 322 workspace tests green.

---

### Phase 21 — Formatter rewrite: Doc IR + width-aware renderer (~2-4 weeks)

**Goal:** retire the single-pass token-rule walker in [`greycat-analyzer-fmt/src/lib.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-fmt/src/lib.rs) (506 LoC of imperative state) and replace it with a Wadler/Leijen-style pretty printer — three small, testable layers: **Doc IR**, **CST → Doc lowering**, **Doc → text renderer**. The current walker has no concept of line width and can't reflow long generics / args / object literals; that's why the parity gauntlet has been stuck at **4/8 byte-for-byte, 6/8 idempotent** since P14.3 and the M9 / M5 acceptance criterion is still open.

**Why a rewrite, not more rules.** The remaining 4 failing fixtures (`args_split`, `nested_args_split`, `if_var_object`, `stmts_rules`) all need _line-width-aware_ decisions: the formatter must lay out a candidate inline, _measure_ the resulting column position, and break-and-indent if it overshoots. Bolting that onto the per-token state machine means tracking a hypothetical column width through every `emit_token` call and a way to "rewind and try again" — that's an interpreter for a Doc IR with extra steps. Porting `cst_format.ts` literally (1,354 LoC across `cst_format.ts` + `cst_rules.ts`) is also out — that design's `Group` / `Rule.kind` mutation is hard to reason about and slower than necessary. A clean Wadler/Leijen IR (Text / Line / Soft / Hard / Indent / Concat / Group + comment-attach) is _less_ code than either approach and is the standard solution.

**Design — borrowed from prettier, scoped to GreyCat.** Three files in [`greycat-analyzer-fmt/src/`](../greycat-analyzer-fmt/src/):

- **`doc.rs`** — the IR. A small `Doc` enum: `Nil`, `Text(Cow<'a, str>)`, `Line { space_if_flat: bool }`, `Hard`, `Indent(Box<Doc>)`, `Concat(Vec<Doc>)`, `Group(Box<Doc>)`, plus `BlankLine` (preserve user blanks) and `Trailing(Box<Doc>)` for the trailing-comma-before-`)` shape. Constructor helpers (`text`, `concat`, `group`, `indent`, `line`, `softline`, `hardline`, `space`) keep call sites readable.
- **`render.rs`** — the printer. Standard "fits-flat" measurement: for each `Group`, compute the unbroken width with the remaining line-width budget; if it fits, emit flat (Line→space, Soft→nothing); otherwise break (Line→newline+indent, Soft→newline+indent). Recursive groups inherit the parent's break decision _only_ when they don't fit on their own. Stack-allocated, no rule-kind mutation, ~150 LoC including comment handling.
- **`lower.rs`** — CST → Doc visitor. One function per construct. Trivia (comments + blank-line counts) attaches via a small `TriviaPicker` helper that consumes the source between two tokens and yields the doc-level shape (inline `// ...`, leading doc-comment block, blank-line separator, etc.). Tree-sitter's `TreeCursor` supplies the structure.

The TS reference's per-construct _intent_ is preserved (e.g. `args_spaced` ↔ `args_multiline` becomes a `Group` containing comma-separated args with `Line` between each; the renderer picks flat vs. broken once via the fits-flat measurement). What gets dropped: the Rule-class hierarchy, the `kind` mutation, the `LineWriter` post-processing.

**Pragma options.** Mirror the TS reference: `@format_line_width(N)` (default 120), `@format_indent(N)` (default 4), `@format_eol_last(bool)` (default true; the TS default is false but real-world files have a trailing newline and the playground / LSP path preserves it). Parsed from the input's `mod_pragma` chain in `format()` before lowering.

**Public API — unchanged.** `pub fn format(source: &str) -> String` and `pub fn format_tree(source: &str, root: Node<'_>) -> String` keep their signatures so the four call sites ([`cmd/fmt.rs`](../greycat-analyzer/src/cmd/fmt.rs), [`capabilities.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-server/src/capabilities.rs) for full + range formatting, [`wasm/src/lib.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-wasm/src/lib.rs)) need no changes. New `format_with(source, FmtOptions)` exposes the pragma options for callers that override.

**Chunks (one commit per chunk):**

- [x] **21.1 Doc IR + width-aware renderer** (M) — `doc.rs` defines `Doc` + constructor helpers. `render.rs` implements the fits-flat printer with the standard Wadler/Leijen algorithm: a `fits(doc, remaining_width)` measurement walks the doc treating Lines as spaces and Hards as overflow-failures; on overflow, the enclosing Group is broken and Lines become newline+indent. Hard breaks always break and reset the column.
