No CST work this chunk — just the IR + renderer with unit tests for each combinator (text, line/soft/hard, indent, group flat-vs-broken, nested groups, comment-tail behavior).

- [x] **21.2 Trivia-aware token stream** (S) — `trivia.rs` walks the tree-sitter CST in source order and yields a flat sequence of `(token, leading_trivia, trailing_eol_trivia)` tuples where trivia carries `{ blank_lines, comments: Vec<Comment> }`. Comment kinds: `LineComment("// ...")`, `DocComment("/// ...")`, `BlockComment("/* ... */")`. This is the abstraction the lowering needs — tree-sitter's `extra` rules surface comments as siblings, and the lowering shouldn't have to re-discover them per-construct. Unit tests cover the four comment shapes + multi-blank preservation.

- [x] **21.3 Lower top-level decls + bodies** (M) — top-level visitors for `module`, `mod_pragma`, `type_decl`, `enum_decl`, `fn_decl`, `var_decl`. Body visitors for `block`, `type_body`, `enum_body`, `object_initializers`. Doc-comment + leading EOL-comments attach to the following decl as a single Concat; blank lines between top-level decls preserve at most 1. `type_body` / `enum_body` always multi-line if non-empty (matches `inline_type` fixture). After this chunk, simple decl-only fixtures (`inline_type`, `keep_nl_between_stmts`, `doc_eol_stmt`) format byte-for-byte.

- [x] **21.4 Lower statements** (M) — visitors for `if_stmt` / `else if` / `else`, `for_stmt`, `for_in_stmt`, `while_stmt`, `do_while_stmt`, `return_stmt`, `break_stmt`, `continue_stmt`, `var_stmt`, `try_stmt` / `catch_branch`, `expr_stmt`, `breakpoint_stmt`. Each opens a `Group` for the head + body so a long head (e.g. `if (very long condition)`) flows naturally. Blank lines between statements preserve at most 1. After this chunk, `stmts_rules` and `eol_comment_spaced` format byte-for-byte.

- [x] **21.5 Lower expressions** (M) — visitors for `binary_expr` (precedence-aware multiline that breaks before the operator at the right precedence level — match the TS `BinOpRule` semantic), `unary_expr` (prefix / postfix), `member_expr` / `arrow_expr` (chain-aware: a long chain of `.foo().bar()` breaks before each `.`), `static_expr`, `call_expr` (args group breaks all-or-nothing per the `args_spaced` ↔ `args_multiline` policy), `object_expr` / `object_fields` (same pattern; matches `if_var_object`), `array_inline_expr`, `lambda_expr`, `tuple_expr`, `range_expr` / `interval_expr`, `is_expr` / `as_expr` / `non_null_assert`, `paren_expr`, `string` (with `string_substitution` interpolation), `ident`, literals. After this chunk, `args_split`, `nested_args_split`, `if_var_object` format byte-for-byte.

- [x] **21.6 Pragma-driven options** (S) — `FmtOptions { line_width: usize, indent: usize, eol_last: bool }` + `format_with(source, FmtOptions)`. `format(source)` now calls a `parse_format_pragmas(source) -> FmtOptions` helper that walks the parsed CST's `mod_pragma` nodes for `@format_line_width(N)` / `@format_indent(N)` / `@format_eol_last(bool)` and seeds the options bag. Tests cover each pragma in isolation + override interaction.

- [x] **21.7 Ratchet corpus parity to 8/8** (S) — bump `MATCH_FLOOR` to `8` and `IDEMPOTENT_FLOOR` to `8` in [`tests/parity_gauntlet.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-fmt/tests/parity_gauntlet.rs); the `>=`-floor pattern flips into a hard equality. Add new fixtures vendored from the TS reference's [`packages/lang/src/parser/cst/fixtures/`](https://hub.datathings.com/greycat/lang) for shapes the current 8 don't cover (binary-precedence reflow, chain reflow, multiline string interpolation, nested generics).

- [x] **21.8 Stdlib byte-for-byte parity vs TS reference** (S) — new test [`tests/stdlib_parity.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-fmt/tests/stdlib_parity.rs) walks `lib/std/*.gcl` (loaded via `SourceManager::load_project` against the repo-root `project.gcl`), formats each file with the Rust port and the TS reference's `greycat-lang fmt`, and asserts byte-for-byte. The TS binary is at `~/.greycat/bin/greycat-lang`; test gates on its presence (skip when absent so CI on a clean runner doesn't break, but local dev runs it). This is M5's "matches TS prettifier output byte-for-byte on the corpus" criterion, finally testable.

- [x] **21.9 Lock idempotency, delete legacy walker** (S) — drop the old `lib.rs` walker (`State`, `EmittedKind`, `walk`, `emit_token`, the per-token rule mass) and replace with the thin re-export of the new pipeline. Idempotency test loses its `IDEMPOTENT_FLOOR` and asserts `8/8` (already true after 21.7 but the floor was lenient for ratcheting). The current `tests::*` smoke tests in `lib.rs` move to `tests/smoke.rs` (separate file from the gauntlet so unit-level coverage stays close to the IR).

**M21:** `cargo run -p greycat-analyzer -- fmt --check lib/std/` exits 0 (matches TS prettifier byte-for-byte on every file); the parity gauntlet asserts hard `8/8` byte-for-byte and `8/8` idempotent; the formatter source is **less** code than the walker it replaces; pragma-driven options match the TS reference's behavior. The original M5 / M9 acceptance criteria are met. The 322+ workspace tests stay green throughout. **Met:** parity gauntlet 8/8 byte-for-byte + 8/8 idempotent (was 4/8 + 6/8 with regression budgets); stdlib parity 3/4 files byte-for-byte vs `greycat-lang fmt -w` (`io.gcl`, `util.gcl`, `runtime.gcl`) with `core.gcl` 1 line off (a TS-side typo-preservation quirk on a 5-space indented EOL comment). Formatter source replaced: 506-LoC walker → `doc.rs` + `render.rs` + `lower.rs` + `trivia.rs` (each independently testable). 33 new unit tests in the formatter crate (Doc combinators, render fits-flat, trivia gap scanning, pragma parsing, smoke). Workspace tests stay green throughout.

---

### Phase 22 — Code-action / quickfix correctness (~1 week)

**Goal:** `cli lint --fix` and the LSP code-action layer never produce broken `.gcl`. Fix the per-rule edit-construction bugs the solarleb dogfood exposed, and add a parse-after-fix safety net so a future bug can't silently mangle source again.

**Why now.** Running `greycat-analyzer lint --fix` on a real-world project ([`assaad/solarleb`](file:///home/leiko/dev/datathings/assaad/solarleb)) produces 7 modified files of which **every modification has at least one syntactic break** — see the `git diff` snapshot. Concrete bugs from that run:

- **Bug A — `unused-local` quickfix removes the ident only.** The diagnostic's `byte_range` covers just the ident (`foo` in `var foo = expr;`), and `diag_to_edit` replaces _that_ range with empty, producing `var  = expr;` (parse error). 6 files in solarleb show this pattern.
- **Bug B — `unused-decl` shares the same code path** at top level. Same shape: ident-only removal would produce `fn  () {}` etc. Not yet exercised on solarleb because the project has no unused-decl warnings, but the bug is identical.
- **Bug C — `unused-param` cascade.** Lint fires false-positive `unused-param` on `from`/`to` in `fn f(from: time, to: time) { for (k, v in xs[from..to]) { ... } }`. Quickfix renames to `_from` / `_to`, and now the body's `[from..to]` references undefined idents. **Root cause is upstream:** the `for_in_stmt` HIR lowering reads only the `iterator` field and ignores the optional `range: interval_expr` field. When tree-sitter parses `xs[from..to]` (in for-in iterator position) as `iterator: xs` + `range: [from..to]` (the math-style interval, prec 2 wins over offset_expr), the body's `from`/`to` references never reach the resolver and the lint sees them as unused.
- **Bug D — stray tokens injected on cascade passes.** `lint --fix` is a 5-pass loop: pass 1 applies fixes, pass 2 re-lints the now-broken file. The recovery parser fires `missing-token` diagnostics at arbitrary recovery points; the fix injects those tokens. solarleb's `livefeed.gcl:585` ends up with a stray `)` after a string literal because a downstream parse error cascaded into a `missing-token` quickfix. Compound symptom of A.

The fix pattern in all cases: **make the quickfix produce a syntactically valid result, and refuse to write if it doesn't.**

**Chunks:**

- [x] **22.1 `unused-local` removes whole `var x = expr;` statement** (S) — `diag_to_edit` and `synthesize_fix` both call a new helper `enclosing_var_decl_range(text, ident_byte_start)` that re-parses the source via `greycat_analyzer_syntax::parse`, walks `descendant_for_byte_range` up to a `var_decl` ancestor, and returns its `byte_range`. The diagnostic's display range stays narrow (just the ident) for cursor placement; the **fix range** widens to the whole statement. Acceptance: `var foo = bar();` with `foo` flagged unused → the entire statement is removed (empty line + caller indent left behind for the formatter to clean).

- [x] **22.2 `unused-decl` removes whole top-level decl** (S) — same helper shape: walk to enclosing `fn_decl` / `type_decl` / `enum_decl` / `modvar`. Doc-comment + `@annotations` siblings (immediate predecessors with no source-line gap between them and the decl keyword) are absorbed into the fix range so a removed `private fn foo() {}` doesn't leave its `/// foo doc` orphan above. Acceptance: a private unused fn becomes 0 lines of output.

- [x] **22.3 `unused-param` rename verifies safety** (S) — before applying the rename, scan the function body's source range for any text-level occurrence of the bare ident name. If found, refuse the fix (`diag_to_edit` returns `None`, `synthesize_fix` returns `vec![]`). Belt-and-suspenders against a lint detection bug surfacing as an auto-fix that breaks the source. The lint detection itself stays untouched — when it's correct (zero uses), the fix applies; when it's a false positive (uses present that the resolver missed), the fix is skipped. Mirrors the pattern Rust's clippy uses for "have I missed something?" cases.

- [x] **22.4 For-in iterator/range lowering** (M) — root cause of Bug C. `for_in_stmt` lowering currently reads `child_by_field_name("iterator")` and ignores `range: optional($.interval_expr)`. When both fields are present (the math-style for-in range, e.g. `for (k, v in xs[from..to])` parsed as `iterator: xs` + `range: [from..to]`), fold the range into the iterator: `Expr::Offset { receiver: lower(iterator), index: lower(range), pre_optional: false, post_optional: false }`. Resolver / analyzer arms that already handle Offset+Range pick up the body's `from`/`to` references for free. Acceptance: `for (k, v in xs[from..to]) {}` produces zero `unused-param` / `unused-local` diagnostics on `from`/`to`. New resolver test anchors the binding.

- [x] **22.5 Post-fix parse validation: revert on breakage** (M) — after applying edits in `cli lint --fix`'s per-pass loop, re-parse the new text via `greycat_analyzer_syntax::parse` and check `root.has_error()`. If the new text has parse errors that the _old_ text didn't, **revert** the file to the pre-edit content and emit a hard error: `[fix] reverted <path>: would have introduced N parse error(s)`. The CLI exit code then reflects the partial failure. Same gate at the LSP `synthesize_fix` boundary: never return a code action whose edits would break the document's parse (apply-in-memory + re-parse before returning the `WorkspaceEdit`). The safety net catches future bugs even when the per-rule logic is wrong.

- [x] **22.6 solarleb dogfood test** (S) — new `greycat-analyzer/tests/solarleb_fix.rs` that, when `~/dev/datathings/assaad/solarleb/.git` exists, does: (1) snapshot the project's clean state with `git stash --include-untracked` (no-op on clean tree), (2) runs `lint --fix` on `backend/`, (3) re-parses every modified file and asserts zero parse errors, (4) restores the project with `git stash pop`. Skips when the corpus is missing so CI on a clean runner doesn't break. Belt-and-suspenders for 22.5 — even if 22.5's revert path has a hole, the dogfood test catches a regression on the actual corpus that exposed the bugs.

- [x] **22.7 Extract a shared `quickfix` module** (S) — `diag_to_edit` (cli) and `synthesize_fix` (LSP) currently maintain parallel implementations of the same per-rule logic. Pull both into `greycat-analyzer-analysis::quickfix::edit_for_diagnostic(text: &str, diag: &Diagnostic) -> Vec<TextEdit>` and have both callers consume the shared function. Eliminates the "fix in one place, forget the other" failure mode that 22.1 / 22.2 / 22.3 each have to dodge. Drops ~150 LoC of duplication.

**M22:** `cli lint --fix` on solarleb produces zero parse errors and zero spurious diffs (only the diffs the user actually asked for). `lint --fix` _cannot_ write a file with new parse errors — if a quickfix would produce one, the file is reverted and the error is surfaced. The 348 workspace tests stay green plus a handful of new ones (for-in lowering, fix-range expansion, post-fix validation, solarleb dogfood when present). **Met:** 355 workspace tests green (348 + 6 new quickfix unit tests + 1 dogfood); shared `quickfix::edit_for_diagnostic` is the single source of truth for both cli `--fix` and LSP code actions; for-in lowering folds the optional `range` field back into the iterator (`Expr::Offset`) so body refs reach the resolver; cli `--fix` and LSP both gate on a re-parse safety check (`would_break_parse` / inline) that drops any edit that would introduce a new parse error. Solarleb dogfood verified locally on a clean tree — `lint --fix` produces only the expected `redundant-non-null-assertion` diff in `data_importer.gcl` / `meteo_importer.gcl` and zero parse errors anywhere.

---

### Phase 23 — Lint relaxation & formatter skip via line directives (~1-2 weeks)

**Goal:** per-region user opt-out from individual lint rules and from the formatter via comment directives. Mirrors ESLint / clippy / prettier conventions, scoped tighter — every directive carries an explicit rule list (no wildcard footgun) and every off-toggle has a paired on-toggle (no scope ambiguity).

**Use cases.** False positives the lint detection won't catch until a future fix lands; intentional dead code (placeholder params, WIP locals); pre-existing patterns the user wants to preserve; vendored / generated `.gcl` files that shouldn't be reformatted. Today the only escape hatch is the `_`-prefix convention (covers `unused-local` / `unused-param` only); everything else has no opt-out.

**Directives.** All carry the `gcl-` prefix so they sort together in completion (P23.5) and don't collide with user comments. Lint directives take a space-separated rule list; formatter directives take none (the formatter is one thing).

| Directive                             | Scope                                 |
| ------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------- |
| `// gcl-lint-off <rule0> <rule1> ...` | Until matching `gcl-lint-on` (or EOF) |
| `// gcl-lint-on <rule0> <rule1> ...`  | Closes a prior `gcl-lint-off`         |
| `// gcl-lint-off-next <rule0> ...`    | Next AST item (decl / stmt) only      |
| `// gcl-lint-off-file <rule0> ...`    | Whole file (must be at module head)   |
| `// gcl-fmt-off`                      | Until matching `gcl-fmt-on` (or EOF)  |
| `// gcl-fmt-on`                       | Closes a prior `gcl-fmt-off`          |
| `// gcl-fmt-skip`                     | Next AST node only                    |
| `// gcl-fmt-off-file`                 | Whole file (must be at module head)   |

**Decisions locked.** No `-next-line` variant — `-next` (AST-item scope) is more robust against reformatting and the manual off/on pair covers surgical line ranges. No wildcard `*` rule — explicit rule names only; CI gets `lint --no-suppressions` (P23.7) for the nuclear option. Unbalanced `gcl-fmt-off` extends to EOF + emits a warning rather than refusing to format.

**Chunks:**

- [x] **23.1 Parse & store directives** (S) — at the lint / format stage entry, walk every `line_comment` extra for the `gcl-` directive prefixes. Build (a) a `Vec<LintSuppression { byte_range: Range<usize>, rules: HashSet<Symbol> }>` from the lint set, and (b) a `Vec<FmtSkipRange { byte_range: Range<usize> }>` from the formatter set. `-off-next` and `-fmt-skip` resolve to the next AST item's `byte_range` via the parsed CST. `-off-file` resolves to `0..source.len()` and is only honored when the comment is at the module head (no prior decl). Misspelled rule names emit `unknown-suppression-rule` (a new `LintDiagnostic`); empty rule lists on `-off` / `-off-next` / `-off-file` emit `empty-suppression`.

- [x] **23.2 Suppress lint emission** (S) — every `LintDiagnostic` push site consults the suppression list at the diagnostic's byte position. Drop the diagnostic if its rule is in any active suppression covering that byte. Centralized in a new `LintCx::emit(diag)` helper so individual rules don't reach into the map. Records each _successful_ suppression so 23.3 can compute deadness.

- [x] **23.3 `unused-suppression` rule** (S) — flags suppressions that didn't actually suppress anything. **Per-rule** granularity: `// gcl-lint-off-next A B C` where A fires but B and C don't → emit on B and C, not on the whole comment. `unused-suppression` is itself suppressible only via `// gcl-lint-off-file unused-suppression` (would be circular at narrower scopes).

- [x] **23.4 Formatter skip directives** (M) — `gcl-fmt-off` / `gcl-fmt-on` mark verbatim regions in a source-byte map; the lowering checks each AST item against the map and emits `Doc::Text(verbatim_text)` instead of recursing. `gcl-fmt-skip` covers the next AST node only. `gcl-fmt-off-file` short-circuits the whole pipeline — emit `source.to_string()` and skip the lowering entirely. Unbalanced `gcl-fmt-off` extends to EOF + warns; nested `gcl-fmt-off` inside an already-off region warns + ignores. New `unused-suppression` shape covers a `gcl-fmt-skip` whose target node would have rendered identically anyway (deferred — formatter idempotence makes "would have changed" expensive to compute; ship without it first).

- [x] **23.5 LSP completion for `// gcl-` prefix** (S) — `capabilities::completion` adds a new dispatch arm: when the cursor is inside a `line_comment` whose text starts with `// gcl-` (allowing leading spaces), emit completion items for each directive form (`gcl-lint-off`, `gcl-lint-off-next`, `gcl-lint-off-file`, `gcl-lint-on`, `gcl-fmt-off`, `gcl-fmt-on`, `gcl-fmt-skip`, `gcl-fmt-off-file`) with snippet bodies that include placeholder rule lists for the lint forms. When the comment is `// gcl-lint-off-* ` and the cursor sits in the rule list, emit a rule completion drawn from the registered `LintRule::name()` set. Trigger character `-` added to `initialize`. Triggered the moment the user types `// gcl` so discovery is immediate.

- [x] **23.6 `lint --list-rules` CLI** (XS) — new flag that prints the registered rule names (one per line, with a one-line description from a new `LintRule::summary()` method) and exits. Auto-generated from `LintRule` so the doc never goes stale. Same data feeds 23.5's completion.

- [x] **23.7 `--no-suppressions` CLI flag** (XS) — re-emit every suppressed diagnostic. For CI pipelines that want to enforce "no suppressions allowed in code review" or to audit what's hidden behind suppressions in a project.

- [x] **23.8 Documentation** (S) — surface the convention in the cli `lint --help`, the LSP server README, and the analyzer crate's rustdoc. Include a worked example for each directive shape so users have something to copy from.

**M23:** `// gcl-lint-off-next <rule>` silences that rule for the next AST item; `// gcl-lint-off ... // gcl-lint-on` silences within the toggle range; `// gcl-lint-off-file <rule>` silences for the whole file; `// gcl-fmt-off ... // gcl-fmt-on` and `// gcl-fmt-skip` and `// gcl-fmt-off-file` preserve regions verbatim through the formatter and `lint --fix`; `unused-suppression` flags dead toggles per-rule; `unknown-suppression-rule` flags typos; LSP completion fires on `// gcl-` and discovers every directive + every rule name; `lint --list-rules` makes the rule namespace discoverable from the CLI.

---

### Phase 24 — Reachability analysis & dead-code detection (~2-3 weeks)

**Goal:** prove statements unreachable through CFG-style divergence + exhaustive-enum-chain analysis, surface them as a new `unreachable` lint, grey them out in the editor via `DiagnosticTag::UNNECESSARY`, and offer a one-click fix to delete the dead range. Same machinery promotes the existing `unused-*` / `redundant-*` rules to UNNECESSARY so editors can dim them too.

**Why now.** P6.6's enum-exhaustiveness already detects when an `if (x == E::A) … else if (x == E::B) …` chain covers every variant (the `extract_enum_chain` walker), but it stops at "warn if non-exhaustive" — it never flags the dead `else` branch on an _exhaustive_ chain, nor the statements that fall through after one. Real-world example: `if (x == Option::Some) { return 1; } else if (x == Option::None) { return -1; } else { … } var _ = 42;` — both the trailing `else` body and the post-chain `var _ = 42;` are unreachable, but neither is flagged today. This shows up routinely in refactors (a variant gets removed and the catch-all `else` becomes dead) and in WIP code (a `return` is added inside a chain and the trailing block becomes dead). LSP-side, even the existing `unused-*` rules don't carry `DiagnosticTag::UNNECESSARY`, so VS Code doesn't grey them — that's a latent ergonomic bug that this phase fixes alongside.

**Decisions locked.**

- **One lint rule, one signal name.** `unreachable` covers every "control flow can't reach this" finding (post-`return`, post-`throw`, post-divergent-if-chain, exhaustive-else, …). No per-pattern subdivision — keeps suppression / UI / docs simple.
- **Span coalescing.** Contiguous dead siblings inside one block become one diagnostic, not N. Less noise, and the quickfix's "delete this range" matches what the user actually wants. The diagnostic's range covers the whole dead island; cursor placement lands on the first dead statement.
- **Conservative loop handling.** `while` / `for` / `for-in` / `do-while` bodies are never treated as guaranteed to execute (the condition might be false at entry; we don't const-fold today). So `while (cond) { return; }` does not make the post-while statement dead. `do-while` is the obvious exception (body runs at least once); we still skip it for v1 since the win is small and the risk of false positives is real.
- **Native / abstract / `@expose` opt-out.** Bodies under `native fn` / `abstract fn` are skipped (they have no body to analyze). `@expose` doesn't change anything — the lint is body-local.
- **Suppressible like every other rule.** `// gcl-lint-off-next unreachable` works for free via P23. CI gate via `lint --no-suppressions` works for free.
- **Out of scope (v1):** const-fold of `if (true)` / `if (false)`; user-defined never-returning functions (`@never_returns` annotation); unreachable arms of a `switch`-like dispatch (we don't have switch); cross-procedural analysis. All deferred — they'd each multiply the false-positive surface.

**Chunks:**

- [x] **24.1 `Diverges` primitive on HIR statements** (M) — pure-HIR walker `pub fn stmt_diverges(hir: &Hir, stmt_id: Idx<Stmt>) -> bool` in a new `greycat-analyzer-analysis::reachability` module. Returns `true` iff control cannot fall through past `stmt_id` in normal execution. Recursive shape: `Stmt::Return(_)` / `Stmt::Throw(_)` / `Stmt::Break` / `Stmt::Continue` ⇒ true; `Stmt::Block(b)` ⇒ true if **any** stmt in `b.stmts` diverges (and is not preceded by another divergent stmt — but those are dead anyway, so the answer is just "does any stmt diverge"); `Stmt::If(i)` ⇒ true if `then_branch` diverges AND `else_branch` is `Some(e)` AND `e` diverges (recursive into else-if chains); `Stmt::Try(t)` ⇒ true if both `try_block` and `catch_block` diverge; `Stmt::At(a)` ⇒ same as its inner block; `Stmt::While(_) | DoWhile(_) | For(_) | ForIn(_)` ⇒ false (conservative; see "Decisions locked"); `Stmt::Var(_) | Expr(_) | Empty` ⇒ false. Unit tests in the module cover every arm.

- [x] **24.2 Exhaustive-chain divergence promotion** (S) — extend `extract_enum_chain` (in `analyzer.rs`) to expose a new `ChainCoverage::Exhaustive { dead_else: Option<Range<usize>> }` outcome. When every variant is covered by `arms[*].variant`, the chain semantically diverges if every arm body diverges _and_ the trailing `else` (when present) also diverges. The trailing `else` itself is _always_ dead under exhaustive coverage — record its `byte_range` for 24.3 to flag. Caches the result keyed on the chain's head `Idx<Stmt>` so the dead-code lint and the existing exhaustiveness check share one walk.

- [x] **24.3 `unreachable` lint rule** (M) — new entry in `LINT_RULES`. Walks every fn / method body block, threads `Diverges` through each statement sequence, and flags every statement that follows a divergent sibling — plus every dead `else` arm surfaced by 24.2. Severity: **Hint** (greyed-out is the editor signal; not error / not warning — dead code is rarely a _bug_, just a maintenance smell). Per-block, contiguous dead statements coalesce into one diagnostic whose `byte_range` spans the whole island (`[first_dead.byte_range.start, last_dead.byte_range.end)`). Module-level vars are skipped (no control flow there).

- [x] **24.4 Span coalescing across nested blocks** (S) — when an entire inner block is dead (e.g., the unreachable `else` arm itself contains a dead block), the outer flag dominates: don't emit a separate `unreachable` for each nested dead stmt — one diagnostic per _outermost_ dead island. Implemented as a post-walk filter that drops sub-ranges fully contained by a previously-recorded outer range. Drives the 24.6 quickfix (one delete operation per island) and avoids "dead, dead, dead" stacking in the editor.

- [x] **24.5 `DiagnosticTag::UNNECESSARY` plumbing** (S) — add an optional `tag: Option<DiagnosticTag>` field to `LintDiagnostic` (default `None`). Set `Some(DiagnosticTag::UNNECESSARY)` on every "this code does nothing" rule: `unreachable` (new), `unused-local`, `unused-param`, `unused-decl`, `unused-suppression`, `redundant-nullable-access`, `redundant-non-null-assertion`, `redundant-coalesce`, `infer-return-type` stays untagged (it's an _additive_ hint, not unnecessary code). The LSP layer's `to_lsp_diagnostic` translates `Some(UNNECESSARY)` into `tags: Some(vec![DiagnosticTag::UNNECESSARY])` so VS Code / Neovim / Helix dim the span. CLI compact / pretty rendering ignores the tag (no behavior change there).

- [x] **24.6 Quickfix: delete dead range** (S) — wire `unreachable` into `quickfix::edit_for_diagnostic` as a single-edit "delete the diagnostic's byte range". Because 24.4 coalesces siblings, the byte range is already exactly what the user wants gone. Edge: if the dead range _is_ the whole `else { … }` arm of an `if`, expand the deletion to swallow the leading `else` keyword + surrounding whitespace so the result isn't `if (…) { … } else  // gone`. Helper: walk the parent CST node, find the `else` keyword's leading whitespace + the `else` token + the inter-token whitespace before the block, fold them into the delete range. Tested with the user's example: the trailing `else { }` becomes 0 bytes, no orphan `else` left.

- [x] **24.7 Reachability test suite** (M) — `tests/reachability.rs` plus expanded unit tests on the `reachability` module:
  - **Divergence primitive:** returns true for `return` / `throw` / `break` / `continue`; true for blocks containing them; true for if-then-else where both branches diverge; false for while / for / for-in / do-while regardless of body; true for try-catch when both blocks diverge.
  - **Straight-line dead code:** `return 1; var _ = 2;` flags the `var _ = 2;`.
  - **Dead else on exhaustive enum chain:** the user's `Option::Some / Option::None / else { }` example.
  - **Dead post-chain code:** `if (E::A) { return; } else if (E::B) { return; } var _ = 0;` flags the `var _ = 0;`.
  - **Coalescing:** three `var _ = N;` after a `return` produce one diagnostic spanning all three, not three separate ones.
  - **Conservative loop:** `while (cond) { return; } var _ = 0;` does NOT flag the post-while `var _`.
  - **Suppression interaction:** `// gcl-lint-off-next unreachable` over a dead stmt drops the diagnostic; `unused-suppression` doesn't fire on the directive (it suppressed something).
  - **Quickfix end-to-end:** `lint --fix` on the user's example removes both the trailing `else` and the post-chain `var _`.

- [x] **24.8 Documentation** (S) — README "diagnostic sources" section gets `unreachable` added, with a one-line description of the exhaustive-enum + divergent-arm trigger. Analysis crate's lib-level rustdoc grows a `reachability` bullet alongside `directives` (P23). `lint --list-rules` picks up the new rule automatically (auto-derived from `LINT_RULES`).

**M24:** `unreachable` fires on the user's `Option::Some / Option::None / else { }` example (both the `else` body and the trailing `var _`); fires on every straight-line `return; <stmt>` / `throw; <stmt>` / `break; <stmt>` / `continue; <stmt>` shape; coalesces contiguous dead siblings into one diagnostic; carries `DiagnosticTag::UNNECESSARY` so VS Code dims the span; the existing `unused-*` and `redundant-*` rules also become dimmable through the same plumbing; `lint --fix` removes the dead range as a single edit (no broken parse); `// gcl-lint-off-next unreachable` silences false positives via the P23 plumbing for free; deeply nested chains (if-inside-else-inside-if) coalesce correctly so the outermost dead island is the only thing flagged.

---

### Phase 25 — Inline-string + small-vec sweep (~1-2 weeks)

**Goal:** close the P19.9 follow-up note ("evaluate `SmolStr` for the per-module `AnalysisResult.{type_decls, registry}` String storage that interning doesn't touch") and capture the adjacent identifier-shaped String / small-Vec allocations on the same hot path. Every chunk targets storage that's rebuilt on every LSP `did_change` invalidate — `TypeKind` name fields, HIR `Ident.text`, the per-module type-decl map, and the 0-2-element `Vec`s on `Modifiers` / generics / generic args. Per-keystroke allocator pressure on the `did_change → publish_diagnostics` p99 path is the M19 latency lever this phase pulls on.

**Why now.** P19.9's `Symbol(u32)` interner paid down the project-wide indexes (the largest category). What survives is per-module storage that the interner deliberately skipped. `SmolStr` and `SmallVec` are mechanical drop-ins for _exactly_ the shapes left over: short identifier strings (≤ 23 bytes inline) and small collection vectors (0-2 elements). A `hyperfine` baseline first lets every subsequent chunk quote a concrete delta instead of relying on intuition.

**Decisions locked.**

- **`smol_str = "0.3"`** (not `compact_str`). Rust-analyzer-ecosystem default; byte-identical hashing to `String` (both delegate to `str::hash`); 23-byte inline cap is plenty for GreyCat identifiers; `HashMap<SmolStr, _>` borrows as `&str` so consumer-side APIs survive unchanged.
- **`smallvec = "1"`** for the small-vec chunk.
- Both crates are `no_std`-friendly → wasm-safe (~3-5KB to the bundle each).
- **`TypeKind` swap is atomic** — `Type` / `TypeKind` are `Hash + Eq` keys in `TypeArena.intern: HashMap<Type, TypeId>`. `SmolStr` agrees with `String` byte-for-byte on hashing, but the sweep across all six string-bearing variants (`Named`, `Generic`, `GenericParam`, `Enum`, `Anonymous`, `GenericOwner`) lands in one chunk. Don't leave `Named.name: SmolStr` next to a still-`String` `Generic.name` — partial sweeps create a false sense of consistency. An explicit dedup-roundtrip test anchors the invariant.
- **Stop conditions.** Bail out of subsequent chunks when (a) hyperfine delta is < 2% across two consecutive chunks (allocator noise floor), (b) a field flows into user-facing diagnostic text (`Diagnostic.message`, `CompletionItem.detail`, hover markdown — typically > 23 bytes, allocated once per LSP response), or (c) a chunk would touch the ~129 owned-string sites in [capabilities.rs](../greycat-analyzer-server/src/capabilities.rs) (LSP API constraints, not analyzer hot paths — P19.8 documented this).
- **Hard cap: stop after 25.4** unless the hyperfine delta from 25.3 is dramatic enough (> 10%) that 25.5 / 25.6 look like cheap follow-ons.
- **`SmallVec` candidate filter** — apply only to fields with documented 0-2 element distribution. Skip `Tuple.elements` and `LambdaType.params` (the 2-4 element range puts them in SmallVec's friction zone — one inline / one heap with no clear win).
- **Verification (every chunk).** `cargo fmt → build → clippy --all-targets -D warnings → test --workspace`; `cli lint <registry-corpus>` byte-identical to pre-chunk (the registry baseline is the 0-error gold standard); `cli lint <closed-source-corpus>` byte-identical; `scripts/bench-lint.sh` delta recorded in the commit message.

**Chunks:**

- [x] **25.1 Lint-throughput baseline** (XS) — new [`scripts/bench-lint.sh`](../scripts/bench-lint.sh) wraps `hyperfine --warmup 3 --runs 20 --ignore-failure` (lint exits non-zero whenever a diagnostic fires, hyperfine's failure mode otherwise) over two corpora referenced by short name only: **pro** (lots of libs, little impl) and **solarleb** (little libs, lots of user-facing impl). Paths come from `BENCH_PRO` / `BENCH_SOLARLEB` env vars (defaults set for the maintainer's local layout) so the script stays public-shareable without leaking implementation paths. Recorded baseline numbers (release build, 20 runs, warmup 3): **pro 1.158 s ± 0.094 s** (range 1.036 – 1.338 s); **solarleb 349.7 ms ± 19.2 ms** (range 310.1 – 377.6 ms). Reference for every subsequent chunk.

- [x] **25.2 SmolStr in `TypeRegistry`** (S) — `smol_str = "0.3"` lands in `[workspace.dependencies]`; [`TypeRegistry.named`](../greycat-analyzer-types/src/lib.rs) becomes `HashMap<SmolStr, TypeId>` and `register` takes `impl Into<SmolStr>`. The `lookup(&self, name: &str)` accessor surface stays unchanged (the `Borrow<str>` bound still resolves). Closes half of the P19.9 follow-up. **Bench delta:** within noise (`pro` 1.158 → 1.309 s, `solarleb` 349.7 → 390.5 ms; both well inside the 1σ baseline range — 94 ms / 19 ms). Expected: `TypeRegistry` holds 10-50 entries per module, both `SmolStr::hash` and `String::hash` delegate to `str::hash`, so this chunk's value is consistency / API surface, not raw throughput. The behaviour-preservation is the headline (workspace tests + corpus diagnostic counts byte-identical for `pro` 96W/4H/225 modules and `solarleb` 4W/6H/41 modules).

- [x] **25.3 SmolStr in `AnalysisResult.type_decls`** (S) — [`AnalysisResult.type_decls`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/analyzer.rs) becomes `FxHashMap<SmolStr, Idx<Decl>>`. Population in `analyzer.rs` (the per-module top-decl walk for `Decl::Type` / `Decl::Enum`) reads `hir.idents[…].text.as_str().into()` directly into `SmolStr` so the per-decl `String` clone is gone. Three lookup sites in [capabilities.rs](../greycat-analyzer-server/src/capabilities.rs) work unchanged (`get(&str)` borrows through `SmolStr: Borrow<str>`); one analyzer site (`resolve_member`) updated to pass `name.as_str()` instead of `&String`. Closes the P19.9 follow-up note in full. **Bench delta** (vs P25.1 baseline): `pro` 1.158 s → 994 ms (–14%), `solarleb` 349.7 ms → 275.3 ms (–21%). The win is the cumulative effect of P25.8's FxHashMap + this chunk's SmolStr keying — the per-decl-walk allocation is gone for the common case (identifiers ≤ 23 bytes inline).

- [x] **25.4 SmolStr in `TypeKind` name fields** (M, atomic sweep) — all six string-bearing sites in [greycat-analyzer-types/src/lib.rs](../greycat-analyzer-types/src/lib.rs) sweep in one chunk: `TypeKind::Named { name: SmolStr }`, `Generic { name: SmolStr, args }`, `GenericParam { name: SmolStr, owner }`, `Enum { name: SmolStr, variants: Vec<SmolStr> }`, `Anonymous { fields: Vec<(SmolStr, TypeId)> }`, `GenericOwner::{Function, Type}(SmolStr)`. New `typekind_name_dedups_across_smolstr_and_string_paths` unit test anchors the hash-equivalence invariant — allocates the same logical `Type` via three name-source paths (`String::from("Foo").into()`, `SmolStr::from("Foo")`, `"Foo"`) and asserts `TypeArena` returns one `TypeId`. Blast radius: every `TypeKind::*` destructure across analyzer.rs / project.rs / stdlib.rs / lint.rs — all mechanical (`p.name().to_string()` becomes `p.name().into()`; match arms get an explicit `Option<SmolStr>` annotation; `String::as_str` map becomes `SmolStr::as_str`; `GenericOwner::Function(text.to_string())` becomes `GenericOwner::Function(text.into())`). **Bench delta** (vs P25.1 baseline): `pro` 1.158 s → 940.6 ms (–19%), `solarleb` 349.7 ms → 281.5 ms (–20%). **`scripts/bench-lint.sh` reference comparison**: when `$BENCH_REF` points at the TS reference's `greycat-lang` binary (default `$HOME/.greycat/bin/greycat-lang`), each corpus benches Rust port and reference side-by-side in one hyperfine table. Current numbers: rust **5.11 ± 0.46×** faster than ref on `pro`, **4.63 ± 0.50×** faster on `solarleb`.

- [x] **25.5 SmolStr in HIR `Ident.text`** (M) — [`Ident { text: SmolStr, byte_range: Span }`](../greycat-analyzer-hir/src/types.rs). `smol_str` lands on `greycat-analyzer-hir`'s deps. Lowerer (`alloc_ident` + `alloc_property_ident`) reads `self.text(node).into()` directly. Reads via `Deref<Target=str>` survive unchanged across the analysis / server / wasm crates; the boundary sites that pipe a SmolStr into a still-`String`-typed downstream API (LSP `DocumentSymbol.name`, `dump-types` / `dump-resolutions` JSONL records, `signature_help` label, `render_type_ref`'s mutable accumulator, `ExposureSite.local_name`) explicitly convert via `.to_string()`. Internal callsites that own a `String` of the ident's text (analyzer's `extract_enum_chain` arm, `chain.enum_name`, `chain.arms[i].variant`) stay `String` for now — P25.6 promotes those to SmolStr. The analyzer's `generics_in_scope: Vec<FxHashMap<SmolStr, GenericOwner>>` propagates the SmolStr win through the type-param scope stack. The lint-side duplicate-decl `seen` set is now `FxHashMap<SmolStr, ()>`, dropping the per-decl `String` clone there. **Bench delta** (vs P25.1 baseline): `pro` 1.158 s → 894.0 ms (–23%), `solarleb` 349.7 ms → 257.0 ms (–27%); reference comparison: rust **4.97 ± 0.46×** faster than ref on `pro`, **4.93 ± 0.41×** faster on `solarleb`. Workspace tests + corpus diagnostic counts byte-identical (pro 96W/4H/225 modules; solarleb 4W/6H/41 modules).

- [x] **25.6 SmolStr cleanup: `Annotation` + `NonExhaustiveFinding` + `ExposureSite` + `TypeFlags`** (S) — consistency sweep across the remaining identifier-shaped String fields. [`Annotation { name: SmolStr, args: Vec<SmolStr> }`](../greycat-analyzer-hir/src/types.rs) (lowerer reads `cx.text(ident).into()` and `value.into()` directly); [`NonExhaustiveFinding { enum_name: SmolStr, missing: Vec<SmolStr> }`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/analyzer.rs); [`ExposureSite { local_name: SmolStr, rename: Option<SmolStr> }`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/stdlib.rs) (the `@expose("renamed")` capture map's value type); [`TypeFlags { deref: Option<SmolStr> }`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/stdlib.rs) (the `@deref("method")` annotation arg). Together this drains every per-decl `String` allocation that flowed through the modifiers/annotations pipeline at lowering time. **Bench delta** (vs P25.1 baseline): `pro` 1.158 s → 933.6 ms (–19%), `solarleb` 349.7 ms → 260.3 ms (–26%) — within noise of P25.5 since these fields aren't on the body-walker hot path. Reference comparison: rust **4.97 ± 0.57×** faster than ref on `pro`, **4.79 ± 0.46×** faster on `solarleb`. Workspace tests + corpus diagnostic counts byte-identical (pro 96W/4H/225 modules; solarleb 4W/6H/41 modules).

- [x] **25.7 SmallVec for ≤2-element collections** (S) — `smallvec = "1"` lands in `[workspace.dependencies]` and on `greycat-analyzer-types` + `greycat-analyzer-hir`. Applied to: `Modifiers.annotations: SmallVec<[Annotation; 1]>`, `FnDecl.generics` / `TypeDecl.generics: SmallVec<[Idx<Ident>; 2]>`, `Annotation.args: SmallVec<[SmolStr; 1]>`, `TypeKind::Generic.args: SmallVec<[TypeId; 2]>`. The HIR lowerer's `lower_annotations` and `lower_generics` return SmallVec directly (no `Vec::new()` → `into()` boundary). The arena's `generic` constructor accepts a `Vec<TypeId>` for caller convenience and converts inline (`args.into()`); the analyzer's two destructure-and-rebuild substitution loops collect into `SmallVec<[TypeId; 2]>` and drop back to `Vec` only at the constructor boundary. Two existing types-crate tests (`arena_substitute_replaces_generic_params`, `arena_substitute_round_trip`) updated to compare via `args.as_slice()` (SmallVec<[T; N]> doesn't impl PartialEq<Vec<T>> — slice comparison is the canonical workaround). **Skipped** `Tuple.elements` and `LambdaType.params` per the locked decision (2-4 element distribution is borderline; one inline / one heap with no clear win). **Bench delta** (vs P25.1 baseline): `pro` 1.158 s → 943.4 ms (–19%), `solarleb` 349.7 ms → 251.4 ms (–28%). Reference comparison: rust **4.94 ± 0.46×** faster than ref on `pro`, **5.04 ± 0.57×** faster on `solarleb`. Workspace tests + corpus diagnostic counts byte-identical (pro 96W/4H/225 modules; solarleb 4W/6H/41 modules).

- [x] **25.8 Faster HashMap (`rustc_hash::FxHashMap`)** (M) — `rustc-hash = "2"` lands in `[workspace.dependencies]` and on every analyzer-domain crate (types / core / analysis / server). Mechanical sweep across [project.rs](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/project.rs), [analyzer.rs](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/analyzer.rs), [stdlib.rs](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/stdlib.rs), [resolver.rs](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/resolver.rs), [lint.rs](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/lint.rs), [directives.rs](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/directives.rs), [types/lib.rs](../greycat-analyzer-types/src/lib.rs), [core/{manager,diagnostics,registry}.rs](../greycat-analyzer-core/src/), [server/{backend,capabilities}.rs](../greycat-analyzer-server/src/). Std `HashMap` uses `SipHash` for DoS-resistance, which is wasted work on analyzer-internal maps that never see attacker input. **Why FxHash and not AHash:** most of our keys are 32-bit (`Idx<T>`, `Symbol`, `TypeId`, `Uri` indices, short interned identifiers); `FxHash` is a one-instruction rotate+multiply per word and beats `AHash` on tiny keys, while `AHash`'s hardware-AES path is gone on wasm anyway. Same ecosystem-fit reasoning as SmolStr — it's the rust-analyzer / rustc default. **Skipped** the three `capabilities.rs` sites that construct `lsp_types::WorkspaceEdit::changes` (LSP API-typed `std::HashMap<Url, Vec<TextEdit>>`, can't swap). `HashMap::new()` rewrote to `FxHashMap::default()` (the `new` ctor needs `RandomState` specifically). The `TypeArena::substitute(&FxHashMap<String, TypeId>)` public signature changed — every callsite already passes ad-hoc maps, so we updated them in lockstep. **Hash-equivalence:** swapping the hasher changes iteration order, but no test today is order-sensitive. **Bench delta:** within noise (`pro` 1.158 → 1.333 s, `solarleb` 349.7 → 380.4 ms; both inside the 1σ baseline range). The hash work is a small fraction of overall analysis time on sub-second workloads, but the savings will compound under the SmolStr sweeps that follow (every name-keyed map now uses the cheaper hasher). Behaviour preservation is the headline (workspace tests + corpus diagnostic counts byte-identical).

**M25:** lint throughput on the maintainer's two reference corpora ends the phase **~19% faster on `pro` and ~28% faster on `solarleb`** vs. the 25.1 baseline (pro 1.158 s → 943 ms; solarleb 349.7 ms → 251 ms — single-shot wall clocks, 20-run hyperfine means). Side-by-side against the TypeScript reference: rust **5.0× faster on both corpora** (`pro` 4.94 ± 0.46×, `solarleb` 5.04 ± 0.57×). Registry parity baseline still 0; closed-source corpus diagnostic counts byte-identical (no behaviour drift across the seven chunks); workspace tests still green throughout. The cumulative win comes from FxHashMap (P25.8) replacing SipHash on every analyzer-internal map, plus SmolStr storage for every identifier-shaped string the analyzer holds (P25.2 / 25.3 / 25.4 / 25.5 / 25.6), plus SmallVec inlining of the four 0–2-element collection slots on the modifiers / generics path (P25.7).

---

### Phase 26 — Easy-win parallelism (rayon, exploration branch — ~1 week)

**Goal:** measure how much wall-clock time `cli lint` (the cold-load path that the bench-lint script exercises) actually loses to single-threaded execution, and try the cheap-to-add parallel seams to see what they buy. **This phase lives on the `parallelism-explore` branch — only landing on `main` if the wins justify the dep / complexity.**

**Why now.** P25 closed at rust ~5× faster than the TS reference and shaved every easy single-threaded allocation win in sight. The remaining latency on the `pro` corpus (~940 ms cold) is dominated by per-module work that is independent across modules: parse + HIR-lower (225 modules × ~3 ms each), per-module body walker (S12), per-module typed-lint pass. A modern laptop has 8-16 cores idling during every `cli lint` run.

**Why caveat-first.** The body walker (S12) takes `&mut TypeArena` for inference — that's the single point of synchronisation that decides whether project-wide parallelism is "embarrassing" or "messy". The cheap chunks (parallel HIR lowering, parallel typed-lint pass) don't touch the arena at all and are obviously safe. The body walker itself is the speculative chunk: gate it behind a Mutex and measure honestly. If contention dominates, drop it.

**Decisions locked.**

- **Crate: `rayon`** (not `tokio` / not `crossbeam` channels). The work is CPU-bound, embarrassingly per-module, and rayon's `par_iter` is the rust-analyzer-ecosystem default for exactly this shape. The work-stealing scheduler is a single small dep.
- **Cargo feature flag: `parallel`**, off by default. The CLI binary (`greycat-analyzer`) and the analysis crate gain a `parallel` feature; rayon is an optional dep gated on it. `cfg(feature = "parallel")` switches between the serial `for` loop and the rayon `par_iter`. **Both shapes ship side-by-side** so we can A/B them without a code-fork.
- **`scripts/bench-lint.sh` flex update**: the TS-reference comparison goes away (the `5×` flex was the P25 finale; further chunks compare to _ourselves_). Replace it with a serial-vs-parallel comparison: build two release binaries — one with `--features parallel`, one without — into separate `target/par-*` dirs, then run hyperfine across both for each corpus.
- **`DashMap`?** Probably not. The `ProjectIndex` is fully populated _before_ the parallel phases run (S1 → S7-S11 are the population stages), and read-only afterwards. `&ProjectIndex` shared across rayon threads needs no DashMap. If profiling surfaces a per-module write hot spot we'll revisit.
- **Hard rule — no behaviour drift.** Diagnostic counts on `pro` and `solarleb` must remain byte-identical between the serial and parallel builds at every chunk. Rayon's iteration order is non-deterministic; any pass that emits diagnostics in a particular order needs an explicit `sort_by_key` step before consumers see it.
- **Stop conditions.** Bail out of subsequent chunks when (a) parallel build is _slower_ than serial on either corpus (overhead exceeds gain — rare on 225-module workloads, common on 41-module ones if startup is the bottleneck), (b) a chunk would require restructuring `&mut TypeArena` flow rather than wrapping it, (c) the diff against serial mode shows non-deterministic diagnostic output that can't be sorted away cheaply.

**Chunks:**

- [x] **26.1 Bench-lint: drop reference comparison, add serial-vs-parallel mode** (XS) — `scripts/bench-lint.sh` no longer reads `$BENCH_REF`. Builds two release binaries side-by-side: `target/par-off` (default features) and `target/par-on` (`--features parallel`). Runs hyperfine across both for each corpus; the summary table reads off the speedup directly. The `parallel` feature is declared on `greycat-analyzer` (CLI) and `greycat-analyzer-analysis` as a no-op stub for this chunk — `rayon = "1"` lands in workspace deps and as an optional dep behind the feature, but no `cfg(feature = "parallel")` blocks exist yet, so both rows show the same number. **Baseline (P26.1)**: `pro` serial 953 ms, parallel 917 ms (1.04 ± 0.11×); `solarleb` serial 253 ms, parallel 253 ms (1.00 ± 0.07×). Both rows within 1σ of each other — confirms the no-op stub state.

- [x] **26.2 `parallel` feature + parallel HIR lowering in `stage_lower`** (S) — `rayon = "1"` lands in workspace deps and as an optional dep on `greycat-analyzer-analysis`. [`stage_lower`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/project.rs) splits into three phases under `cfg(feature = "parallel")`: (a) serial — borrow each `RefCell<Document>` once, clone `(Uri, text: String, lib: String, tree: Tree)` into an owned vec (Document is `!Sync` because of its embedded `Parser` + `OnceCell`; `Tree::clone` is rc-cheap so the only real allocations are the strings); (b) parallel — `par_iter` over the cloned vec, calling `lower_module` + `parse_directives` per module; (c) serial — `index.ingest` over the results, which mutates the project-wide interner. The serial path under `cfg(not(feature = "parallel"))` is preserved verbatim — the per-doc clones are skipped entirely so the serial cost stays at zero. **Bench delta** (vs P26.1 baseline, same scripts/bench-lint.sh harness): `pro` serial 999 ms → parallel 770 ms (**1.30 ± 0.16× faster**, -23 %); `solarleb` serial 278 ms → parallel 207 ms (**1.34 ± 0.16× faster**, -26 %). User time on the parallel runs is 1083 ms / 289 ms (both > wall clock — confirms real concurrent CPU work). Diagnostic output byte-identical between serial and parallel modes (corpus counts, ranges, messages all match).

- [x] **26.3 Parallel `run_typed_lints`** (S) — extracted the per-module lint sequence into a free fn `run_typed_lints_for_module(uri, module, arena, index, bypass, doc_data)` so the parallel and serial paths share one body. Under `cfg(feature = "parallel")` the function (a) pre-extracts each in-scope doc's `(text, tree)` into a sendable `FxHashMap<Uri, (String, Tree)>` (RefCell<Document> is `!Sync`), (b) collects `(&Uri, &mut ModuleAnalysis)` into a Vec, (c) runs `into_par_iter().for_each(...)` over the vec, calling the helper per-module. Every typed lint takes `&arena` (immutable) and `&index` (immutable); writes go to `module.lints` / `module.directives` (disjoint per thread). The serial path is preserved verbatim. **Bench delta**: `pro` serial 870 ms → parallel 688 ms (**1.26 ± 0.09× faster**); `solarleb` serial 264 ms → parallel 184 ms (**1.43 ± 0.14× faster**). User time on the parallel runs reaches 1179 ms / 304 ms — strong CPU saturation. Diagnostic output sorted-byte-identical between serial and parallel modes (CLI sorts by `(file, line, col)` before printing, so iteration order doesn't leak through).

- [x] **26.4 Parallel resolver + HIR-shape lints in `stage_per_module_analysis`** (S) — split the per-module loop into two phases: (a) **Pass A (parallel)** runs `resolve_with_index` and `run_lints_with_directives` per module — both read-only against `&self.index`, both write only to per-module return values; (b) **Pass B (serial)** runs `analyze_with_index_into` against `&mut self.arena`, then assembles `ModuleAnalysis`. Pass A widened from "just resolver" to "resolver + HIR-shape lints" because `run_lints_with_directives` (the unused-decl / generic shape pass) doesn't touch the arena either — same Sync constraints, same parallelisation discount. Pass B stays serial; P26.5 probes whether wrapping the arena in a Mutex makes it parallel too. **Bench delta**: `pro` serial 983 ms → parallel 658 ms (**1.49 ± 0.16× faster**, -33 %); `solarleb` serial 275 ms → parallel 187 ms (**1.46 ± 0.12× faster**, -32 %). User time on parallel runs 1178 ms / 321 ms — strong CPU saturation. Diagnostic output sorted-byte-identical.

- [~] **26.5 Speculative: parallel S12 body walker via `Mutex<TypeArena>`** (M) — **deliberately not pursued.** The body walker's `Cx<'a>` holds `arena: &'a mut TypeArena` and threads it through hundreds of `alloc` / `get` / `nullable` / `substitute` call sites across [analyzer.rs](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/analyzer.rs) and the typed-lint helpers. Switching to `&Mutex<TypeArena>` (with `lock()` at every call) is technically tractable but touches the entire analyzer surface — that's exactly the "redesign everything" the phase was scoped to avoid. The smaller-blast-radius alternative — give each rayon worker an exclusive lock for the _whole_ body walk of its module — degenerates to "serial body walk + thread-startup overhead" and so isn't a win. Per-thread arenas with a TypeId-remap merge step is the correct shape for this seam, but it's an XL refactor that belongs in its own phase if profiling on a 1000-module workspace ever surfaces the need. P26.2-4 already shaved ~33 % off the cold-load wall-clock; the body walker is what's left, but it stays serial here.

- [x] **26.6 Parallel CLI hydration loop** (XS) — the CLI's [`lint`](../greycat-analyzer/src/cmd/lint.rs) command's per-doc `Entry`-build loop ran `parse_diagnostics` + optional `pragma_diagnostics` + per-doc translation of analyzer diagnostics into LSP shape. Per-doc work is fully independent. Extracted the loop body into a `hydrate(uri, path, text, root)` closure so the parallel and serial paths share one body; under `cfg(feature = "parallel")` it pre-extracts each doc's `(text, tree)` into a Send-safe vec, then `par_iter` hydrates entries. `rayon` lands as an optional dep on `greycat-analyzer` (CLI) gated by the same `parallel` feature. **Bench delta**: `pro` serial 947 ms / parallel 660 ms (**1.44 ± 0.13× faster**); `solarleb` serial 268 ms / parallel 185 ms (**1.45 ± 0.15× faster**). Within noise of P26.4 (the CLI hydration is fast relative to analysis), but the consistency is worth keeping — every cold-load loop in the binary now goes through the same parallel seam.

**M26:** the parallel build ships **~33 % faster cold-load on `pro`** and **~32 % faster on `solarleb`** vs. the serial build of the same revision (`pro` 947 → 660 ms = 1.44× ; `solarleb` 268 → 185 ms = 1.45×). User-time on the parallel runs (1205 ms / 323 ms) confirms multi-core saturation. Workspace tests + corpus diagnostic output sorted-byte-identical between serial and parallel modes at every chunk. **Recommendation: land `--features parallel` as the default** in the CLI distribution if `main` adopts this branch — the cold-load wall-clock drop dominates the wasm-bundle / dep-tree cost (rayon adds ~50 KB stripped + 4 transitive deps). The body walker (S12) is the remaining serial bottleneck; that's an XL refactor (per-thread arena + TypeId remap merge) parked for a future profiling-driven phase if a 1000-module workspace ever arrives.

---

### Phase 27 — Parallelism shim (drop the feature flag) (~half a day)

**Goal:** consolidate P26's six scattered `cfg(feature = "parallel")` blocks into a single shim module, switch the gating from a Cargo feature to `cfg(target_arch = "wasm32")` (the _actual_ reason the dual path exists), and drop the now-vestigial `parallel` feature. After this phase the native CLI / LSP unconditionally use rayon, the wasm playground unconditionally uses the serial fallback, and there's exactly one place in the workspace that knows about the dual path.

**Why now.** P26 proved parallelism is a strict win on every measured workload (1.44× / 1.45× cold-load, byte-identical output). The remaining reason to gate is wasm — `rayon` compiles to `wasm32-unknown-unknown` but `par_iter` panics at runtime because `std::thread::spawn` doesn't work without `wasm-bindgen-rayon` + cross-origin-isolation headers, and the playground doesn't enable that. So the dual path stays, but it should be gated on the platform constraint (`target_arch`), not on a Cargo feature pretending parallelism is opt-in. And the dual-path code that's currently spread across `stage_lower` / `stage_per_module_analysis` / `run_typed_lints` / CLI hydration should consolidate into one shim — when the body-walker work lands in P28 it'll use the same seam.

**Decisions locked.**

- **Gate on `cfg(target_arch = "wasm32")`**, not on a Cargo feature. The constraint is "wasm doesn't have threads," so the cfg should say that. `default-features = false` dances in the wasm crate's Cargo.toml go away.
- **Per-target rayon dep.** `rayon = { workspace = true }` moves from `[dependencies]` (optional) to `[target.'cfg(not(target_arch = "wasm32"))'.dependencies]` (unconditional on native). Wasm builds don't pull rayon at all.
- **Shim lives in `greycat-analyzer-analysis::parallel`**, exposing a tight set of free functions (`par_map`, `par_map_ref`, `par_for_each`) with `T: Send` / `U: Send` / `F: Sync + Send` bounds. Each function dispatches once on `cfg(target_arch)`. Adding a new function takes ~10 lines.
- **Drop the `parallel` feature** from `greycat-analyzer-analysis/Cargo.toml` and `greycat-analyzer/Cargo.toml`. No more A/B build comparison in the bench script — there's only one binary on native.
- **`scripts/bench-lint.sh` simplifies.** Single binary build, single hyperfine run per corpus. Keep the corpus split (`pro` / `solarleb`) — that's still useful for tracking deltas across future chunks. The serial-vs-parallel A/B mode goes away with the feature it measured.
- **No behaviour change.** Workspace tests + corpus diagnostic output stay byte-identical to the parallel build of P26.6.

**Chunks:**

- [x] **27.1 Shim module + cfg gating + drop `parallel` feature** (M, atomic) — new [`greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/parallel.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/parallel.rs) with three free fns (`par_map`, `par_map_ref`, `par_for_each`), each dispatching once on `cfg(target_arch = "wasm32")`. Four call sites migrated: `stage_lower` (`par_map`), `stage_per_module_analysis` Pass A (`par_map`), `run_typed_lints` (`par_for_each`), CLI `lint`'s hydration loop (`par_map`). Every `#[cfg(feature = "parallel")]` block in those files is gone; the `run_typed_lints_for_module` helper is now a plain fn used by both native and wasm. The `parallel` feature is dropped from `greycat-analyzer-analysis/Cargo.toml` + `greycat-analyzer/Cargo.toml`. `rayon = { workspace = true }` moved from optional `[dependencies]` to unconditional `[target.'cfg(not(target_arch = "wasm32"))'.dependencies]` — only in the analysis crate (the CLI no longer needs its own rayon dep, it goes through `analysis::parallel::*`). **Verification**: `cargo tree -p greycat-analyzer | grep rayon` shows rayon in the native dep tree; `cargo tree --target wasm32-unknown-unknown -p greycat-analyzer-wasm | grep rayon` is empty. **Bench delta**: `pro` 628 ms (was 660 ms in P26.6 parallel mode), `solarleb` 172 ms (was 185 ms) — within noise; no perf regression from the shim hop. User-time on the new runs (1148 ms / 299 ms) preserved — same multi-core saturation. Workspace tests + corpus diagnostic counts byte-identical.

- [x] **27.2 Simplify `scripts/bench-lint.sh`** (XS) — landed alongside 27.1. Dropped the dual-build (`target/par-off` + `target/par-on`) plumbing. Single `cargo build --release -p greycat-analyzer` into the default `target/` dir, single hyperfine run per corpus. The script's purpose collapses from "A/B parallel vs serial" (27's premise) to "track lint throughput delta across phases" (the long-term role). Output reads `pro` / `solarleb` instead of `serial (pro)` / `parallel (pro)`.

**M27:** the workspace builds with no `--features` flags and runs at the same wall-clock as P26.6's parallel build (`pro` 628 ms / `solarleb` 172 ms — actually marginally better than P26.6's 660 / 185 ms numbers, attributable to the shim consuming the input vec instead of borrowing it on the rayon side). `cargo tree --target wasm32-unknown-unknown -p greycat-analyzer-wasm | grep rayon` is empty (rayon excluded from the wasm dep tree by the per-target dep declaration); `cargo tree -p greycat-analyzer | grep rayon` shows rayon in the native tree. Workspace tests + corpus diagnostic counts byte-identical to P26.6.

---

### Phase 28 — Parallel body walker (S12, per-thread arena merge) — **executed and reverted**

**Status:** all four chunks (`4e5aea1` 28.1, `103a2ca` 28.2, `0fc7d35` 28.3, `e8873e2` 28.4) shipped end-to-end and were **reverted** in `53ed7c0..431321b`. The full implementation is preserved in history (`git log 4e5aea1..e8873e2`) so the architectural pattern can be lifted again if a future workload sends the body walker back to dominating wall-clock.

**Original goal:** parallelize the per-module body walker (`analyze_with_index_into`) — the _assumed_ last serial bottleneck after P26 — by giving each rayon worker its own `LocalArena`, then merging the locals into the canonical project arena via a TypeId-remap step at the end of the parallel phase.

**What was built (in commits, then reverted):**

- [x] **28.1 Design + scaffold `LocalArena`** (L) — new type in `greycat-analyzer-types/src/lib.rs` wrapping a read-only snapshot of the canonical arena plus an append-only local tail; `TypeView` + `TypeArenaMut` traits to abstract over canonical vs. local; `TypeArena::merge_local(base_len, items) -> Vec<TypeId>` for the canonicalization remap. `LocalArena: Send`. _Implemented in `4e5aea1`, reverted._
- [x] **28.2 Refactor `Cx` to take `LocalArena`** (M) — `Cx` grew a second lifetime to hold `arena: &'a mut LocalArena<'b>`; `seed_builtins` and `register_module_types` generalized over `TypeArenaMut`; analyze pipeline stays serial but routes through the local arena, with merge + remap at the end. Diagnostic output byte-identical. _Implemented in `103a2ca`, reverted._
- [x] **28.3 Per-thread arena + merge step** (L) — `stage_per_module_analysis` Pass B fanned out via `parallel::par_map`; each worker took a `&TypeArena` snapshot, ran the body walker against its `LocalArena`, returned `(AnalysisResult, Vec<Type>, base_len)`; sequential merge phase canonicalized each thread's local items and remapped its result. Diagnostic output byte-identical. _Implemented in `0fc7d35`, reverted._
- [x] **28.4 Bench + ratchet** (XS) — apples-to-apples hyperfine on `pro` (225 modules) and `solarleb` (41 modules), 30 runs each, calm host: P27 head 665.9 ± 45.6 ms → P28.3 head 657.0 ± 44.0 ms = **1.01× ± 0.10×** on `pro`; 196.8 ± 16.6 ms → 186.9 ± 13.3 ms = **1.05× ± 0.12×** on `solarleb`. Both indistinguishable from noise. User-time on `pro` _increased_ (1213 → 1288 ms): more cores spinning, no wall-clock win. _Documented in `e8873e2`, reverted._

**M28 (closed, reverted):** the architectural foundation is correct (byte-identical output, sound merge invariant, `LocalArena: Send`, ~0.6 ms / 225-module merge cost — well below the contingency's "delta-only remap" threshold), but the bench delta is statistically zero on both corpora. **The premise was wrong:** the body walker was not the dominant remaining serial cost after P26. Stage-level instrumentation on warmed-up `pro` showed the actual breakdown of `analyze_staged` (~270 ms total): `lower` 65 ms (already parallel, P26.2), `sigs` 8 ms, `per_module` 30 ms (Pass A parallel + Pass B body walker — even fully parallelized, ~12 ms wall, with serial body walker estimated at 50-80 ms), `xmod` 48 ms (`run_typed_lints` already parallel + `validate_type_relations` serial), `qref` 122 ms (the unused-decl lint's cross-module reference counter, fully serial). P26.2 + P26.3 had already absorbed most of the body-walker-adjacent serial cost; what's left is dominated by `qref`. **Lesson:** the original P28 ROADMAP stated "Bench delta is the only acceptance criterion" and then proceeded to lock in a design built on an unverified assumption about _where_ the serial cost was. Future parallelism phases must instrument the suspected bottleneck **before** committing to a design (see Phase 29's 29.1 below). The full P28 implementation stays in history because the abstraction is sound; if the body walker grows back into the hot path, lift it from the reflog rather than re-deriving.

---

### Phase 29 — Parallelize `stage_compute_qualified_refs` (~3-5 days)

**Goal:** target the largest remaining serial slice in `analyze_staged` — `stage_compute_qualified_refs`, ~120 ms warm on `pro` (~45 % of `analyze_staged`'s ~270 ms total) per the M28 stage profile. The function already has the shape of two embarrassingly-parallel phases over modules, separated by a cheap aggregation step, so the parallelization pattern lifts straight from P26.3's `run_typed_lints` (the existing `crate::parallel::par_for_each` + Send-safe `(text, Tree::clone())` pre-extract dance).

**Why this stage, not the body walker.** P28 proved by reverted experiment that the body walker is not the bottleneck. Stage-level instrumentation on warmed-up `pro`:

| stage                  | wall (ms) | parallel today                                                                                 |
| ---------------------- | --------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `lower` (S1)           | ~65       | yes (P26.2)                                                                                    |
| `sigs` (S7-S11)        | ~8        | no — too small to matter                                                                       |
| `per_module`           | ~30       | Pass A parallel (P26.4); Pass B serial body walker, P28-shaped attempt yielded zero wall-clock |
| `xmod`                 | ~48       | `run_typed_lints` parallel (P26.3); `validate_type_relations` serial                           |
| **`qref`**             | **~122**  | **fully serial — Phase 29 target**                                                             |
| `analyze_staged` total | ~270      |                                                                                                |

`qref` is the biggest unparallelized chunk by a clear margin — bigger than everything in `per_module` combined, bigger than the post-S12 cross-module work.

**The work `compute_qualified_refs` does** (existing serial code in [`greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/project.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/project.rs) at `compute_qualified_refs`):

1. **Build name → URI map.** One scan of `manager.iter()` collecting `module_name → uri`. O(modules), microseconds.
2. **CST walk every module** for top-level `static_expr` chains. For each chain whose root is a known module name, look up `chain[1]` against the target module's HIR decls and record a bump for the matching decl. Read-only on `&self.modules`; writes only to a per-iteration `bumps` map. **Almost certainly the dominant serial cost** (educated guess; 29.1 confirms).
3. **Apply bumps** to each target module's `references_to` counter. O(bumps), cheap.
4. **Re-run the `UnusedDecl` lint per module** with the enriched counts. Each module's `lints` / `directives` are independent; the loop already iterates `self.modules.values_mut()` serially.

Phases 2 and 4 are both _embarrassingly parallel over modules with no shared mutable state inside each phase_, separated by phase 3's cheap serial aggregation. Same shape as P26.3.

**Why this lift is much smaller than P28.** No new abstraction layer (no per-thread arena, no merge step, no remap). Pure call-site replacement: serial loop → `crate::parallel::par_map` / `par_for_each`. The Send-safety dance for `Document` is already solved (P26.3's `Tree::clone` + `text.clone()` pre-extract). No lifetime parameters added. No public surface change.

**Investigation first — don't repeat the P28 mistake.**

The `~120 ms` figure is the whole function. The plan above assumes Phase 2 (CST walk) dominates inside it, but that's not measured yet. If Phase 4 (UnusedDecl re-run) is actually the hot one, the plan's chunks reorder; if neither dominates and the cost is split, parallelizing only one phase delivers half the win.

- [x] **29.1 Sub-phase profile** (XS, _no code ships_) — instrument `compute_qualified_refs` with `Instant::now()` deltas around (a) the name→URI build, (b) the CST walk loop, (c) the apply-bumps fold, (d) the UnusedDecl re-run loop. Gate the print on `P29_DEBUG=1` env var. Capture warmed-up numbers (3+ runs) on `pro` and `solarleb`. **Acceptance:** the four sub-phase totals are recorded in 29's milestone block. **Decide before 29.2 starts:** if Phase 2 < 25 ms on `pro`, abort the parallelization plan and retarget — the `qref` 120 ms must be coming from somewhere we haven't budgeted (e.g. the CST node walk's `parent()` lookups, the linear `target_module.hir.decls` scan inside the inner loop, etc.); fix that _first_. If Phase 2 > 80 ms but Phase 4 < 10 ms, ship 29.2 only and skip 29.3. If Phase 4 dominates, swap the order and ship 29.3 first. The instrumentation is reverted before 29.2 lands; the numbers go in the milestone. **Result:** Phase 2 (CST walk) dominates on both corpora — Phase 4 is in the noise. `pro` (5 warm runs after 1 warmup): name_uri 0.16-0.41 ms, **cst_walk 87-121 ms (median ~104)**, apply_bumps ≈ 0 ms, unused_rerun 0.12-0.33 ms. `solarleb` (5 warm runs): name_uri 0.03-0.06 ms, **cst_walk 25-29 ms**, apply_bumps ≈ 0 ms, unused_rerun ≈ 0.04 ms. Decision: **ship 29.2 only, skip 29.3** (Phase 4 < 10 ms gate). Instrumentation reverted in the same commit.

- [x] **29.2 Parallelize the CST walk** (M, gated on 29.1) — **executed and reverted** in 29.4 per the bench gate. Implementation preserved at commit `67f4972` (parent `1cc5c1a`); lift it again if a future workload makes the 60-100 ms savings worth the complexity. _Original chunk text:_ pre-extract `(uri, text, Tree::clone())` for every module into a Send-safe Vec (the P26.3 dance: `Document` is `!Sync` because of `Parser` + `OnceCell`, so we can't hold a `Ref<'_, _>` across rayon's worker boundaries; `Tree::clone` is reference-counted). Capture `&by_name` and `&self.modules` (both `Sync`) into the closure. Each closure produces `Vec<(target_uri, decl_id)>` for its module. Dispatch through `crate::parallel::par_map`. Then a serial fold aggregates into the existing `bumps` map and runs the existing apply step. **Acceptance** (met before revert): lint output on `pro` and `solarleb` byte-identical (sorted) — `references_to` counts are an internal state, but the externally-visible signal is whether the `unused-decl` lint fires on the same set of decls. Verified via `lint --format=compact --no-suppressions --lint-libs`: 73 lines on `pro`, 55 on `solarleb`, `diff` exits 0 against pre-29.2 head.

- [~] **29.3 Parallelize the UnusedDecl re-run** (S, gated on 29.1) — **skipped** per 29.1 gating decision: Phase 4 measured at < 0.5 ms on `pro` and < 0.1 ms on `solarleb`, far below the 10 ms threshold. Parallelizing would add rayon dispatch overhead with no measurable wall-clock win. The chunk is left in the ROADMAP as a record of the alternative plan; lift only if a future workload pushes Phase 4 into the budget. _Original chunk text:_ collect `(uri, &mut ModuleAnalysis)` into a Vec (same pattern as P26.3's `run_typed_lints`); pre-extract `doc_data` if the lint body needs `text` / `tree`; dispatch through `crate::parallel::par_for_each`; the closure body is the existing `LintRule::check(&UnusedDecl, …)` block.

- [x] **29.4 Bench + ratchet** (XS) — apples-to-apples hyperfine on `pro` + `solarleb` (30 runs each, 3 warmups, calm host), comparing the current `main` head vs. the P29 head. **Acceptance:** ≥ 1.15× wall-clock on `pro` (~80-100 ms shaved out of ~660 ms total CLI wall) AND user-time-to-wall-time ratio increases (proves cores are saturated, not just shifting cost around). If delta is < 1.10× **revert the chunks and write up the actual finding** (analogous to M28's writeup). _Do not amend the success criterion to match the result._ **Result:** revert triggered. Two independent rounds, hyperfine warm (5 warmups, 50 runs, calm host), comparing pre-29.2 head `1cc5c1a` vs post-29.2 head `67f4972`: round 1 `pro` 636.1 ± 38.2 ms → 600.4 ± 35.0 ms = **1.06 ± 0.09×** (User: 1308.6 → 1416.7 ms; ratio 2.06 → 2.36); round 2 `pro` 637.9 ± 45.0 ms → 596.4 ± 42.0 ms = **1.07 ± 0.11×** (User: 1310.7 → 1422.9 ms; ratio 2.05 → 2.39). User-time-to-wall ratio rose in both rounds (cores more saturated, as required), but wall-clock delta is below the 1.10× revert threshold both times. `solarleb` (3 warmups, 30 runs): 175.2 ± 10.2 ms → 168.8 ± 11.0 ms = 1.04 ± 0.09×, expected per the chunk ("`solarleb` too small for parallelization to overcome rayon overhead"). 29.2 reverted in this commit; ROADMAP records the actual finding rather than amending the gate to match.

**M29 (closed, reverted):** the parallel CST-walk implementation is correct (byte-identical lint output, sound aggregation invariant, `Tree::clone` + `text.clone()` Send-safe inputs lifted from P26.3) but the bench delta sits at 1.06-1.07× — below the documented < 1.10× revert threshold. The 29.1 sub-phase profile _did_ identify the right hot spot (Phase 2 = CST walk dominates `compute_qualified_refs`), so the architectural premise was correct, unlike P28 which assumed a hot spot that wasn't there. What the experiment actually proves is that even when you target the right serial slice, 12 rayon workers + the per-task dispatch overhead + the tree-sitter CST walk's poor cache behavior together can't deliver more than ~6-7% wall-clock on this workload. The serial slice was ~104 ms on a ~660 ms total run; theoretical max savings if perfectly parallelized to 12 cores is ~94 ms, and we captured ~40 ms of that — which sounds like ~40% efficiency, not bad in absolute terms, but the absolute floor on the rest of the pipeline (lower, sigs, per_module already-parallel + body walker, xmod, lints) puts a hard ceiling on what `qref` parallelization alone can achieve. Sub-phase profile from 29.1 stays in this writeup; 29.3 was correctly skipped (Phase 4 < 0.5 ms). Future parallelism phases should not target `compute_qualified_refs` unless something in the surrounding pipeline shrinks first and lifts `qref`'s relative weight.

**Stretch (no longer in scope):** with 29.2 reverted, the per-stage breakdown on `pro` looks roughly the same as before P29 — `qref` ~104 ms, `xmod` ~48 ms (with `validate_type_relations` ~30-40 ms estimated inside it), `lower` ~65 ms, `per_module` ~30 ms, `sigs` ~8 ms. The biggest remaining serial slice is still `qref`, but P29 just proved parallelizing it doesn't pay; chasing `validate_type_relations` next would cost a similar amount of complexity for a similar marginal win. If a future workload shifts where the cost lands (e.g. a corpus where `validate_type_relations` dominates `qref`), revisit then with the same profile-first / decide-second / ship-third discipline 29 used. Otherwise, leave the parallelism budget alone — the architectural cost of more `Sync` plumbing is no longer worth it on this pipeline.

---

### Phase 31 — Inheritance-aware LSP navigation (~3-5 days)

**Goal:** fix three issues with `textDocument/{definition,implementation}` and add `textDocument/declaration` so jumping between abstract methods and their concrete overrides works correctly across the supertype chain. The analyzer already has every piece of information needed (`ProjectIndex::is_subtype_of`, `type_instance_method_id_chain`, `foreign_member_uses`, `static_methods`); the LSP handlers just don't use it consistently.

**The three issues:**

- **Cross-module goto-def silently fails.** [`goto_definition`](../greycat-analyzer-server/src/capabilities.rs) consults `member_lookup` (in-module `member_uses` only) and falls through to `None` when the resolved member lives in another module. The analyzer already populates `foreign_member_uses` with the URI and `Idx<Decl>` / `Idx<TypeAttr>` of the foreign decl; the handler should read it and resolve to a cross-file `Location`. P11.3 left this as a stub.
- **Goto-implementation over-matches by name.** [`goto_implementation`](../greycat-analyzer-server/src/capabilities.rs) and [`goto_implementation_across_project`](../greycat-analyzer-server/src/capabilities.rs) walk every `TypeDecl::methods`, filter `abstract` / `native`, and return everything that matches by name. From an abstract `process` in `Base`, it returns any concrete `process` from any unrelated type. The receiver's declaring type is never consulted.
- **No `textDocument/declaration` handler.** The inverse of goto-implementation — jumping from a concrete override to its abstract declaration in the supertype chain — has no path in the current LSP. The `declaration_provider` capability isn't even advertised.

**Chunks:**

- [x] **31.1 Cross-module goto-def via `foreign_member_uses`** (S) — when the in-module `member_lookup` returns `None`, fall through to `foreign_member_lookup`. The `ForeignMember` carries `uri` + `MemberDef::{Attr, Method}`; resolve the foreign module's text + HIR via `SourceManager` to compute the byte range of the decl's name ident, then return a cross-file `Location`. Routes through `goto_definition_handler` in `server.rs`, not the `capabilities` free-function (which has no `&SourceManager`). Tests: chain `Sub` declared in `mod_a.gcl` with method on `Base` declared in `mod_b.gcl` — cursor on `instance.method()` in `mod_c.gcl` jumps to `mod_b.gcl`'s declaration site.
- [x] **31.2 Goto-implementation subtype filter** (M) — when the cursor lands on a method-name ident, first determine its _declaring type_ (via `member_uses` / `foreign_member_uses`, or — if the cursor is on the method's own decl site — the enclosing `TypeDecl`). Then filter the candidate-set to types that satisfy `index.is_subtype_of(candidate, declaring_type)` (or are the declaring type itself). The existing abstract / native skip stays. This is a tightening, not a broadening: any returned location is now a true override. Cross-module variant gets the same filter against the project index. Tests: abstract `process` on `Base`, override on `Child extends Base`, unrelated `Bystander::process` — goto-impl returns `Child::process` only.
- [x] **31.3 `textDocument/declaration` capability** (M) — advertise `declaration_provider: Some(true)` in the server's capability initialisation. Add a `GotoDeclaration` request handler routing to a new `capabilities::goto_declaration_across_project`. Semantics: cursor on a method-name ident, find the method's _declaring type_, walk the supertype chain via `type_instance_method_id_chain` (or a chain walker that filters by `modifiers.abstract_`), return the first abstract ancestor's location. If the cursor's method is itself abstract, fall through to `goto_definition`. Tests: concrete `Child::process` overrides abstract `Base::process` — goto-declaration jumps to `Base`'s decl, not `Child`'s.
- [x] **31.4 Cross-module ancestor walker helper** (S, gated on 31.3) — `ProjectIndex::find_abstract_ancestor_method(type_name, method_name)` that walks the supertype chain (already capped at `MAX_SUPERTYPE_CHAIN_DEPTH`) and returns `(Uri, Idx<Decl>)` for the first ancestor whose method with that name has `modifiers.abstract_`. If no such ancestor exists, return `None`. Shared between 31.3 and any future "Implementations of …" tooling.

**M31:** all three LSP navigation requests return inheritance-aware results. Goto-def works across modules for inherited members; goto-impl returns only true overrides (no unrelated-type false positives); goto-declaration is wired and jumps to the abstract parent. Per-chunk tests cover the cross-module path and the same-module path.

**Out of scope:** "find all implementations" with multi-level chains (Type A → B → C, where B is abstract and C concretes A's method — both A and C are interesting; this phase only returns the _direct_ abstract declarer for now).
