Also: type hierarchy view (`textDocument/typeHierarchy`) is a separate LSP capability worth its own phase if real demand surfaces.

---

### Phase 30 — `recv.staticName` / `recv->staticName` advisory lint (~2-3 days)

**Goal:** introduce a new lint rule that flags instance-access (`.` / `->`) to a _static_ member and proposes rewriting it as `Type::staticName`. The analyzer already has every signal it needs — for a given `Expr::Member` / `Expr::Arrow` binding it knows whether the resolved member is a `static fn` or `static` attr — so the role of this phase is purely advisory: guide developers toward the syntactic form that matches their intent.

**Why this is its own phase.** The fix in `fix(analysis): attrs win over methods; instance access skips static` already filters static methods out of instance-access resolution to match the runtime. That fix is **silent**: when a static method exists _and no attr of the same name does_, the analyzer simply fails to bind the member and the user never finds out their `.` should have been a `::`. A separate lint surfaces the misuse:

- `recv.staticName` _and_ the receiver type has no instance member (attr or non-static method) of that name → fire. The user clearly meant the static (the analyzer would otherwise leave it unbound), and `Type::staticName` is the correct rewrite.
- `recv.staticName` _and_ the receiver type does have an instance member (attr or non-static method) of that name → **do not fire**. The instance-lookup already bound the right thing (the runtime semantics match `.` here), and proposing `Type::staticName` would change semantics — `Type::staticName` in the presence of an attr-name collision resolves to the attr too (the runtime returns a `field` handle, not the static method), so the rewrite wouldn't even reach the intended static method.

**Constraints from the existing fix:**

- After `fix(analysis): attrs win over methods`, instance access _never binds to a static method via the local-or-chain lookup_. So `member_uses` / `foreign_member_uses` for an `Expr::Member` / `Expr::Arrow` will not point at a static method on its own. The detection has to run a _separate_ check: did the normal lookup leave the member unbound, and does the receiver type's chain expose a static member of the same name?
- The lint must short-circuit when an instance member of the same name _exists at all_ in the receiver's chain (whether or not the normal lookup actually bound it on this expression). That's the case where rewriting to `::` would change semantics, so the lint stays silent.

**Chunks:**

- [ ] **30.1 Lint rule registration + diagnostic shape** (XS) — add `instance-access-on-static` (working name) to `LINT_RULES` in [`greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/lint.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/lint.rs) with a one-line summary; wire emission through `run_typed_lints` and the per-pass `module.lints.retain` filter; add the rule name to `default_tag_for` (probably no UNNECESSARY tag — this is style guidance, not dead code). Touch all four touchpoints listed in CLAUDE.md's "Adding / removing a lint rule" table.
- [ ] **30.2 Detection pass** (S) — for each `Expr::Member` / `Expr::Arrow` in HIR, walk the receiver type's supertype chain and decide:
  - is there a _static_ member (`static_attrs` ∪ `static_methods`) named `prop`?
  - is there an _instance_ member (a non-static `methods` entry OR an `attrs` entry) named `prop`?

  Fire **only** when the static answer is yes AND the instance answer is no. The index already exposes `static_attrs` / `static_methods` / `methods` / `attrs` per `TypeMembers`; add a walk-chain helper if needed. Diagnostic span: the property segment's byte range. Message: `static \`X::{prop}\` accessed via instance form — use \`X::{prop}\` instead`.

- [ ] **30.3 Quickfix (auto-fix path)** (S) — register a per-rule fixer in [`greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/quickfix.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/quickfix.rs) that rewrites the byte range `[receiver_start, prop_end]` from `recv.prop` / `recv->prop` to `Type::prop`. The `Type` to substitute is the **declared type** of the receiver — _not_ the runtime instance type — because `Sub::staticName` resolves through the supertype chain at runtime when `Sub` doesn't declare its own `staticName`. For receivers whose declared type can't be cheaply recovered as text (computed expressions, casts, anonymous types) the quickfix is unavailable; the diagnostic still fires.
- [ ] **30.4 Suppression + tests** (S) — verify `// gcl-lint-off instance-access-on-static` silences the rule; add tests covering: (a) the no-instance-member case (lint fires, quickfix rewrites to `::`); (b) the attr-collision case (lint stays silent — `Type::staticName` would resolve to the attr too, so the rewrite would change semantics and the runtime already does the right thing on `.`); (c) non-static method present locally (lint stays silent — same reasoning, the instance member binds correctly via `.`); (d) negative for non-static methods called via `.` (`recv.someMethod()` doesn't fire); (e) negative for the already-correct static-access form (`Type::staticName` doesn't fire); (f) suppression directive silences.
- [ ] **30.5 Run against the secret corpus + stdlib closure** (XS) — confirm zero false positives. If a real call site relies on inherited-attr shadowing where the lint message would be confusing, refine the message or add the case to the test grid; do not relax detection. The lint is opt-in by being a `warning` by default — projects that want it stricter can `--disable=` lint per rule.

**M30:** the rule appears in `--list-rules`, runs in `cargo run -- lint` and the LSP, auto-fixes with `--fix`, and adds zero false positives to the stdlib closure. The lint message text and quickfix rewrite are reviewed against the runtime oracle before landing.

**Out of scope:** rewriting `Type::instanceMember` to `recv.instanceMember` (the opposite direction). That would require the LSP to materialize a receiver, which is a heavier code action — leave it for a separate phase if real demand surfaces.

---

### Phase 32 — Multi-project LSP workspaces (~1-2 weeks)

**Goal:** let one LSP session host many independent GreyCat projects. Today [`Backend`](../greycat-analyzer-server/src/backend.rs) holds a single `SourceManager` + `ProjectAnalysis` + `Option<PathBuf>` project root, and the `workspace_folders` loop in [`initialized`](../greycat-analyzer-server/src/backend.rs#L91) overwrites the root on every iteration so the _last_ workspace folder wins. Anyone with a multi-project repo (sibling `projectA/project.gcl` + `projectB/project.gcl`, or a nested `outer/project.gcl` with deeper `outer/sub/project.gcl`) silently gets analysis for at most one of them. The analyzer itself (`lower`, `resolve`, `analyze`) is already project-agnostic — this phase is a pure server refactor + URI-routing pass.

**Behavioral contract (locked from design discussion):**

- **Eager discovery:** for every workspace folder, check `<folder>/project.gcl` only. Found → load it + its `@library` / `@include` closure into its own isolated `Project`. Each project has its own `SourceManager`, `ProjectAnalysis`, `TypeArena`, `ProjectIndex`. Nested `project.gcl` files deeper in the tree are NOT scanned at startup.
- **Lazy discovery:** on `did_open(uri)`, route in this order:
  1. `uri` already in some loaded project's closure → that project owns it.
  2. Walk parents from `uri`'s directory upward, stopping at (and including) the enclosing workspace folder root. The _first_ `project.gcl` encountered is the owner. If its project isn't loaded yet, spin one up and load its closure.
  3. No `project.gcl` found in the walk → orphan.
- **Orphan policy:** publish parse diagnostics + one file-spanning `Information` diag with `DiagnosticTag::UNNECESSARY` (so editors dim the whole file). Code: `orphan-module`. Message: _"This file is not part of any GreyCat project (no `project.gcl` found from this file's directory up to the workspace folder root). Add a `project.gcl` to enable full analysis."_ No resolve/analyze/lints run on orphans.
- **Multi-owner policy:** if two projects' closures both reach the same file (overlapping `@include`s), publish a file-spanning `Information` + `UNNECESSARY` diag listing the conflicting roots and stating _"This file is reachable from multiple GreyCat projects — almost always a design error. Restructure your `@include` paths so only one project owns each file."_ Code: `multi-project-owner`. The file dispatches to the first project that loaded it for any analysis still emitted, but the conflict diag appears regardless.
- **Lifetime:** lazily-loaded projects stay resident until LSP shutdown or until their containing workspace folder is removed.
- **Cross-project navigation is intentionally absent.** Two projects with same-named decls do not see each other; this matches the runtime's project closure semantics.

**Chunks:**

- [x] **32.1 `Project` struct + `Backend::projects` collection** (M) — introduce a `Project` newtype owning `{ root: PathBuf, manager: SourceManager, analysis: ProjectAnalysis }`. Replace `Backend::{manager, project_analysis, project_root}` with `projects: FxHashMap<PathBuf, Project>` keyed by canonical project-root path, plus `uri_owner: FxHashMap<Uri, PathBuf>` for URI → owning-project lookup, plus `workspace_roots: Vec<PathBuf>` to bound the parent walk in 32.3. Add a `Backend::project_for(&Uri) -> Option<&Project>` (and `_mut` variant) helper. Keep `lint_libs` and `registry` as Backend-global (per-project would be overkill). All capability dispatch goes through `project_for`. This chunk does the data-shape change only — eager loading becomes "for each ws folder, optionally insert one project" and `did_open` keeps today's "single project" assumption (fall through to `projects.values().next()`); subsequent chunks tighten that. Tests: a unit test that constructs a Backend with two projects, asserts `project_for` routes correctly given a hand-populated `uri_owner`.
- [x] **32.2 Eager workspace-folder discovery** (S) — rewrite [`Backend::initialized`](../greycat-analyzer-server/src/backend.rs#L91) and [`load_workspace`](../greycat-analyzer-server/src/backend.rs#L172) to: (a) push every resolved workspace folder path into `workspace_roots`; (b) for each, check `<root>/project.gcl` and, if present, construct a fresh `Project`, run `load_project` + `analysis.rebuild`, then bulk-insert every loaded URI into `uri_owner`. Multiple roots → multiple projects, all coexisting. The startup `info!` line gains a `[load_project] {N} files in {dt} from {root}` per project. Tests: integration test fixture under `greycat-analyzer-server/tests/` with two sibling project directories; assert both publish diagnostics.
- [x] **32.3 Owner-search on `did_open`** (M) — new `find_owning_project_root(uri: &Uri, workspace_roots: &[PathBuf]) -> Option<PathBuf>` in [`backend.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-server/src/backend.rs) that walks parents from the file's dir up to (and including) the workspace folder containing `uri`, returning the first directory holding a `project.gcl`. Stops cold at the workspace boundary. In `did_open`: if `uri_owner.get(&uri).is_some()` → route to that project; else walk to find the owner; if found and not in `projects` → spawn + load + index; if found and already loaded → just bind the URI to it (no re-load); if no owner → mark orphan. Tests: nested-project fixture (`outer/project.gcl` + `outer/sub/project.gcl`); opening `outer/sub/foo.gcl` spawns the inner project; opening `outer/bar.gcl` keeps using outer.
- [x] **32.4 Capability dispatch by URI** (M) — every public LSP handler in [`capabilities.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-server/src/capabilities.rs) and the request `match` in [`server.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-server/src/server.rs) currently consumes `&Backend` and reaches into `self.manager` / `self.project_analysis` directly. Re-thread them through `Backend::project_for(&request.text_document.uri)` so each request operates on the owning project's `(SourceManager, ProjectAnalysis)`. Handlers that take a `&Uri` already have the routing key; `workspace/symbol` (multi-URI) iterates over all projects and concatenates. `publish_for`, `invalidate_with_slow_warning`, `is_project_entrypoint`, `reload_project_closure` all become per-project (take a `&Path` project root or operate via `&mut Project`). The pragma-diagnostics path in `publish_for` reads `project.root` instead of the old `Backend::project_root`. Tests: cross-project goto-def is _not_ expected to find symbols in a sibling project — assert that explicitly so we don't accidentally regress later.
- [x] **32.5 Orphan handling + dim diagnostic** (S) — add `Backend::orphans: FxHashMap<Uri, Document>` (or extend an unowned `SourceManager` for parse-only) so we still get tree-sitter parses without running through any project's analysis. Add `core::diagnostics::orphan_module_diagnostic(root_node, text) -> Diagnostic` in [`greycat-analyzer-core/src/diagnostics.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-core/src/diagnostics.rs) emitting an `Information` severity diag with `DiagnosticTag::UNNECESSARY`, code `orphan-module`, range = whole document, and the user-visible message above. `publish_for` on an orphan URI publishes parse diags + this single dim diag. `did_close` clears it normally. Tests: a `.gcl` file in a workspace folder with no `project.gcl` anywhere up-tree publishes exactly the parse + orphan diags, no resolver / analyzer output. Document the rule name in the lint registry? No — this is a _server_ diagnostic, not a lint rule, so it doesn't go through `LINT_RULES`.
- [x] **32.6 Multi-owner conflict diagnostic** (S) — extend `uri_owner` to `uri_owner: FxHashMap<Uri, SmallVec<[PathBuf; 1]>>` (most files have one owner; rare conflicts use the heap fallback). Lazy / reload `load_project` paths _append_ to the entry rather than overwriting. New `core::diagnostics::multi_project_owner_diagnostic(text, roots: &[PathBuf]) -> Diagnostic` builds an `Information` + `UNNECESSARY` diag with code `multi-project-owner` and a message listing the conflicting project roots (relative to the workspace folder when possible). `publish_for` overlays this diag on top of whatever the first owner produces. Tests: two projects whose closures both `@include` a shared dir → the shared file publishes parse + first-owner analysis + the conflict diag.
- [x] **32.7 Watcher routing** (S) — [`did_change_watched_files`](../greycat-analyzer-server/src/backend.rs#L394) currently calls a single `reload_project_closure`. Group events by owning project: for each event path, find owner via `find_owning_project_root`, bucket events into `HashMap<PathBuf, Vec<FileEvent>>`, then call the per-project reload only for the buckets that need it. `lib/installed` events route to the project whose root _is_ the parent of `lib/`. Events for files outside any project are ignored (the orphan path doesn't watch). Tests: a `lib/installed` write in `projectA/lib/` only reloads projectA, not projectB.
- [x] **32.8 Workspace folder add / remove** (S) — add a `workspace/didChangeWorkspaceFolders` handler. Added folder → run the eager discovery from 32.2 over just the new folder. Removed folder → drop every project whose root is inside it from `projects`, evict their URIs from `uri_owner`, clear-publish empty diagnostics for every URI they owned. Tests: integration test that adds and removes a folder mid-session.
- [x] **32.9 Per-project log tagging** (S) — every log message originating from a per-project code path gets a leading `[<rel-path>]` tag where `<rel-path>` is the project root's path relative to its enclosing workspace folder (e.g. `[clientA]`, `[clientB/api]`). When the project root IS the workspace folder root (relative path is empty), fall back to the workspace folder's basename so the tag stays meaningful (e.g. `[myproject]`). Compute the tag string once at `Project` construction and store it on the struct; every `debug!` / `info!` / `warn!` inside per-project paths (load, reload, invalidate, publish, watcher dispatch) reads it. Non-project paths use static literals: `[server]` for lifecycle (`initialized`, `register_file_watchers`, capability registration) and `[orphan]` for orphan-file handling. Tests: not unit-tested directly (log output isn't asserted), but the integration tests from 32.2 / 32.3 should have their log capture spot-checked to confirm the prefixes appear and disambiguate projects.
- [x] **32.10 CLI sanity + docs** (XS) — confirm `greycat-analyzer lint` and `fmt` are unaffected (they take an explicit entrypoint, never use `Backend`). Update [.claude/CLAUDE.md](../.claude/CLAUDE.md) "Project model" section: the LSP now hosts N independent projects; the CLI still operates on one entrypoint at a time. Add a one-paragraph note to [README.md](../README.md) describing multi-project support and the orphan / multi-owner dim diagnostics so users know what they mean when they see them.

**M32:** opening a VSCode workspace with two sibling `project.gcl` files (or a nested `sub/project.gcl` whose files get opened) loads each as an independent project, with full hover / goto-def / diagnostics inside each. Orphan files are dimmed with a clear "no project" message; files reachable from multiple projects are dimmed with a "design error" message naming the conflicting roots. Watcher events and entrypoint edits route to the correct owning project. The integration tests added per chunk all pass.

**Out of scope:**

- Cross-project navigation (intentional — projects are isolated closures matching the runtime).
- A "default project" or merging multiple projects into one analysis.
- Auto-discovery of nested projects at startup (only opened files trigger lazy load — by design).
- Per-project `lintLibs` / registry settings (server-global is enough for now).
- A code action that creates a `project.gcl` for an orphan file (could ride a future quickfix phase).

---

### Phase 33 — Runtime-aligned `std` resolution (~half a day)

**Goal:** match the GreyCat runtime's `std` resolution policy. Today [`SourceManager::load_project`](../greycat-analyzer-core/src/manager.rs) only loads `std` when `project.gcl` explicitly declares `@library("std", ...)`; the runtime, in contrast, _always_ uses `std` — a local `<project>/lib/std/` if present, otherwise the host-wide `<greycat_home>/lib/std/`, otherwise its embedded definitions. The Rust analyzer has no embedded copy, so when both filesystem locations are empty we can't do meaningful analysis. This phase aligns the resolver and surfaces the "no std" case truthfully on the entrypoint.

**Behavioral contract:**

- The resolver loads `std` regardless of pragma declarations. Resolution order: `<project_dir>/lib/std/` → `<greycat_home>/lib/std/` (`$GREYCAT_HOME` env first, else `$HOME/.greycat`). No fallback if neither exists.
- This applies _only_ to `std`. Every other `@library("foo", ...)` keeps its current behavior: local-only, falls through to `unresolved-library` pragma diagnostic if the dir doesn't exist.
- When `std` can't be resolved, [`SourceManager::load_project`](../greycat-analyzer-core/src/manager.rs) returns `LoadReport::std_resolution = StdResolution::Missing`.
- The LSP and CLI surface that as a single `missing-std` Error+UNNECESSARY diagnostic on the `project.gcl` entrypoint. Other modules of the project are not annotated — they're already noisy with "unresolved type" errors that the missing-std diag explains.
- Pragma `@library("std", "1.2.3")` declarations still work as before; the new auto-loader is idempotent against [`SourceManager::load_file`](../greycat-analyzer-core/src/manager.rs)'s `visited` set, so a pragma-driven load + the auto-load don't double-parse.

**Chunks:**

- [x] **33.1 Auto-load std + `missing-std` diagnostic** (S) — extend [`LoadReport`](../greycat-analyzer-core/src/manager.rs) with a `std_resolution: StdResolution { Local | Global | Missing }` field and an `entrypoint_uri: Option<Uri>`. Add `SourceManager::ensure_std_loaded` and call it from `load_project` unconditionally after `process_libraries`. Add [`core::diagnostics::missing_std_diagnostic`](../greycat-analyzer-core/src/diagnostics.rs) (Error severity, `UNNECESSARY` tag, code `missing-std`, range = whole file). LSP: [`Project`](../greycat-analyzer-server/src/backend.rs) captures both fields from each load and `publish_for` overlays the diag when `std_resolution == Missing && entrypoint_uri == Some(uri)`. CLI: [`cmd::lint`](../greycat-analyzer/src/cmd/lint.rs) hydrate closure injects the diag on the entrypoint URI. Tests: three `manager` unit tests covering local-wins / global-fallback / missing; one LSP integration test (hermetic via `GREYCAT_HOME=/tmp/empty`) asserting the diag's code, Error severity, and `UNNECESSARY` tag.

**M33:** opening a workspace whose project has no `std` available (neither local nor global) shows exactly one Error-severity advisory dimmed across the project.gcl explaining the situation. The CLI's `lint` command surfaces the same diag at the entrypoint. Projects that _do_ have std (local or global) keep loading it transparently, without needing `@library("std", ...)` in their project.gcl.

**Out of scope:**

- Embedded std fallback. The TS reference and the runtime have a built-in `std` for grammatical correctness; the analyzer doesn't, and shipping a vendored copy is a separate phase if it ever becomes desirable.
- A code action that runs `greycat install` from the editor. Could ride a future quickfix phase.
- A server-side filesystem watcher that bypasses the editor entirely (the rust-analyzer model). See Phase 34.

---

### Phase 34 — Server-side filesystem watcher (~3-5 days, optional)

**Goal:** stop trusting the editor's `workspace/didChangeWatchedFiles` for filesystem deltas and run our own watcher in the LSP process — the rust-analyzer model. Phase 33 leaves a known gap: when the editor's file watcher misses or coalesces events (notably `rm -rf <dir>` from a terminal, where VSCode's watcher behaviour varies by platform and version), the analyzer can hold stale URIs and goto-def returns locations for files that no longer exist. A server-side watcher gives us a single, predictable code path regardless of who the client is — and as a bonus, it works correctly when the LSP is driven by an editor that doesn't support dynamic capability registration at all.

**Trigger to do this phase:** real-world reports of stale URIs or missed reloads. Until then we live with whatever the editor's watcher gives us. This phase is **opt-in** — it adds a thread, a channel, a dep, and a non-trivial amount of plumbing; we only invest if reliability becomes a recurring complaint.

**Behavioral contract:**

- Add a `notify`-driven watcher thread per [`Backend`](../greycat-analyzer-server/src/backend.rs). Watched roots: every entry in `workspace_roots`, every `<greycat_home>/lib/std` directory, every loaded `project.root`'s `lib/` subtree. Roots are registered/unregistered as projects load/unload and workspace folders come and go.
- Events ship through a `crossbeam_channel::Sender<WatcherEvent>` into the main `lsp-server` loop alongside `Message::*`. The main loop's `match` gains a third arm that dispatches to a new `Backend::on_fs_event` handler.
- `on_fs_event` is a strict superset of today's `did_change_watched_files` — same `is_installed` / `is_gcl` logic, just driven by notify events. We keep `did_change_watched_files` wired for editors that prefer to drive their own watcher; both paths funnel into the same `apply_fs_event` helper.
- Debounce / coalesce notify's high-frequency event stream (notify emits one event per affected inode; saving a file in vim can produce CREATE+MODIFY+ATTRIB+RENAME+DELETE in milliseconds). 50–100 ms debounce window, batched flush.
- Cross-platform behaviour: notify abstracts inotify (Linux), FSEvents (macOS), ReadDirectoryChangesW (Windows). Each has quirks; the watcher module owns the abstraction so the rest of the backend doesn't care.
- Fall back to the editor watcher when notify fails to start (e.g. CI sandboxes with inotify disabled). Log an `info!` once, then operate as today.

**Chunks (sketch):**

- [ ] **34.1 Add `notify` dep + per-Backend watcher thread** (S) — spawn the thread in `Backend::initialized` (or lazily on first project load). Channel into the main loop. Plumb `WatcherEvent { uri, kind: Create | Modify | Remove }` through.
- [ ] **34.2 Root registration** (S) — `Backend::register_fs_root(path)` / `unregister_fs_root(path)`, called from `load_workspace`, `spawn_lazy_project`, `drop_project`, `did_change_workspace_folders`. Watch only what's loaded.
- [ ] **34.3 Event → handler dispatch** (M) — main loop's `select!` between `conn.receiver` and the watcher channel. Debounce. Translate notify events into the existing `did_change_watched_files`-shaped processing.
- [ ] **34.4 Editor-watcher coexistence** (S) — keep the existing `register_file_watchers` capability registration so editors that _do_ forward events still work; route both paths through a shared `apply_fs_event`. Avoid double-counting identical events.
- [ ] **34.5 Tests** (S) — drop a real file on disk between `did_open` and a subsequent `goto_definition`; assert the LSP picks up the change without needing an editor-side event. Test the failure-to-start fallback by injecting a watcher mock that always errors.

**M34:** stale-URI / stale-diagnostic bugs caused by missed editor events disappear from real-world reports. The LSP behaves identically whether it's driven by VSCode, Helix, Emacs lsp-mode, or a headless client that never registers a watcher.

**Out of scope:**

- Watching arbitrary subtrees the user might care about (e.g. an external schema dir). Limit watched roots to the loaded project closure and `<greycat_home>/lib/std`.
- A user-facing knob to disable the watcher. The fallback already covers the "won't start" case; a manual toggle would just complicate the configuration surface.

---

### Phase 35 — Decl-handle type identity (~1-2 weeks)

**Goal:** replace name-based type identity with decl-handle identity. Today the analyzer identifies a generic head by its `SmolStr` name (`TypeKind::Generic { name: "node", args }`), tests well-known status with hard-coded string matches ([`is_node_tag`](../greycat-analyzer-types/src/lib.rs)), and seeds runtime types via a parallel string allowlist ([`BUILTIN_RUNTIME_TYPES`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/stdlib.rs)). All of this is structurally wrong: `node`, `Array`, `Map`, `function`, `type`, `field`, the tuple shapes, etc. **are real `native type` decls in [`lib/std/core.gcl`](../lib/std/core.gcl)**. The analyzer just needs to resolve them once at load time, stash the resulting `TypeId` (or `Idx<Decl>`) under a named slot per well-known type, and reference those handles thereafter. After the refactor, identity is exact (handle equality), unforgeable (a user-declared `type node<T>` cannot impersonate the std-core `node`), and the `BUILTIN_RUNTIME_TYPES` / `arena.named("...")` stubs disappear.

**Trigger to do this phase:** revealed by the modvar+`node` completion bug (the receiver type is `Generic { name: "node", args }` but `member_completion` has nowhere to look up `node`'s members because `name: "node"` isn't bound to a decl). Same root cause behind: `is_node_tag` accepting user-defined `node` decls as auto-deref-eligible; 15+ `arena.named("function")` / `"type"` / `"field"` sentinels with no connection to actual decls; the `Named ↔ GenericParam` and `Named ↔ Enum` fallback rules in `is_assignable_to` papering over arena-boundary leaks.

**Behavioral contract:**

- Introduce `TypeDeclId` (newtype over `(Uri, Idx<Decl>)` or a project-wide interned ID) as the stable handle for resolved type decls. Every `Decl::Type` and `Decl::Enum` is assigned one when the project is built; cross-module references key off this rather than text.
- Add a `WellKnown` registry on the project context — a struct of `Option<TypeDeclId>` slots, one per std-core native type the analyzer cares about (`node`, `nodeTime`, `nodeIndex`, `nodeList`, `nodeGeo`, `Array`, `Map`, `Set`, `function`, `type`, `field`, `tuple`, `cubic`, `t2`–`t4f`, plus primitive aliases if any). Populated as part of [`ProjectAnalysis::stage_lower_signatures`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/project.rs) when a decl whose `(module.lib, module.name, decl_name)` matches `("std", "core", N)` is processed. All slots are `Option` so partial-project / missing-std states stay representable.
- Split `TypeKind::Named` and `TypeKind::Generic` into three precise variants whose invariants are enforced by the enum shape, not by runtime `args.is_empty()` checks:
  - `TypeKind::Type(TypeDeclId)` — a resolved non-generic type. `Point`, the non-generic native types in `std/core` (`time`, `duration`, `geo`, `cubic`, etc.).
  - `TypeKind::GenericInstance { decl: TypeDeclId, args: SmallVec<[TypeId; 2]> }` — an instantiation of a generic decl. `args` is guaranteed non-empty. `Array<int>`, `node<int?>`, `Map<String, V>`.
  - `TypeKind::Unresolved { name: SmolStr, byte_range: Span }` — type-refs whose name didn't resolve (typo, missing import, in-progress code). The _only_ surviving SmolStr-keyed type variant; explicitly means "resolution failure," diagnostic-shaped, not value-shaped.
- This is not a "Generic with empty args" model. A non-generic type is a structurally distinct concept from a generic instantiation; encoding both as one variant pushes the invariant into runtime checks scattered across consumers (substitution, variance, node-tag dispatch all only apply to `GenericInstance`). Match arms that don't care about the distinction can bind across variants via `Type(d) | GenericInstance { decl: d, .. }`; arms that DO care get correctness from the shape.
- Remove `TypeKind::Named` entirely. The three workaround branches in [`is_assignable_to`](../greycat-analyzer-types/src/lib.rs) (`Named ↔ GenericParam`, `Named ↔ Enum`, `Named ↔ Generic` raw-form) get deleted along with the leaks they paper over.
- Rewrite [`is_node_tag`](../greycat-analyzer-types/src/lib.rs) as a handle comparison: `decl == well_known.node_decl || decl == well_known.node_time_decl || …`. Callers at lib.rs:530, lib.rs:615, lib.rs:870 dispatch on handles, not strings. Only applicable on `GenericInstance` — node-tags are always generic — so the call sites also narrow the variant they're matching against.
- Replace every [`arena.named("function")`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/analyzer.rs) / `"type"` / `"field"` sentinel. These are runtime types declared in `std/core` (`function`, `type`, `field` — all non-generic), so they become `arena.alloc(Type { kind: TypeKind::Type(well_known.function_decl), .. })` etc. Each site already knew which runtime concept it was minting; the handle just makes that explicit and connects it to the actual decl in `std/core.gcl`. When `well_known.X_decl` is `None` (no std loaded), fall through to `any` plus the existing `missing-std` diagnostic from P33 — no string fallback.
- Delete [`BUILTIN_RUNTIME_TYPES`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/stdlib.rs) and the parallel seeding loop in [`ProjectIndex::new`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/stdlib.rs). The decls are real; the project pipeline walks them like any other. The matching `BUILTIN_RUNTIME_GLOBALS` (`Infinity`, `NaN` — value-position globals that genuinely have no decl) stays, with handle-keyed lookup if appropriate.
- The validation-pass's `Named{"V"}` leak (where a generic param `V` lowers without scope, [types/src/lib.rs:540-557](../greycat-analyzer-types/src/lib.rs)): fix the validation pass to thread the enclosing fn/type's generic scope through [`mint_type_shape`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/project.rs), producing `GenericParam` directly. The bridge rule is then dead and removed.
- The arena-boundary `Named ↔ Enum` leak ([types/src/lib.rs:683-692](../greycat-analyzer-types/src/lib.rs)): when foreign enum types cross arenas, carry the `TypeDeclId` (now decl-keyed) instead of re-minting as `Named{name}`. The bridge rule is dead and removed.
- Cross-module foreign refs ([project.rs:381](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/project.rs) note "resolves to `Named { name: "Foo" }`"): route through `Definition::ProjectDecl { uri, decl }` (already available from P11.2) to mint `Generic { decl: TypeDeclId::from(uri, decl), args }`. No more text-fallback.

**Architectural notes:**

- Provenance triple `(lib, module, name)` is already carried by [`Module`](../greycat-analyzer-hir/src/types.rs) — no HIR change needed to match it. The well-known recognizer is a single match in the lowering pass.
- `TypeArena::alloc` interns by `Type` value. Once `Type(decl)` / `GenericInstance { decl, args }` key on `TypeDeclId` instead of `SmolStr`, interning is exact: user-`node<int>` and std-core-`node<int>` cannot collapse because their decl handles differ. This is the soundness fix, not a side effect.
- Display / formatting code that prints type names (e.g. [`display_type`](../greycat-analyzer-types/src/lib.rs)) reads the decl's name through the project index: `proj.decl_name(decl_id)`. One indirection, called only when rendering — not on hot equality paths.
- Member resolution: a `Type(decl)` receiver walks `decl`'s `TypeDecl.members` directly (no substitution). A `GenericInstance { decl, args }` receiver walks the same members but substitutes `args` into each member's declared types via the existing substitution machinery. This is the exact mechanism used today for user types; it now also Just Works for `node`, `Array`, `Map`, etc., because they have real member decls in `std/core.gcl`. This is the fix the modvar+`node` completion bug needs.
- Migration is incremental: introduce `TypeDeclId` and `WellKnown` first, populate them, _then_ mass-rewrite `TypeKind::Generic` and `TypeKind::Named` callsites into `Type` / `GenericInstance` / `Unresolved`. The transition can land in a few large-ish but mechanical commits rather than one explosion.

**Chunks (sketch):**

- [x] **35.1 `TypeDeclId` + `WellKnown` registry** (S) — introduce the newtype and the slot struct in [`greycat-analyzer-types`](../greycat-analyzer-types/src/lib.rs). `WellKnown` lives on `ProjectAnalysis`. Populate slots in [`stage_lower_signatures`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/project.rs) by matching `(module.lib, module.name, decl_name)` against the canonical list. Unit test: load a synthetic `std/core.gcl` with the well-known native types, assert every slot is `Some(_)`; load _without_ std, assert every slot is `None`.
- [x] **35.2 Introduce `TypeKind::Type(TypeDeclId)` + `TypeKind::GenericInstance { decl, args }`** (L) — add the two new variants alongside the existing `Generic` / `Named`. New constructors: `arena.alloc_type(decl_id)`, `arena.alloc_generic_instance(decl_id, args)`. Update every constructor of the old `arena.generic(name, args)` to use `alloc_generic_instance` and resolve `name → decl_id` at the call site (~50 sites: analyzer, lint, project, capabilities, dump_types, wasm). `is_assignable_to` and related routines gain match arms for the new variants while still handling the old `Generic { name, .. }` and `Named { name }` ones — the old variants stay until 35.8. Tests pass.
- [x] **35.3 `TypeKind::Unresolved` + sunset `Named`** (M) — introduce `Unresolved`. All call sites that today mint `arena.named(name)` for an unresolved type-ref switch to `arena.unresolved(name, byte_range)`. Call sites that mint `arena.named(name)` for a _resolved_ non-generic type (user `Point`, runtime `function` / `type` / `field`) switch to `arena.alloc_type(decl_id)` from 35.2. Display, diagnostics, and `is_assignable_to`'s `Unresolved` arms emit the existing "unresolved type" diagnostic and otherwise behave like `any` (don't propagate cascading errors). `Named` still exists at the end of this chunk; subsequent chunks remove its remaining users.
- [x] **35.4 Replace `arena.named(N)` sentinels with handles** (M) — sweep the 15+ `arena.named("function")` / `"type"` / `"field"` sites in [`analyzer.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/analyzer.rs). Each becomes the corresponding `well_known.*_decl` handle (wrapped in `Generic { decl, args: [] }`). When the well-known slot is `None`, fall through to `any` (the `missing-std` diagnostic from P33 already explains why).
- [x] **35.5 Rewrite `is_node_tag` to a handle check** (S) — change the function signature to `pub fn is_node_tag(well_known: &WellKnown, decl: TypeDeclId) -> bool`. Update the three call sites at [lib.rs:530, lib.rs:615, lib.rs:870](../greycat-analyzer-types/src/lib.rs). Stop the silent-impersonation bug where a user `type node<T>` triggers node-tag auto-deref.
- [x] **35.6 Validation-pass generic-scope fix** (S) — thread the enclosing fn/type's generic-param scope through [`mint_type_shape`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/project.rs) so generic param refs lower as `GenericParam`, not `Unresolved` (and not `Named` — which is gone). Delete the `Named ↔ GenericParam` bridge rule at [types/src/lib.rs:552-557](../greycat-analyzer-types/src/lib.rs).
- [x] **35.7 Cross-module foreign-type handle propagation** (M) — route foreign-type lowering through `Definition::ProjectDecl { uri, decl }` to produce `Generic { decl: TypeDeclId, args }` instead of falling back to text. Delete the `Named ↔ Enum` and `Named ↔ Generic` raw-form bridge rules at [types/src/lib.rs:683-692, 631-641](../greycat-analyzer-types/src/lib.rs).
- [~] **35.8 Delete `TypeKind::Named` + `TypeKind::Generic` (old) + `BUILTIN_RUNTIME_TYPES`** — **deferred to Phase 36.** The original sizing ("S, once 35.4–35.7 land, zero remaining callers") was wrong. 35.7 migrated cross-module foreign types only; `register_module_types` still mints `arena.named(name)` for _local_ user types, and the cascade through member resolution, narrow tracking, subtype-chain assignability, lints, capabilities, and ~30+ `TypeKind::Named` / `Generic { name }` match arms is wider than a small chunk. Captured in full as [Phase 36](#phase-36--complete-decl-handle-identity-migration-23-weeks).
- [x] **35.9 Wire `member_completion` to walk runtime-type decls** (S) — the bug that triggered this phase. With `node`'s `TypeDecl` now reachable via the project index (it's just another `Decl::Type` in the std-core module) and the receiver typed as `GenericInstance { decl: well_known.node_decl, args: [int?] }`, [`member_completion`](../greycat-analyzer-server/src/capabilities.rs) walks `decl`'s members (substituting `args` into each member's declared types) the same way it does for user types. The two failing modvar+`node` tests added pre-phase should now pass without special-casing.
- [x] **35.10 Stage 3 of `receiver_type_at`: top-level vars** (S) — extend [`lookup_name_type_at`](../greycat-analyzer-server/src/capabilities.rs) to walk top-level `Decl::Var` by name, so the ERROR-recovery path (cursor inside `(ERROR (ident))` — the user's exact `project.gcl` shape) finds modvars. Independent of 35.1–35.9 but ships in the same phase since the trigger bug needs both halves. Add `def_types[modvar_name]` population in [`visit_top_var`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/analyzer.rs) at the same time.

**M35 (achieved):** the type-system identity model has been _extended_ with handle-keyed variants alongside the legacy SmolStr-keyed ones. `TypeKind::Type(decl)`, `TypeKind::GenericInstance { decl, args }`, and `TypeKind::Unresolved { name, byte_range }` exist in the enum and are minted by:

- The sentinel sites in the analyzer body walker (`function_ty` / `type_ty` / `field_ty`) when `WellKnown.*_decl` is populated (35.4).
- Cross-module foreign type-refs that resolve via `Definition::ProjectDecl` (35.7).
- The truly-unresolved-name fallback in `lower_type_ref` / `lower_type_ref_project` (35.3).

`is_node_tag` is deprecated in favour of handle-keyed `WellKnown::is_node_tag(decl)` (35.5). The `Named ↔ GenericParam` and `Named ↔ Enum` / `Named ↔ Generic` raw-form bridge rules in `is_assignable_to` are gone (35.6, 35.7). Member completion on `var n: node<int?>;` then `n.` surfaces `node`'s actual members (35.9, 35.10).

**M35 (NOT achieved, deferred to Phase 36):** `TypeKind::Named` and `TypeKind::Generic` (the SmolStr-keyed variants) are _still present and load-bearing_: every local user-type reference (`register_module_types`, `this_ty`, the body walker's `lower_type_ref`) still produces `Named { name }` / `Generic { name, args }`. `BUILTIN_RUNTIME_TYPES` still seeds `arena.named(...)` shapes into the `ProjectIndex` for std-less projects. The handle-keyed model is _additive_ today, not yet a replacement.

**Out of scope:**

- Reworking `TypeKind::Primitive` to also key off decl handles. Primitives are runtime-baked and don't have user-overridable decls; keeping them as a dedicated variant is correct.
- Changing how `lib/std/` is _located_ (P33 covers that). This phase consumes whatever's loaded.
- Optimizing `is_assignable_to`'s hot path with the new decl-keyed equality. Likely faster than today's SmolStr comparison but benchmark before claiming.
- Adding a generic-bound system (`T: Bound`). Out of scope by language design — GreyCat doesn't have bounds.

---

### Phase 36 — Complete decl-handle identity migration (~2-3 weeks)

**Goal:** finish what Phase 35 started — delete `TypeKind::Named` and `TypeKind::Generic` (the SmolStr-keyed variants) and `BUILTIN_RUNTIME_TYPES`, leaving exactly three resolved-type variants in `TypeKind`: `Type(TypeDeclId)`, `GenericInstance { decl, args }`, and `Unresolved { name, byte_range }`. Closes the soundness gap where user-`Foo` and stdlib-`Foo` can still collide in the type arena (the legacy `Named { name: "Foo" }` shape interns by string, so a user-defined `type node<T>` still collapses with std-core's `node<T>` in any code path that hasn't been migrated).

**Trigger:** deferred from Phase 35.8. The original chunk description estimated this as a small post-cleanup once 35.4–35.7 landed. In practice every `Named`-minting site (`register_module_types`, `this_ty`, the body walker's `lower_type_ref`, `mint_type_shape` — now gone post-refactor, and various ProjectIndex seedings) has a downstream cascade: ~30+ match arms that read `TypeKind::Named { name }` / `TypeKind::Generic { name, args }` and key behaviour off the SmolStr name (member resolution, narrow tracking, subtype-chain assignability, lints, capabilities, hover rendering). Deleting the variants requires migrating each of those sites either to read handles or to receive a name-resolver alongside the arena.

**Behavioral contract:**

- Every resolved-type reference in `expr_types` / `def_types` / `attr_types` / `method_returns` / `var_types` is one of `Type(decl)` / `GenericInstance { decl, args }`. No `Named` / `Generic` shapes remain. `Unresolved` is the _only_ SmolStr-keyed type variant and it explicitly means "name didn't resolve".
- Every consumer that today branches on `TypeKind::Named { name }` or `TypeKind::Generic { name, .. }` either (a) reads the decl name via `decl_registry.name(handle)` when it needs a string, or (b) dispatches on the handle directly when it can.
- The `arena.named(...)` and `arena.generic(name, args)` constructors are gone. `arena.alloc_type(handle)` and `arena.alloc_generic_instance(handle, args)` are the only handle-aware constructors; primitives, enums, lambdas, tuples, anonymous, unions, generic-params, and unresolved keep their existing constructors.
- The string-keyed `greycat_analyzer_types::is_node_tag(name)` function is deleted. `WellKnown::is_node_tag(decl)` is the only node-tag check.
- `BUILTIN_RUNTIME_TYPES` is deleted. Std-less projects produce `Unresolved` for names the resolver can't bind (the `missing-std` Phase 33 diagnostic already explains why); they do _not_ mint synthetic `Named` shapes.
- The `function_ty()` / `type_ty()` / `field_ty()` analyzer helpers (Phase 35.4) drop their legacy `arena.named(...)` fallback. Either `well_known.X_decl` is populated (std loaded → `Type(handle)`) or the helper returns `any` (std missing → matches the existing P33 fallback semantics).
- Cross-arena enum identity (the `Named ↔ Enum` bridge) is replaced by `Enum` itself carrying a `TypeDeclId` and matching on that; no string fallback. Variant data (`variants: Vec<SmolStr>`) stays on the enum kind — it's part of the value, not the identity.

**Cascade map (sites that need migration):**

The chunks below group these by file. Each match arm typically needs _either_ a new arm for the handle variants OR migration of the source minter to produce handles instead — fewer total touch sites than treating them all as "add an arm" would suggest.

| Subsystem               | Files                                                                                                                  | Hot paths                                                                                                                                                                                                                      |
| ----------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| Body walker (in-module) | [`analyzer.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/analyzer.rs)                                                          | `register_module_types`, `this_ty`, `lower_type_ref` (local-type branch), `method_return_for`, `resolve_member`, `foreign_member_type`, member-narrow path keys, callee-shape extraction                                       |
| Assignability + display | [`types/src/lib.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-types/src/lib.rs)                                                             | `is_assignable_to` (Named/Generic arms, node-tag auto-deref, raw-form widening), `is_castable` (node-tag heads, tuple primitives), `display` / `display_fqn` (string fallbacks), `generic_or_named_name`                       |
| Project pipeline        | [`project.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/project.rs)                                                            | `lower_type_ref_project`, `is_assignable_to_with_index` (subtype-chain via `index.is_subtype_of` — needs handle-keyed variant), `lower_module_signatures` for attr/method/var types                                            |
| ProjectIndex seeding    | [`stdlib.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/stdlib.rs)                                                              | `BUILTIN_RUNTIME_TYPES` registry seed, `BUILTIN_RUNTIME_GLOBALS` (stays — those have no decl), the `ProjectIndex::new` initialization                                                                                          |
| Lints                   | [`lint.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/lint.rs)                                                                  | `receiver_head_name` (partially done in 35.7), `lint_arrow_on_non_deref` (partially done), all rules that match `TypeKind::Named` / `Generic` on receivers / inits / return types                                              |
| Capabilities            | [`capabilities.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-server/src/capabilities.rs)                                                    | `type_head_name` (partially done in 35.7), hover, completion (member / static / object-field / type-position), goto-def, signature-help, inlay-hints — every site that formats a type for display or branches on its head name |
| HIR introspection       | [`wasm/src/lib.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-wasm/src/lib.rs), [`dump_types.rs`](../greycat-analyzer/src/cmd/dump_types.rs) | `dump-types` CLI, the wasm bridge's type rendering                                                                                                                                                                             |

**Chunks:**

- [x] **36.1 Handle-keyed subtype-chain in `ProjectIndex`** (S) — `ProjectIndex::is_subtype_of` is name-keyed today (`(&str, &str) -> bool`). Add a handle-keyed variant `is_subtype_of_decl(TypeDeclId, TypeDeclId) -> bool` that resolves both handles to their names via `DeclRegistry` and delegates to the existing name-keyed implementation. Both forms coexist during the migration. The handle-keyed form becomes the only one in 36.7 once `Named` is gone.
- [x] **36.2 Migrate `register_module_types` to mint `Type(handle)`** (M) — the keystone migration. `register_module_types` runs before the body walker and seeds `out.registry: TypeRegistry` (name → TypeId map) + `out.type_decls: name → Idx<Decl>` map. Switch the mint to `arena.alloc_type(decl_registry.lookup(uri, decl)?)`, fall back to `arena.named` only when std isn't loaded (transitional, removed in 36.7). This single change cascades into every consumer of `out.registry.lookup(name)` — receivers that today read `TypeKind::Named { name: "Box" }` start reading `TypeKind::Type(box_handle)` instead. **Bundled with 36.5** since `lower_type_ref_project` and `is_assignable_to_with_index` had to migrate in lockstep to keep call-arg validation consistent.
- [x] **36.3 Body-walker consumers: member resolution + narrow tracking** (L) — every `TypeKind::Named { name } | TypeKind::Generic { name, .. } => name` extraction in [`analyzer.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/analyzer.rs) gains parallel `Type(d) | GenericInstance { decl: d, .. } => decl_registry.name(d)?` arms. P35.7 covered the receiver / member-resolution shapes (`resolve_member`, `try_member_call_typing`, `foreign_member_type`); this chunk added the `arrow_deref_receiver` handle-keyed dispatch (`WellKnown::is_node_tag`) and the cast-validity `inheritance_ok` extractor. Member-path narrow tracking uses ident text as the path key (`"this.foo.bar"`), not type names — already independent of the handle migration, no key normalization needed. Specialty dispatchers that key on specific generic names (`Array`, `Map`, `node`, …) in for-in / index-access / witness-collection paths still produce `TypeKind::Generic` and migrate when `arena.generic` switches to `GenericInstance` for std-core types in a future chunk.
- [ ] **36.4 Assignability + display in [`types/src/lib.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-types/src/lib.rs)** (M) — the `Named ↔ Named` and `Generic ↔ Generic` arms in `is_assignable_to` (line ~640+) are deleted; the `Type ↔ Type` and `GenericInstance ↔ GenericInstance` arms (already added in 35.2) become the only paths. Same for `is_castable`'s node-tag-head dispatch and tuple-primitive special-case — both use `is_node_tag(name)` today; replace with a closure passed in OR thread `&WellKnown` through. `generic_or_named_name` (used by display) drops its Named/Generic arms.
- [x] **36.5 Project pipeline: `lower_type_ref_project` + `lower_module_signatures` + `is_assignable_to_with_index`** (M) — bundled into 36.2. `lower_type_ref_project` now resolves non-generic local-type names to their decl handle via the registry (with `Named` as a transitional fallback). `lower_module_signatures` runs after a pre-pass that populates `decl_registry` so signatures land in the same handle-keyed shape as the per-module analyzer's mints. `is_assignable_to_with_index` gained a `(Type, Type)` subtype-chain arm via 36.1's `is_subtype_of_decl`. Generic instances (`arena.generic`) remain Named-keyed pending a separate pass.
- [x] **36.6 Capability + lint sweep** (M) — `lint.rs`'s `receiver_head_name` and `capabilities.rs`'s `type_head_name` already had parallel `Type` / `GenericInstance` arms from P35.7. This chunk adds `member_completion`'s handle-keyed node-tag dispatch (`WellKnown::is_node_tag(decl)`), exposes `ProjectAnalysis::well_known()` for capability handlers to consume, and verifies every public-API display call routes through `display_with_names` with a registry-backed resolver. Remaining `TypeKind::Generic { name, .. }` matches in capability code dispatch on specific std-core names (`node`, `Array`) and migrate when `arena.generic` switches to `GenericInstance` for std-core types.
- [ ] **36.7 Delete the variants + `BUILTIN_RUNTIME_TYPES` + legacy constructors** (S) — once 36.1–36.6 land and no production caller mints `Named` / `Generic`, the variants can go. Delete `TypeKind::Named`, `TypeKind::Generic`, `arena.named`, the old `arena.generic`, `greycat_analyzer_types::is_node_tag(&str)`, `BUILTIN_RUNTIME_TYPES` (and its seeding loop in `ProjectIndex::new`), the legacy `function_ty()` / `type_ty()` / `field_ty()` `arena.named(...)` fallbacks. Update the `stdlib.rs` doc-comment about stubs. The `is_subtype_of` name-keyed form on `ProjectIndex` goes too (only the handle-keyed `is_subtype_of_decl` from 36.1 survives).
- [ ] **36.8 Migrate `TypeKind::Enum` to carry `TypeDeclId`** (S) — the last name-keyed identity variant. Enums today carry `name: SmolStr, variants: Vec<SmolStr>`; after this, `decl: TypeDeclId, variants: Vec<SmolStr>` (variants stay because they're part of the value, not identity). Cross-arena enum identity now lives on the handle. `enum_type_for(name)` in `ProjectIndex` keeps working — same name → TypeId pipeline, just minting `Enum { decl, variants }` instead of `Enum { name, variants }`.

**M36:** the type-kind enum's resolved-name variants are _exactly_ `Type(decl)`, `GenericInstance { decl, args }`, `Enum { decl, variants }`, and `Unresolved { name, byte_range }`. No SmolStr-name keys anywhere in the identity-bearing variants. Two `TypeId`s being equal _means_ they refer to the same decl in the same module; a user-defined `type node<T>` cannot be confused with std-core's `node<T>` at any level of the analysis pipeline. `BUILTIN_RUNTIME_TYPES` is gone, the stdlib.rs stub-laments docstring is deleted, and `is_node_tag(&str)` is gone (handle-keyed only).

**Out of scope:**

- Migrating `TypeKind::Primitive` to also key off a decl handle. Primitives don't have user-overridable decls.
- Re-keying narrow-tracking paths on `(TypeDeclId, SmolStr)` tuples instead of the current "display string" form. 36.3 normalizes paths via the registry-backed name to keep the migration mechanical; the structural rework belongs to a future phase if profiling shows it matters.
- Removing `Unresolved`. It's a deliberate kept variant — the only diagnostic-shaped type kind.

---

### Phase 37 — `breakpoint` keyword end-to-end (~2-3 days)

**Goal:** add first-class support for the GreyCat `breakpoint` statement — a no-op-shaped control statement that signals the runtime to pause the current worker for debugging. The keyword exists in the runtime (`8.0.291-dev` build accepts `fn main() { breakpoint; }`; `greycat run main` pauses on entry) but was missing from the grammar and every downstream stage of the Rust port. Today an `.gcl` containing `breakpoint;` parses as `ERROR` in tree-sitter, which cascades into `Expr::Unsupported` / parse diagnostics, breaking lint, format, and LSP on any file using the construct.

**Trigger:** user-reported gap on 2026-05-12. The keyword was never ported because no stdlib / corpus file uses it; the analyzer didn't surface it until someone wrote `breakpoint;` in their own project.

**Semantics (confirmed against the runtime, oracle for this phase):**

- `breakpoint` is a **statement-level keyword**, parsed as `seq("breakpoint", $._semi)` — same shape family as `break_stmt` / `continue_stmt`.
- It is **not loop-scoped** — `fn main() { breakpoint; }` is valid GreyCat (unlike `break` / `continue`). Allowed anywhere a statement is.
- It is **not a control-flow terminator** — execution resumes from the next statement after the debugger detaches. Code after `breakpoint;` is reachable; the reachability / unreachable-code lint must NOT flag it.
- The runtime ident probe (`breakpoints;` → "unresolved identifier breakpoints") confirms exact spelling: singular, no trailing `s`. `breakpoint` matches the ident regex like every other keyword (`word: $.ident`), so the grammar literal token preempts the ident match.

**Behavioral contract:**

- `breakpoint;` parses to a `breakpoint_stmt` CST node, lowers to `Stmt::Breakpoint`, and round-trips through `cargo run -p greycat-analyzer -- fmt` byte-identical (modulo surrounding-statement formatting).
- `cargo run -p greycat-analyzer -- lint project.gcl` on a file using `breakpoint;` produces exactly one `no-breakpoint` Warning (the advisory lint from 37.7); `lint --fix` deletes the statement.
- LSP keyword completion at a statement position offers `breakpoint`.
- The reachability pass treats `breakpoint;` as a non-terminating statement: a `return` after it is _not_ dead code; a function whose only statement is `breakpoint;` still fails missing-return analysis if a value-returning signature demands one.
- The `unsupported_audit` HIR test stays clean (no new `Expr::Unsupported` shapes; `breakpoint_stmt` is a stmt-level node so it never goes through expression lowering anyway).

**Surface map (touchpoints, in dependency order):**

| Layer                      | Files                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | What changes                                                                                                                                                                                                             |
| -------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| Grammar                    | [`tree-sitter-greycat/grammar.js`](../tree-sitter-greycat/grammar.js), [`queries/highlights.scm`](../tree-sitter-greycat/queries/highlights.scm), `src/parser.c` + `src/node-types.json` (regenerated), [`test/corpus/`](../tree-sitter-greycat/test/corpus/)                                                           | New `breakpoint_stmt` rule; added to `_stmt` choice; highlight as `@keyword.control`; corpus test pinning shape.                                                                                                         |
| HIR                        | [`greycat-analyzer-hir/src/types.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-hir/src/types.rs), [`src/lower.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-hir/src/lower.rs)                                                                                                                                                                                     | `Stmt::Breakpoint` unit variant (mirror `Break` / `Continue`); `"breakpoint_stmt"` arm in `lower_stmt`.                                                                                                                  |
| Analysis                   | [`analyzer.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/analyzer.rs), [`reachability.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/reachability.rs), [`resolver.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/resolver.rs), [`lint.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/lint.rs), [`project.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/project.rs) | Add `Stmt::Breakpoint` arm to every `match stmt` site. **Critical:** in `reachability.rs:40` and `analyzer.rs:54`, `breakpoint` is NOT in the "terminates" set (unlike `Break` / `Continue` / `Return` / `Throw`).       |
| Formatter                  | [`greycat-analyzer-fmt/src/lower.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-fmt/src/lower.rs)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             | `"breakpoint_stmt" => Doc::text("breakpoint;")` — matches the `break_stmt` / `continue_stmt` shape.                                                                                                                      |
| CLI dump                   | [`greycat-analyzer/src/cmd/dump_types.rs`](../greycat-analyzer/src/cmd/dump_types.rs)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | Add to the no-op exhaustive arm alongside `Break` / `Continue` / `Throw(_)`.                                                                                                                                             |
| WASM bridge                | [`greycat-analyzer-wasm/src/lib.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-wasm/src/lib.rs)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | `Stmt::Breakpoint => HirNode { kind: "stmt:breakpoint", … }` — mirror the `Break` / `Continue` shapes.                                                                                                                   |
| LSP                        | [`capabilities.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-server/src/capabilities.rs)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | `ALL_KEYWORDS` registry: add `"breakpoint"`. `stmt_byte_range` helper: add `HS::Breakpoint => 0..0` arm (matches `Break` / `Continue`). Hover text optional but worth adding: "Pauses the GreyCat worker for debugging." |
| VSCode TM grammar          | [`editors/code/grammar/Greycat.tmLanguage.json`](../editors/code/grammar/Greycat.tmLanguage.json)                                                                                                                                                                                                                       | Add `breakpoint` to both keyword.control alternations (lines 34 and 38 today).                                                                                                                                           |
| VSCode snippets (optional) | [`editors/code/snippets/snippets.json`](../editors/code/snippets/snippets.json)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | `bp` → `breakpoint;` snippet for ergonomic insertion.                                                                                                                                                                    |

**Chunks:**

- [x] **37.1 Grammar + corpus test + queries (submodule)** (S) — edit `tree-sitter-greycat/grammar.js`: add `breakpoint_stmt: ($) => seq("breakpoint", $._semi)` and append it to the `_stmt` choice (next to `break_stmt`). Run `npx tree-sitter generate` to refresh `src/parser.c`, `src/grammar.json`, `src/node-types.json`. Add a corpus test in `tree-sitter-greycat/test/corpus/breakpoint_stmt.txt` exercising both standalone (`fn main() { breakpoint; }`) and trailing-after-breakpoint shapes (`fn f() { breakpoint; return 0; }`) to lock the not-a-terminator parse and prove the next statement still attaches as a sibling, not as an ERROR child. Update `queries/highlights.scm`: add `breakpoint` to the keyword alternation (line 6 today) and add `(breakpoint_stmt "breakpoint" @keyword.control)`. Run `npx tree-sitter test` + `npx tree-sitter parse project.gcl` (the submodule's smoke file — add a `breakpoint;` line first) to verify no `ERROR` nodes. Commit inside submodule, push to `maxleiko/tree-sitter-greycat`. **Submodule pointer bump lands in 37.2.**
- [x] **37.2 Bump submodule pointer + HIR variant + lowering** (S) — bump `tree-sitter-greycat` SHA in the parent repo to the 37.1 commit. Add `Stmt::Breakpoint` to [`types.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-hir/src/types.rs) (unit variant alongside `Break` / `Continue` — no byte_range, mirroring those two; if the user later wants hover positioning beyond the CST fallback, plumbing a `byte_range` field is a separate, mechanical pass). Add `"breakpoint_stmt" => Stmt::Breakpoint` to `lower_stmt` in [`lower.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-hir/src/lower.rs). Smoke test in `greycat-analyzer-hir/tests/`: parse `fn f() { breakpoint; }`, lower, assert the function body's first stmt is `Stmt::Breakpoint`. **Bundled with 37.3 / 37.4 / 37.5 / 37.6** — the HIR variant cascades exhaustive matches into every downstream crate, so the analysis arms (37.3), fmt / dump / wasm arms (37.4), and LSP wiring (37.5) all had to land together for build-green. VSCode TM (37.6) followed in the same commit to keep the keyword end-to-end.
- [x] **37.3 Analysis stages: non-exhaustive match audit + reachability semantics** (M) — add `Stmt::Breakpoint` to every `match stmt` site in `greycat-analyzer-analysis`. Six sites today: `resolver.rs:449`, `analyzer.rs:54`, `analyzer.rs:2742`, `reachability.rs:40`, `lint.rs:1914`, `project.rs:2489`. The **load-bearing decision** is in `reachability.rs:40` and `analyzer.rs:54` — both currently group `Break | Continue | Return | Throw` as "terminates control flow." `Breakpoint` does NOT belong in that group; it goes in the no-op arm next to `Expr` / `Var` / `Assign`. Add a `tests/reachability_breakpoint.rs` integration test asserting `fn f(): int { breakpoint; return 0; }` produces no `unreachable` diagnostic on the return. **Bundled with 37.2.**
- [x] **37.4 Formatter + CLI dump + WASM bridge** (S) — three mechanical mirrors of the `Break` / `Continue` pattern. (a) [`greycat-analyzer-fmt/src/lower.rs:144`](../greycat-analyzer-fmt/src/lower.rs): add `"breakpoint_stmt" => Doc::text("breakpoint;")`. (b) [`greycat-analyzer/src/cmd/dump_types.rs:818`](../greycat-analyzer/src/cmd/dump_types.rs): add `Stmt::Breakpoint` to the no-op exhaustive arm. (c) [`greycat-analyzer-wasm/src/lib.rs:532`](../greycat-analyzer-wasm/src/lib.rs): add `Stmt::Breakpoint => HirNode { kind: "stmt:breakpoint".into(), label: None, range: (0..0).into(), children: Vec::new() }`. Add a formatter snapshot test pinning the round-trip. **Bundled with 37.2.**
- [x] **37.5 LSP keyword completion + `stmt_byte_range` arm** (S) — [`capabilities.rs:3616`](../greycat-analyzer-server/src/capabilities.rs): add `"breakpoint"` to `ALL_KEYWORDS` (alphabetic position between `at` and `catch`). `break` and `continue` were added to the same list in a prior `chore:` commit, so the only insert in this chunk is `breakpoint`. [`capabilities.rs:4200`](../greycat-analyzer-server/src/capabilities.rs): extend the `0..0` fallback to include `HS::Breakpoint`. Optional: when hover lands on a `breakpoint` keyword (cursor inside the CST keyword token), return a fixed markdown string explaining the semantics ("Pauses the GreyCat worker for debugging. Resumes from the next statement after the debugger detaches."). Integration test in `greycat-analyzer-server/tests/`: assert `textDocument/completion` at a fresh stmt position includes `breakpoint`. **Bundled with 37.2.**
- [x] **37.6 VSCode TextMate grammar + snippet** (S) — [`editors/code/grammar/Greycat.tmLanguage.json`](../editors/code/grammar/Greycat.tmLanguage.json) line 34: insert `breakpoint` into the main keyword alternation. Line 38: insert into the `return|break|continue` group (the "control-flow exit-shape" group). Optional: snippet `bp` → `breakpoint;` in [`snippets.json`](../editors/code/snippets/snippets.json). Smoke-test by opening a `.gcl` file with `breakpoint;` in the bundled VSCode extension dev host. **Bundled with 37.2.**
- [x] **37.7 Advisory lint: `no-breakpoint`** (S) — lint that flags every `Stmt::Breakpoint` in committed source, default severity Warning, LSP DiagnosticTag `UNNECESSARY` for the dimmed-text rendering. Rationale: `breakpoint` is a debug aid that pauses the worker; leaving one in committed code stalls production runs and is almost always unintended — the same shape of mistake as committing a Rust `dbg!()` or a JS `debugger;`. **Default-off** (`LintRuleInfo::default_enabled = false`) — a vanilla `lint --fix` would otherwise silently delete debug aids the user has every right to leave temporarily; users opt in via `lint --enable=no-breakpoint`. (A future `@lint_enable("no-breakpoint")` project pragma will land as a separate chunk so projects can opt in declaratively without per-invocation flags.) Suppression via `// gcl-lint-off no-breakpoint` for the rare intentional case (e.g. `breakpoint;` inside an `@test` that is meant to attach a debugger). Touchpoints (per the [CLAUDE.md "Adding / removing a lint rule"](../../greycat-analyzer/.claude/CLAUDE.md#adding--removing-a-lint-rule) checklist, all four touched in the same commit, plus the registry-level `default_enabled` + `enabled_rules` plumbing): (1) `LINT_RULES` registry entry with `default_enabled: false` via the new `advisory_rule(…)` helper; (2) emission wiring — CST-walking `lint_no_breakpoint(root, directives, bypass, out)` in [`lint.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/lint.rs), called from `run_typed_lints_for_module` in [`project.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/project.rs) under an `enabled_rules.contains("no-breakpoint")` gate, with the rule name added to the typed-pass `retain` filter; (3) auto-fix dispatch in [`quickfix.rs`](../greycat-analyzer-analysis/src/quickfix.rs) — `no_breakpoint_fix(text, start, end)` deletes the `breakpoint_stmt` byte range plus the trailing newline when the line is otherwise blank (mirrors `unreachable_fix`'s trailing-line cleanup), wired through both `lint --fix` and the LSP `textDocument/codeAction` path; (4) `default_tag_for` returning `Some(DiagnosticTag::UNNECESSARY)` for editor-side dimming. CLI plumbing: `--enable=<rule>` flag mirroring `--disable`, validated against the same `valid_rules` set, populates `ProjectAnalysis::enabled_rules`. `--list-rules` annotates default-off rules with a leading `*` and prints a footer legend. Fixture tests in `greycat-analyzer-analysis/tests/no_breakpoint.rs`: (a) default-off invocation produces no diagnostic on `fn f() { breakpoint; }`, (b) `enabled_rules.insert("no-breakpoint")` surfaces the Warning with `UNNECESSARY` tag, (c) `--fix` deletes the statement + trailing newline, (d) `// gcl-lint-off no-breakpoint` suppresses.

**M37:** `cargo run -p greycat-analyzer -- lint project.gcl` on a file containing `breakpoint;` produces exactly one `no-breakpoint` Warning (dimmed in editors); `lint --fix` deletes the statement; `... fmt project.gcl` round-trips byte-identical; LSP completion offers `breakpoint` at stmt position; reachability doesn't flag `return` after `breakpoint;` as dead. `cargo test --workspace` + `cargo clippy --workspace --all-targets` clean. Tree-sitter corpus regression test pins the parse shape.

**Out of scope:**

- Wiring the analyzer to anything debugger-protocol-shaped (DAP). The analyzer's job ends at "this statement parses, lowers, types-checks, and round-trips." Whether the runtime actually pauses on it is the runtime's contract.
- Plumbing a `byte_range` onto `Stmt::Breakpoint` (or onto `Stmt::Break` / `Continue`). Capability handlers fall back to the CST when they need precise positioning; HIR keeps the unit-variant shape consistent.
- Updating the external `/greycat:greycat` skill or the upstream TS reference docs. The runtime already accepts the keyword; nothing in this phase asks us to publish a language-reference change. Flag the gap to the user if it matters.
- Adding `break` / `continue` to `ALL_KEYWORDS` (separate completion-keyword gap, not what was reported).
